Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Conditions for the Validity of Takbirat al-Ihram (8th–15th)
Lists and explains the final eight conditions for the opening takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight conditions for the validity of the opening takbir and identify which violations invalidate or merely impair the prayer.

Core Idea
The takbir must be a pure Arabic declaration of Allah's greatness; linguistic errors can invalidate the prayer.

The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is the first essential act of prayer. Its validity depends on precise pronunciation and intention. In this passage, al-Tahtawi explains the final eight conditions, resolving an intra-Hanafi dispute on language and clarifying common pitfalls that beginners and even seasoned worshippers may encounter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling context
Recognize that this passage deals with the conditions (shurut) for the validity (sihhah) of the takbirat al-ihram, not with its obligation or pillars.
The takbir itself is a rukn, but these conditions must be fulfilled for it to be valid.
2
Work through condition 8: Arabic language
Note the requirement that the takbir be in Arabic for those able, and the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa permits Persian even for the capable, while the Sahibayn require Arabic. The relied-upon view is the Sahibayn's.
This is a key ikhtilaf within the school; know both positions but follow the mufta bihi.
3
Examine conditions 9–15
Go through each condition: no prolonging hamza/ba', complete sentence (though leniency exists), pure dhikr, no basmalah, no dropping the ha' of Allah, including the 'haawi' (alif in second lam), and no coupling with nullifying speech.
Some conditions are strict (e.g., condition 15 makes the takbir invalid), others are linguistic errors that do not invalidate (e.g., prolonging the ha').
4
Distinguish between invalidating and non-invalidating violations
The text clarifies that some violations (e.g., dropping the ha', adding human speech) invalidate the takbir, while others (e.g., lengthening the ha' vowel) are merely linguistic mistakes that do not break the prayer.
This distinction is crucial for correct practice and fatwa.
5
Synthesize the practical application
Combine all conditions into a mental checklist: the takbir must be in Arabic (for the capable), pronounced correctly without substitution or addition, and purely for Allah's glorification.
Use the checklist when teaching others or checking one's own prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : لتتميم عدد شروط صحة التحريمة الثامن كونها بلفظ العربية للقادر عليها في الصحيح (أما العاجز عنها فلا خلاف في صحة شروعه بما قدر عليه اللغات . قوله : (في الصحيح هو قولهما أولاً، وقال الإمام يصح شروعه بغير العربية ولو مع القدرة عليها، ووقع للعيني مثل ما وقع للشرح ونقل في الدر عن التتارخانية أن الشروع بالفارسية كالتلبية يجوز مطلقاً إتفاقاً . قال : وظاهر رجوعهما إليه لا . هو إليهما في الشروع كرجوعه إليهما في القراءة حيث لا تجوز بغير العربية إلا للعاجز أفاده السيد) التاسع أن لا يمد همزاً فيها ولا باء أكبر، وإشباع حركة الهاء من الجلالة خطأ لغة ولا تفسد به الصلاة وكذا تسكينها العاشر أن يأتي بجملة تامة من مبتدأ وخبر (هو ظاهر الرواية عن الإمام نقله في البحر يدوبه قال أبو يوسف ومحمد قاله المؤلف في الشرح أن تكون البداءة بلفظ الله حتى لو قال : أكبر الله لا تصح عنده بزازية والأولى حذف قوله من مبتدأ وخبر لأنهما لا يشترطان وذلك لصحة الشروع بلا إله إلا الله وبسبحان مع الكراهة) الحادي عشر أن يكون بذكر خالص الله تعالى (فلو شرع بنحو اللهم اغفر لي لا يصح لأنه ليس بثناء خالص بل مشوب بحاجته) الثاني عشر أن لا يكون بالبسملة كما سيأتي (من أنها للتبرك فكأنه قال: بارك الله لي وهو الأصح كما في السراج والأشبه كما في شرح المنية) الثالث عشر أن لا يحذف الهاء من الجلالة (قال في الشرح المذكور : وعن حذفه لم يصح) الرابع عشر أن يأتي بالهاوى، وهو الألف في اللام الثانية (ترك ها و والمراد بالهاوي الألف الناشيء بالمد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة، فإذا حذفه الحالف، أو الذابح، أو المكبر للصلاة، أو حذف الهاء من الجلالة إختلف في إنعقاد يمينه وحل ذبيحته، وصحة تحريمته، فلا يترك ذلك إحتياطاً) الخامس عشر أن لا يقرن التكبير بما يفسده فلا يفسد مشروعه لو قال الله أكبر العالم بالمعدوم والموجود، أو العالم بأحوال الخلق لأنه يشبه كلام الناس ذكر هذا الأخير في البزازية وهذا مما من الله سبحانه بالايقاظ لجمعه، ولم أره قبله مجموعاً فله الحمد إذ إنعامه وفضله ليس محصوراً ولا محظوراً ولا ممنوعاً (قوله : (ذكر هذا الأخير) إسم الإشارة راجع إلى الشرط الأخير قوله : (إذ إنعامه) علة لقوله من بالايقاظ لجمعه، ولم أره الخ، وكأنه في جواب سؤال حاصله كيف جمعت هذه الشروط، ولم تسبق بها قوله: (ولا ممنوعاً) تكرار مع ما قبله)
Alert: To complete the number of conditions for the validity of the takbirat al-ihram: eighth: it must be in the Arabic phrase for one who is able, according to the correct opinion (as for the incapable, there is no dispute about the validity of his starting with whatever language he can...). Ninth: that he should not prolong the hamza in 'Allahu' nor the ba' in 'Akbar', and prolonging the vowel of the ha' of the Majesty is a linguistic error but does not invalidate the prayer, similarly making it silent. Tenth: that he should come with a complete sentence of subject and predicate (this is the apparent narration from the Imam...). Eleventh: that it should be purely a remembrance of Allah Almighty. Twelfth: that it should not be the basmalah as will come. Thirteenth: that he should not drop the ha' from the word of Majesty. Fourteenth: that he should bring the 'haawi' which is the alif in the second lam... Fifteenth: that he should not couple the takbir with something that nullifies it.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is an expansion by al-Tahtawi on the conditions for the validity of the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) in prayer. The author lists the eighth through fifteenth conditions, each accompanied by commentary. The eighth condition requires the takbir to be in Arabic for those capable; a famous intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Imam Abu Hanifa allowed starting prayer in Persian even if able, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restricted it to Arabic except for the incapable. The ninth condition prohibits prolonging the hamza or ba', and clarifies that lengthening the ha' of 'Allah' or making it silent are linguistic mistakes but do not invalidate prayer. The tenth condition demands a complete sentence (subject + predicate); however, the commentator notes that this is not strictly necessary because starting with 'la ilaha illa Allah' or 'subhan' is valid, albeit disliked. The eleventh condition requires the takbir to be pure praise of Allah, not mixed with personal needs like 'Allahumma ighfir li'. The twelfth prohibits the basmalah as it is for blessing. The thirteenth prohibits dropping the ha' of 'Allah'. The fourteenth requires producing the 'haawi' (the long alif in the second lam of 'Allah'); dropping it affects oaths, slaughter, and takbir, so caution is needed. The fifteenth forbids coupling the takbir with something that invalidates it, e.g., 'Allahu Akbar, the Knower of the existing and non-existing', which resembles human speech. Al-Tahawi praises Allah for guiding him to collect these conditions, as he had not seen them gathered before.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes something forbidden (haram) — i.e., it initiates the state of prayer (ihram) where worldly actions become forbidden.
باء أكبر (ba' akbar): The letter 'ba' in the word 'Akbar'.
هاوى (hawi): The long alif (alif al-madd) that appears in the second lam of the word 'Allah' when pronounced with a prolonged vowel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on starting prayer with Persian (Farsi) if one is capable of Arabic?
A) Valid, because intention matters more than language.
B) Invalid, because Arabic is required for the capable.
C) Valid but disliked (makruh).
D) Invalid only if one deliberately avoids Arabic.

Key Takeaway
The validity of the opening takbir depends on eight precise conditions; violation of any except minor linguistic errors invalidates the prayer's start.

Specifying Intention (Ta'yin) in Supererogatory Prayers
Intra-Hanafi ruling on specifying intention for supererogatory prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'yin in supererogatory prayers and explain the intra-madhhab difference regarding Tarawih.

Core Idea
Specification of intention is not required for sunan; precautionary specification avoids disagreement.

This lesson examines whether a worshipper must explicitly name the specific supererogatory prayer (e.g., Fajr sunnah, Tarawih) in the intention. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the dominant Hanafi view and notes a precautionary position and a stricter view for Tarawih.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
According to the text, specification (ta'yin) is not required in supererogatory prayers, even for the sunnah of Fajr.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason is that the occurrence of these prayers in their specific times (e.g., after Fajr adhan) suffices to identify them, so a general intention of 'sunnah of the time' is enough.
3
Identify the majority view on Tarawih
According to most scholars ('عامة المشايخ'), specification is not required for Tarawih either.
4
Note the minority view
Some later scholars, including the author of al-Mughni and the one who corrected in al-Khaniyyah, require specification for Tarawih.
5
Apply the precautionary approach
The text recommends precaution (ihtiyat) by specifying, to avoid disagreement with those who require it.
This is the operative recommended practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يشترط التعيين في النقل) ولو سنة الفجر في الأصح وكذا التراويح عند عامة المشايخ وهو الصحيح والاحتياط التعيين فينوي مراعياً صفتها (مراده به ما يعم السنن لأن وقوعها في أوقاتها يغني عن التعيين وبه صارت سنة لا بالتعيين ولا فرق بين أ أن ينوي الصلاة، أو الصلاة الله تعالى لأن المصلي لا يصلي لغير الله تعالى قوله : (والإحتياط التعيين) قاله صاحب المنية، وذلك للخروج من خلاف من إشترط في فعل السنة نيتها . قال صاحب المغني : في التراويح لا يكفيه مطلق النية، ولا نية التطوع عند بعض المتأخرين، بل يشترط نية التراويح، وصححه في الخانية)
His statement: (And specification is not required in supererogatory prayers) even for the sunnah of Fajr according to the most correct view, and likewise for Tarawih according to most scholars, and that is correct. Precaution is specification, so one should intend observing its characteristic. (He means by it what includes the sunan because their occurrence in their times dispenses with specification, and by that they become sunnah, not by specification. There is no difference between one intending 'the prayer' or 'the prayer for Allah Almighty' because the worshipper does not pray for other than Allah. His statement: (Precaution is specification) said by the author of al-Munya, and that is to exit from the disagreement of those who require intention for the performance of the sunnah. The author of al-Mughni said: Regarding Tarawih, absolute intention is not sufficient, nor intention of supererogatory prayer according to some later scholars; rather, intention of Tarawih is required, and it was corrected in al-Khaniyyah.)
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on specifying intention (ta'yin) for supererogatory prayers (nawafil) including sunan. The author states that specification is not required, even for the sunnah of Fajr according to the most correct view, and for Tarawih according to the general body of scholars. The reason given is that these prayers are identified by their prescribed times, so a general intention to pray the sunnah of the time suffices. There is no need to specify 'Fajr sunnah' etc. The precaution (ihtiyat) is to specify, to avoid disagreement with those who require it. For Tarawih, some later scholars require explicit intention of Tarawih, and this is supported in al-Khaniyyah. The passage thus presents an intra-Hanafi difference: the majority do not require ta'yin, but some recommend it as precaution, and a minority for Tarawih require it.

Key Terms
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specifying the particular prayer (e.g., Fajr sunnah, Tarawih) in one's intention.
النقل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayers (nawafil), including sunan and voluntary prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, is it necessary to specify 'Tarawih' in the intention for Tarawih prayer?
A) Yes, it is absolutely required.
B) No, a general intention of supererogatory prayer is sufficient.
C) It is disliked to specify.
D) One must intend both the prayer and the reward.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, specification of intention is not required for supererogatory prayers, but precaution recommends it, especially for Tarawih.

The Ruling and Conditions of Standing (Qiyam) in Obligatory Prayers
Defines the obligation of standing and its rulings for valid prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of qiyam in obligatory prayers, identify the conditions for its obligation, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the measure of standing.

Core Idea
Standing is an obligatory pillar for every capable person in obligatory prayers; inability excuses one from standing but not from the prayer.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the obligation of standing (qiyam) in obligatory and wajib prayers. It defines what constitutes valid standing, outlines the conditions for its obligation, and addresses exceptions for those who are unable. The text also touches on an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the minimum duration of standing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that qiyam is an agreed-upon pillar (rukn) in obligatory and wajib prayers. Note that this is a ruling of obligation (fard).
The term 'متفق عليه' indicates consensus among the four Sunni schools.
2
Understand the definition of valid standing
The standard is that if one extends his hands while standing, they should not reach his knees. This ensures upright posture.
This excludes leaning or bending.
3
Recognize the conditions for obligation
Standing is obligatory only on one who is able to stand and also able to bow and prostrate while standing. If standing is not possible, the obligation drops.
The text lists scenarios where standing is excused or replaced.
4
Explore exceptions and alternatives
The passage details several exceptions: difficulty, inability to prostrate, incontinence, exposure of awrah, inability to recite while standing, etc. Each has a specific ruling.
In some cases, the person may choose between gesturing while standing or sitting.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on duration
Imam Abu Hanifa requires standing long enough for one long verse; the Sahibayn require three short verses. The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn.
This difference affects the minimum time one must remain standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفترض (القيام) وهو ركن متفق عليه في الفرائض والواجبات وحد القيام أن يكون بحيث إذا مد يديه لا ينال ركبتيه (في غير النفل) ترك ها و والمراد بالهاوي الألف الناشيء بالمد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة، فإذا حذفه الحالف، أو الذابح، أو المكبر للصلاة، أو حذف الهاء من الجلالة إختلف في إنعقاد يمينه وحل ذبيحته، وصحة تحريمته، فلا يترك ذلك إحتياطاً قوله : (ويفترض القيام على قادر عليه وعلى الركوع والسجود، ولا يفوته بقيامه شرط طهارة مثلاً، ولا قدرة القراءة، فلو تعسر عليه القيام، أو قدر عليه وعجز عن السجود لا يلزمه لكنه يخير في الثانية بين الإيماء قائماً، أو قاعداً كما لو كان معه جرح يسيل إذا سجد فإنه يخير كذلك، ولو كان بحيث لو قام سلس بوله أو لو قام ينكشف من العورة ما يمنع الصلاة، أو بعجز عن القراءة حال القيام وفي القعود لا يحصل شيء من ذلك يجب القعود، وكذا إن كان بحيث لو صلى قاعداً قدر على الإتمام، وقائماً لا ومفروض القيام وواجبه ومستونه ومستحبه بقدر القراءة فيه كما في سكب الأنهر ويقدر ذلك في نحو الامي، أن يقف قدر ثلاث آيات قصار على قولهما أو آية طويلة على قول الإمام لتحصيل الفرض، وعند سقوط القراءة يسقط التجديد كالقيام في الشفع الثاني من الفرض لأنه لا قراءة فيه فالركن فيه أصل القيام لا إمتداده كما في القهستاني، ويكره على إحدى الرجلين إلا لعذر. قوله : (وهو ركن متفق عليه أصلي والقراءة ركن زائد إذ هي زينة القيام، ولهذا يتحمل الإمام القراءة دون القيام قاله في الشرح)
And standing is obligatory; it is an agreed-upon pillar in obligatory and wajib prayers. The definition of standing is that one should be in a position such that if he extends his hands, they do not reach his knees (in other than supererogatory). ... And standing is obligatory upon one who is able for it and for bowing and prostration, and he does not miss through his standing a condition of purification, for example, nor ability to recite. If standing becomes difficult for him, or he is able but unable to prostrate, it is not obligatory on him, but he is given a choice in the second [rak'ah] between gesturing while standing or sitting... And it is disliked to pray standing on one leg without an excuse. ... He said: It is an original agreed-upon pillar, and recitation is an additional pillar, for it is the adornment of standing; for this reason the imam bears the burden of recitation but not standing.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation of standing (qiyam) in obligatory and wajib prayers. It is an agreed-upon pillar (rukn). The definition of standing is that the hands when extended do not reach the knees (full standing). For those unable to stand, the obligation drops, and they may pray sitting or gesturing. Various scenarios are discussed: if standing causes inability to prostrate, one may choose; if standing leads to incontinence or exposure of awrah, one should sit; if one can complete the prayer only while sitting, sitting becomes obligatory. The measure of required standing is the time needed for recitation (at least three short verses or one long verse according to Imam). The passage also notes that recitation is a separate pillar, which the imam bears for the congregation. Standing on one leg is disliked unless excused.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing upright in prayer, a rukn for obligatory prayers.
متفق عليه (muttafaq alayh): Agreed upon by all schools of thought as a pillar.
ركن زائد (rukn za'id): An additional pillar (recitation) that complements standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person can stand but cannot prostrate due to injury, what is the ruling?
A) He must pray standing and gesture for prostration.
B) He is excused from prayer altogether.
C) He may choose between gesturing while standing or sitting.
D) He must pray sitting.

Key Takeaway
Standing is a fundamental pillar of obligatory prayer, but its requirement adapts to the worshipper's ability, reflecting the principle that burdens are not placed beyond capacity.

Intention in Sunnah Prayers: Specification Not Required
Commentary on intention for supererogatory prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention specification for supererogatory prayers and explain the reasoning based on time specification.

Core Idea
For sunnah prayers, time specifies — general intention suffices, but precaution recommends specification.

The Hanafi school holds that in supererogatory prayers, a general intention is sufficient because the time itself identifies the prayer. However, to avoid disagreement with other schools, it is cautious to specify the intention. This lesson examines the ruling and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify supererogatory prayers (nafl/sunnah) and the ruling: specification of intention (ta'yin) is not required.
The matn states: 'Wa la yushtarat al-ta'yin fi al-nafl'.
2
Understand the dalil
The reason given is that the occurrence of these prayers at their designated times suffices for identification (time specifies).
Al-Tahtawi comments: 'li-anna wuqu'aha fi awqatiha yughni 'an al-ta'yin'.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars, especially from other madhhabs, require specification. The precaution (ihtiyat) is to specify to exit the disagreement.
The author of al-Munyah is cited for precaution, and al-Mughni mentions a requirement for Tarawih.
4
Distinguish between types
Distinguish between absolute sunnah and time-specific sunnah (like sunnah of Fajr). For time-specific, the time alone designates.
The passage also notes 'sunnah of the time' should be distinguished between before and after the obligatory prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يشترط التعين في النقل) ولو سنة الفجر في الأصح وكذا التراويح عند عامة المشايخ وهو الصحيح والاحتياط التعين فينوي مراعياً صفتها. ثم قوله: (ولا يشترط التعين في النقل) مراده به ما يعم السنن لأن وقوعها في أوقاتها يغني عن التعين وبه صارت سنة لا بالتعين ولا فرق بين أ أن ينوي الصلاة، أو الصلاة الله تعالى لأن المصلي لا يصلي لغير الله تعالى. قوله: (والإحتياط التعين) قاله صاحب المنية، وذلك للخروج من خلاف من إشترط في فعل السنة نيتها. قال صاحب المغني: في التراويح لا يكفيه مطلق النية، ولا نية التطوع عند بعض المتأخرين، بل يشترط نية التراويح، وصححه في الخانية. قاله السيد قوله: (أو سنة الوقت أي سنة فرض الوقت، وعليه فينبغي التمييز بين القبلية، والبعدية. قوله: (و) يفترض (القيام) وهو ركن متفق عليه في الفرائض والواجبات وحد القيام أن يكون بحيث إذا مد يديه لا ينال ركبتيه وقوله (في غير النفل) ترك ها و والمراد بالهاوي الألف الناشيء بالمد الذي في اللام الثانية من الجلالة، فإذا حذفه الحالف، أو الذابح، أو المكبر للصلاة، أو حذف الهاء من الجلالة إختلف في إنعقاد يمينه وحل ذبيحته، وصحة تحريمته، فلا يترك ذلك إحتياطاً. قوله : (ذكر هذا الأخير) إسم الإشارة راجع إلى الشرط الأخير. قوله : (إذ إنعامه) علة لقوله من بالايقاظ لجمعه، ولم أره الخ، وكأنه في جواب سؤال حاصله كيف جمعت هذه الشروط، ولم تسبق بها. قوله: (ولا ممنوعاً) تكرار مع ما قبله. قوله ولا يشترط التعين في النقل مراده به ما يعم السنن لأن وقوعها في أوقاتها يغني عن التعين وبه صارت سنة لا بالتعين ولا فرق بين أ أن ينوي الصلاة، أو الصلاة الله تعالى لأن المصلي لا يصلي لغير الله تعالى. قوله : (والإحتياط التعين) قاله صاحب المنية، وذلك للخروج من خلاف من إشترط في فعل السنة نيتها. قال صاحب المغني : في التراويح لا يكفيه مطلق النية، ولا نية التطوع عند بعض المتأخرين، بل يشترط نية التراويح، وصححه في الخانية. قاله السيد. قوله : (أو سنة الوقت أي سنة فرض الوقت، وعليه فينبغي التمييز بين القبلية، والبعدية. قوله : ( ويفترض القيام على قادر عليه وعلى الركوع والسجود، ولا يفوته بقيامه شرط طهارة مثلاً، ولا قدرة القراءة، فلو تعسر عليه القيام، أو قدر عليه وعجز عن السجود لا يلزمه لكنه يخير في الثانية بين الإيماء قائماً، أو قاعداً كما لو كان معه جرح يسيل إذا سجد فإنه يخير كذلك، ولو كان بحيث لو قام سلس بوله أو لو قام ينكشف من العورة ما يمنع الصلاة، أو بعجز عن القراءة حال القيام وفي القعود لا يحصل شيء من ذلك يجب القعود، وكذا إن كان بحيث لو صلى قاعداً قدر على الإتمام، وقائماً لا ومفروض القيام وواجبه ومستونه ومستحبه بقدر القراءة فيه كما في سكب الأنهر ويقدر ذلك في نحو الامي، أن يقف قدر ثلاث آيات قصار على قولهما أو آية طويلة على قول الإمام لتحصيل الفرض، وعند سقوط القراءة يسقط التجديد كالقيام في الشفع الثاني من الفرض لأنه لا قراءة فيه فالركن فيه أصل القيام لا إمتداده كما في القهستاني، ويكره على إحدى الرجلين إلا لعذر. قوله : (وهو ركن متفق عليه أصلي والقراءة ركن زائد إذ هي زينة القيام، ولهذا يتحمل الإمام القراءة دون القيام قاله في الشرح. فلا بد. قوله: (و) يفترض (القراءة) ولا تكون إلا بسماعها كما تقدم لقوله تعالى فاقرؤا ما تيسر من القرآن وهي ركن زائد على قول الجمهور لسقوطها بلا ضرورة عن المقتدي عندنا، وعن المدرك في الركوع إجماعاً. وبالنص كانت القراءة فرضاً ولو قرأ آية قصيرة مركبة من كلمتين كقوله تعالى، ثم نظر في ظاهر الرواية وأما الآية التي هي كلمة كمدها متان أو حرف ص ن ق، أو حرفان حم طس. قوله: (والواجبات) ظاهره شمول قضاء النفل الذي أفسده، وكذا المنذور وإن لم ينص على القيام فيه على أحد قولين. قوله: (وحد القيام) أي حد أدناه، وتمامه بالإنتصاب كالقنا وهو بهذه الصفة مما يورث الخشوع في الصلاة كما ذكره العارف بالله تعالى سيدي أحمد زروق في نصيحته. قوله: (متعلق بالقيام لو يفترض الذي قدره الشرح. قوله: (كما سنذكره) من أن مبناه على التوسع. قوله: (ولا تكون إلا بسماعها إلا لمانع كصمم أو جلية أصوات، أو نحو ذلك من العوارض المانعة لصحة الحاسة عن السماع واكتفى الكرخي بمجرد تصحيح الحروف نفسه لأن القراءة فعل اللسان والسماع فعل الصماخ دون اللسان فليس من مورد القراءة، قال في البدائع، وقول الكرخي أصح وأقيس وبعضهم نسبه إلى أبي يوسف والمعتمد الأول، وخفض صوته ببعض الحروف بحيث لا يسمع نفسه مقتصراً لا تفسد الصلاة على الصحيح لعموم البلوى كما في المضمرات عن الذخيرة، ومحلها القيام ولو حكماً كالقعود لعذر، أو في نافلة فلو قرأ في ركوع أو سجود، أو قعود لم يكن بدلاً عن قيام لا يسقط بها الواجب، ويكره تحريماً لأنه تغيير المشروع وإن كان ساهياً، وجب عليه سجود السهو. قوله: (لقوله تعالى: فاقرؤا ما تيسر من القرآن وجه الدلالة أن الأمر يقتضي الوجوب، والقراءة لا تجب خارج الصلاة بالإجماع فتعين الأمر في الصلاة، وقال: لا صلاة إلا بقراءة رواه مسلم من حديث أبي هريرة، وعليه إنعقد الإجماع ولا عبرة عن خرق الإجماع كأبي بكر الأصم بقوله القراءة في الصلاة ليست فرضاً أصلاً بل سنة. قوله: (وهي ركن زائد على قول الجمهور) وقال الغزنوي صاحب الحاوي القدسي أنها فرض، ولست بركن. قوله: لسقوطها بلا ضرورة أشار به إلى الفرق بين الركن الزائد، وغيره وهو الأصلي فإنه إنما يسقط في بعض الأحوال لضرورة لكن إلى خلف والزائد ما يسقط لا إلى خلف، وقال في الشرح: الزائد هو الجزء الذي إذا انتفى كان الحكم المركب باقياً بحسب إعتبار الشرع، وعلى هذا لو حلف لا يصلي فأحرم، وقام وركع وسجد بلا قراءة حنث. قال السيد: اعترض بأن في تسمية القراءة ركناً زائداً تدافعاً وأجيب بأنها ركن بإعتبار إنتفاء الماهية في حالة وزائد في أخرى فمن حيث فساد الصلاة بترك القراءة فيها حالة الإنفراد مع القدرة عليها تكون ركناً، ومن حيث صحة صلاة المقتدي مع ترك القراءة تكون زائداً. قوله: (وبالنص كانت الخ) النص هو الآية المتقدمة لأن المراد قراءة القرآن حقيقة.
He said: (And specification is not required in supererogatory [prayers]) even for the Fajr sunnah according to the most correct view, and similarly for Tarawih according to general scholars, and it is correct, and precaution is specification, so one intends considering its description. Then he said: (And specification is not required in supererogatory [prayers]) meaning it includes the sunan because their occurrence at their times suffices for specification, and by that they become sunnah not by specification, and there is no difference between intending prayer or prayer for Allah because the one praying prays only for Allah. He said: (And precaution is specification) said by the author of al-Munyah, and that is to exit from the disagreement of those who require intention for supererogatory acts. The author of al-Mughni said: In Tarawih, absolute intention does not suffice, nor intention of supererogation according to some later scholars, rather intention of Tarawih is required, and it was authenticated in al-Khaniyyah. Said al-Sayyid: He said: (Or the time sunnah meaning the sunnah of the obligatory time, so accordingly one should distinguish between before and after. He said: (And) standing (is obligatory) and it is a pillar agreed upon in obligatory prayers and wajib prayers, and the minimum of standing is such that if he extends his hands he does not reach his knees. And his statement: (in other than supererogatory) left ha and waw, and the meaning of al-hawi is the alif that arises with madd in the second lam of al-Jalalah, so if the swearer, slaughterer, or magnifier for prayer omits it, or omits the ha of al-Jalalah, there is disagreement about the validity of his oath, permissibility of his slaughtered animal, and correctness of his tahrimah, so one should not leave it out of precaution. He said: (mentioned this last one) the demonstrative pronoun refers to the last condition. He said: (Indeed His favors) is a reason for his statement 'by awakening me to compile it, and I have not seen it before compiled' and it is as if in answer to a question: how did you gather these conditions, not preceded by them. He said: (And not prevented) is repetition with what precedes. He said: And specification is not required in supererogatory... (repetition)... He said: (And standing is obligatory for one able to do it, and for bowing and prostration, and he does not lose by his standing a condition like purity, nor ability to recite. So if standing is difficult for him, or he is capable but unable to prostrate, it is not required but he has a choice in the second [rak'ah] between gesturing while standing or sitting, as if he had a wound that oozes when he prostrates, he has a choice similarly. And if when he stands he has urinary incontinence, or his private part is exposed preventing prayer, or he is unable to recite while standing but while sitting none of that occurs, sitting is obligatory. Similarly if he is such that if he prays sitting he can complete, but standing he cannot. And the obligatory, wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb of standing are according to the recitation therein as in Saki al-Anhur, and that is estimated for the illiterate as standing for three short verses according to them, or one long verse according to Imam for fulfilling the obligation. And when recitation drops, newness drops like standing in the second cycle of obligatory because there is no recitation therein, so the pillar is the origin of standing not its duration as in al-Qahistani. And it is disliked to stand on one foot except for an excuse. He said: (It is a basic agreed-upon pillar, and recitation is an additional pillar because it is the adornment of standing, and therefore the imam carries recitation but not standing, as stated in the Sharh. Necessarily. He said: (And) recitation (is obligatory) and it is only with hearing it as previously explained, because Allah says: 'Recite what is easy of the Quran', and it is an additional pillar according to the majority because it drops without necessity for the follower in our madhhab, and for the one who catches the bowing, by consensus. And by text, recitation was obligatory, even if one recites a short verse composed of two words like His statement 'then he looked' in the apparent narration, and as for a verse that is one word like 'Madhammatan' or a letter like 'Sad Noon Qaf' or two letters like 'Ha Meem Ta Seen'. He said: (And the obligations) apparently includes making up a supererogatory that one has spoiled, and likewise a vowed prayer even if standing was not stipulated therein according to one of two sayings. He said: (And the definition of standing) means its minimum, and its completion is with erectness like a spear, and this attribute brings humility in prayer as mentioned by the knower of Allah Sayyidi Ahmad Zarruq in his advice. He said: (Related to standing if it is obligatory which the Sharh estimated. He said: (As we will mention) that it is based on expansion. He said: (And it is only with hearing it except for an impediment like deafness or loud noises or similar hindrances that prevent the sense from hearing, and al-Karkhi relied on mere correct articulation of letters themselves because recitation is an action of the tongue and hearing is an action of the ear, not the tongue, so it is not from the domain of recitation. He said in al-Bada'i': al-Karkhi's view is more correct and more analogous, and some attributed it to Abu Yusuf, and the relied-upon is the first. And lowering his voice with some letters such that he does not hear himself alone does not invalidate the prayer according to the correct view due to general affliction as in al-Mudmarat from al-Dhakhirah. And its place is standing, even if de jure like sitting due to an excuse, or in supererogatory. So if one recites in bowing or prostration or sitting, it is not a substitute for standing, the obligation is not fulfilled by it, and it is prohibitively disliked because it changes what is legislated. And if he was forgetful, he must perform sajdah al-sahw. He said: (For His saying: 'Recite what is easy of the Quran') the aspect of evidence is that the command necessitates obligation, and recitation is not obligatory outside prayer by consensus, so the command is specified to prayer. And he said: 'No prayer except with recitation' narrated by Muslim from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and upon it consensus is formed, and no attention is paid to breaking consensus like Abu Bakr al-Asamm's statement that recitation in prayer is not obligatory at all but rather sunnah. He said: (And it is an additional pillar according to the majority) and al-Ghaznawi, author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, said it is fard but not a pillar. He said: 'Because it drops without necessity' he indicated by it the difference between an additional pillar and other than it, which is the basic pillar, for indeed it only drops in some situations due to necessity but to a successor, while the additional one drops without a successor. And he said in the Sharh: The additional is the part that if it is absent, the composite ruling remains according to the consideration of the Shari'ah. On this, if one swears not to pray, then enters ihram, stands, bows, and prostrates without recitation, he breaks his oath. Al-Sayyid said: It was objected that calling recitation an additional pillar is contradictory. And it was answered: It is a pillar with regard to the absence of the essence in a situation and additional in another, so from the perspective that the prayer is invalidated by leaving recitation when praying alone while able, it is a pillar, and from the perspective that the prayer of the follower is valid with leaving recitation, it is additional. He said: (And by text it was...) the text is the aforementioned verse because the intention is recitation of the Quran literally.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah critically refines the rulings on intention (niyyah), standing (qiyam), and recitation (qira'ah) in prayer, following the Hanafi school. The author begins by restating the matn: specification of intention is not required for supererogatory prayers (nafl), even for the sunnah of Fajr or Tarawih, according to the most correct view. The reason given is that the time itself designates the prayer, so a general intention suffices. However, precaution (ihtiyat) is to specify the intention to avoid disagreement with those who require it. The commentary then distinguishes between 'sunnah of the time' and other supererogatory prayers, noting that one should differentiate between before and after the obligatory prayer. Next, the passage discusses the pillar of standing (qiyam). It is an agreed-upon pillar in obligatory and wajib prayers. The minimum standing is defined as such that when one extends his hands, he does not reach his knees. For those unable to stand or prostrate, concessions apply. The text explains that the obligation of standing is linked to the ability to recite, and if recitation drops, the standing's duration is reduced. Standing on one foot is disliked unless excused. Finally, the passage addresses recitation (qira'ah) as an additional pillar. It is fard (obligatory) based on the Quranic command 'Recite what is easy' and the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation.' Recitation must be audible to oneself. It drops for the follower (muqtadi) and for one who catches the bowing (mudrik) by consensus. A verse of at least two words or a single word like 'Mudhammatan' suffices. The distinction between a basic pillar and an additional pillar is clarified: an additional pillar is one whose omission does not require repetition but may necessitate sajdah al-sahw, and it can drop without a substitute (la ila khalaf). The commentary also notes a difference with al-Ghaznawi who said recitation is fard but not a pillar, and with Abu Bakr al-Asamm who denied its obligation altogether—but these are not followed.

Key Terms
التعين (al-ta'yin): Specifying which prayer one is performing by intention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is specification of intention not required for sunnah prayers?
A) Because the Prophet did not specify his intention.
B) Because the time of the prayer itself identifies it.
C) Because supererogatory prayers are less important.
D) Because intention is never required in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require specification of intention for sunnah prayers; the time serves as the identifier.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
Standing (Qiyam) in Prayer: Pillar and Conditions
Commentary on standing in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on standing in prayer, define its minimum, and identify valid excuses for omitting or modifying it.

Core Idea
Standing is a basic agreed-upon pillar; its minimum is defined by hand-to-knee distance, and it drops only with valid excuse.

Standing (qiyam) is an essential pillar of obligatory and wajib prayers, agreed upon by all schools. The Hanafi school defines its minimum length and specifies conditions under which it may be omitted or performed differently. This lesson examines the ruling, its definition, and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on standing
Standing is fard (obligatory) and a rukn (pillar) in obligatory and wajib prayers for those able.
The matn states: 'Yaf'tarid al-qiyam' – standing is obligatory.
2
Define the minimum standing
The minimum is that when one extends his hands, he does not reach his knees (i.e., erect posture).
Al-Tahtawi adds: 'wa hadd al-qiyam an yakuuna bihaythi idha madda yadayhi la yanalu rukbatayhi'.
3
Identify conditions for obligation
Standing is required only for those able; if unable due to illness, injury, or safety, one may sit or gesture.
The text mentions exceptions for urinary incontinence, exposure of awrah, inability to recite while standing, etc.
4
Understand the role of recitation in duration
The obligatory amount of standing corresponds to the obligatory recitation (e.g., three short verses). If recitation drops, the standing requirement may reduce.
From 'Saki al-Anhur': 'al-qiyam wujubuhu biqadr al-qira'ah'.

هي كلمة كمدها متان أو حرف ص ن ق، أو حرفان حم طس. قوله: (والواجبات) ظاهره شمول قضاء النفل الذي أفسده، وكذا المنذور وإن لم ينص على القيام فيه على أحد قولين. قوله: (وحد القيام) أي حد أدناه، وتمامه بالإنتصاب كالقنا وهو بهذه الصفة مما يورث الخشوع في الصلاة كما ذكره العارف بالله تعالى سيدي أحمد زروق في نصيحته. قوله: (متعلق بالقيام لو يفترض الذي قدره الشرح. قوله: (كما سنذكره) من أن مبناه على التوسع. قوله: (ولا تكون إلا بسماعها إلا لمانع كصمم أو جلية أصوات، أو نحو ذلك من العوارض المانعة لصحة الحاسة عن السماع واكتفى الكرخي بمجرد تصحيح الحروف نفسه لأن القراءة فعل اللسان والسماع فعل الصماخ دون اللسان فليس من مورد القراءة، قال في البدائع، وقول الكرخي أصح وأقيس وبعضهم نسبه إلى أبي يوسف والمعتمد الأول، وخفض صوته ببعض الحروف بحيث لا يسمع نفسه مقتصراً لا تفسد الصلاة على الصحيح لعموم البلوى كما في المضمرات عن الذخيرة، ومحلها القيام ولو حكماً كالقعود لعذر، أو في نافلة فلو قرأ في ركوع أو سجود، أو قعود لم يكن بدلاً عن قيام لا يسقط بها الواجب، ويكره تحريماً لأنه تغيير المشروع وإن كان ساهياً، وجب عليه سجود السهو. قوله: (لقوله تعالى: فاقرؤا ما تيسر من القرآن وجه الدلالة أن الأمر يقتضي الوجوب، والقراءة لا تجب خارج الصلاة بالإجماع فتعين الأمر في الصلاة، وقال: لا صلاة إلا بقراءة رواه مسلم من حديث أبي هريرة، وعليه إنعقد الإجماع ولا عبرة عن خرق الإجماع كأبي بكر الأصم بقوله القراءة في الصلاة ليست فرضاً أصلاً بل سنة. قوله: (وهي ركن زائد على قول الجمهور) وقال الغزنوي صاحب الحاوي القدسي أنها فرض، ولست بركن. قوله: لسقوطها بلا ضرورة أشار به إلى الفرق بين الركن الزائد، وغيره وهو الأصلي فإنه إنما يسقط في بعض الأحوال لضرورة لكن إلى خلف والزائد ما يسقط لا إلى خلف، وقال في الشرح: الزائد هو الجزء الذي إذا انتفى كان الحكم المركب باقياً بحسب إعتبار الشرع، وعلى هذا لو حلف لا يصلي فأحرم، وقام وركع وسجد بلا قراءة حنث. قال السيد: اعترض بأن في تسمية القراءة ركناً زائداً تدافعاً وأجيب بأنها ركن بإعتبار إنتفاء الماهية في حالة وزائد في أخرى فمن حيث فساد الصلاة بترك القراءة فيها حالة الإنفراد مع القدرة عليها تكون ركناً، ومن حيث صحة صلاة المقتدي مع ترك القراءة تكون زائداً. قوله: (وبالنص كانت الخ) النص هو الآية المتقدمة لأن المراد قراءة القرآن حقيقة.
He said: (And specification is not required in supererogatory [prayers]) even for the Fajr sunnah according to the most correct view, and similarly for Tarawih according to general scholars, and it is correct, and precaution is specification, so one intends considering its description. Then he said: (And specification is not required in supererogatory [prayers]) meaning it includes the sunan because their occurrence at their times suffices for specification, and by that they become sunnah not by specification, and there is no difference between intending prayer or prayer for Allah because the one praying prays only for Allah. He said: (And precaution is specification) said by the author of al-Munyah, and that is to exit from the disagreement of those who require intention for supererogatory acts. The author of al-Mughni said: In Tarawih, absolute intention does not suffice, nor intention of supererogation according to some later scholars, rather intention of Tarawih is required, and it was authenticated in al-Khaniyyah. Said al-Sayyid: He said: (Or the time sunnah meaning the sunnah of the obligatory time, so accordingly one should distinguish between before and after. He said: (And) standing (is obligatory) and it is a pillar agreed upon in obligatory prayers and wajib prayers, and the minimum of standing is such that if he extends his hands he does not reach his knees. And his statement: (in other than supererogatory) left ha and waw, and the meaning of al-hawi is the alif that arises with madd in the second lam of al-Jalalah, so if the swearer, slaughterer, or magnifier for prayer omits it, or omits the ha of al-Jalalah, there is disagreement about the validity of his oath, permissibility of his slaughtered animal, and correctness of his tahrimah, so one should not leave it out of precaution. He said: (mentioned this last one) the demonstrative pronoun refers to the last condition. He said: (Indeed His favors) is a reason for his statement 'by awakening me to compile it, and I have not seen it before compiled' and it is as if in answer to a question: how did you gather these conditions, not preceded by them. He said: (And not prevented) is repetition with what precedes. He said: And specification is not required in supererogatory... (repetition)... He said: (And standing is obligatory for one able to do it, and for bowing and prostration, and he does not lose by his standing a condition like purity, nor ability to recite. So if standing is difficult for him, or he is capable but unable to prostrate, it is not required but he has a choice in the second [rak'ah] between gesturing while standing or sitting, as if he had a wound that oozes when he prostrates, he has a choice similarly. And if when he stands he has urinary incontinence, or his private part is exposed preventing prayer, or he is unable to recite while standing but while sitting none of that occurs, sitting is obligatory. Similarly if he is such that if he prays sitting he can complete, but standing he cannot. And the obligatory, wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb of standing are according to the recitation therein as in Saki al-Anhur, and that is estimated for the illiterate as standing for three short verses according to them, or one long verse according to Imam for fulfilling the obligation. And when recitation drops, newness drops like standing in the second cycle of obligatory because there is no recitation therein, so the pillar is the origin of standing not its duration as in al-Qahistani. And it is disliked to stand on one foot except for an excuse. He said: (It is a basic agreed-upon pillar, and recitation is an additional pillar because it is the adornment of standing, and therefore the imam carries recitation but not standing, as stated in the Sharh. Necessarily. He said: (And) recitation (is obligatory) and it is only with hearing it as previously explained, because Allah says: 'Recite what is easy of the Quran', and it is an additional pillar according to the majority because it drops without necessity for the follower in our madhhab, and for the one who catches the bowing, by consensus. And by text, recitation was obligatory, even if one recites a short verse composed of two words like His statement 'then he looked' in the apparent narration, and as for a verse that is one word like 'Madhammatan' or a letter like 'Sad Noon Qaf' or two letters like 'Ha Meem Ta Seen'. He said: (And the obligations) apparently includes making up a supererogatory that one has spoiled, and likewise a vowed prayer even if standing was not stipulated therein according to one of two sayings. He said: (And the definition of standing) means its minimum, and its completion is with erectness like a spear, and this attribute brings humility in prayer as mentioned by the knower of Allah Sayyidi Ahmad Zarruq in his advice. He said: (Related to standing if it is obligatory which the Sharh estimated. He said: (As we will mention) that it is based on expansion. He said: (And it is only with hearing it except for an impediment like deafness or loud noises or similar hindrances that prevent the sense from hearing, and al-Karkhi relied on mere correct articulation of letters themselves because recitation is an action of the tongue and hearing is an action of the ear, not the tongue, so it is not from the domain of recitation. He said in al-Bada'i': al-Karkhi's view is more correct and more analogous, and some attributed it to Abu Yusuf, and the relied-upon is the first. And lowering his voice with some letters such that he does not hear himself alone does not invalidate the prayer according to the correct view due to general affliction as in al-Mudmarat from al-Dhakhirah. And its place is standing, even if de jure like sitting due to an excuse, or in supererogatory. So if one recites in bowing or prostration or sitting, it is not a substitute for standing, the obligation is not fulfilled by it, and it is prohibitively disliked because it changes what is legislated. And if he was forgetful, he must perform sajdah al-sahw. He said: (For His saying: 'Recite what is easy of the Quran') the aspect of evidence is that the command necessitates obligation, and recitation is not obligatory outside prayer by consensus, so the command is specified to prayer. And he said: 'No prayer except with recitation' narrated by Muslim from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and upon it consensus is formed, and no attention is paid to breaking consensus like Abu Bakr al-Asamm's statement that recitation in prayer is not obligatory at all but rather sunnah. He said: (And it is an additional pillar according to the majority) and al-Ghaznawi, author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, said it is fard but not a pillar. He said: 'Because it drops without necessity' he indicated by it the difference between an additional pillar and other than it, which is the basic pillar, for indeed it only drops in some situations due to necessity but to a successor, while the additional one drops without a successor. And he said in the Sharh: The additional is the part that if it is absent, the composite ruling remains according to the consideration of the Shari'ah. On this, if one swears not to pray, then enters ihram, stands, bows, and prostrates without recitation, he breaks his oath. Al-Sayyid said: It was objected that calling recitation an additional pillar is contradictory. And it was answered: It is a pillar with regard to the absence of the essence in a situation and additional in another, so from the perspective that the prayer is invalidated by leaving recitation when praying alone while able, it is a pillar, and from the perspective that the prayer of the follower is valid with leaving recitation, it is additional. He said: (And by text it was...) the text is the aforementioned verse because the intention is recitation of the Quran literally.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah critically refines the rulings on intention (niyyah), standing (qiyam), and recitation (qira'ah) in prayer, following the Hanafi school. The author begins by restating the matn: specification of intention is not required for supererogatory prayers (nafl), even for the sunnah of Fajr or Tarawih, according to the most correct view. The reason given is that the time itself designates the prayer, so a general intention suffices. However, precaution (ihtiyat) is to specify the intention to avoid disagreement with those who require it. The commentary then distinguishes between 'sunnah of the time' and other supererogatory prayers, noting that one should differentiate between before and after the obligatory prayer. Next, the passage discusses the pillar of standing (qiyam). It is an agreed-upon pillar in obligatory and wajib prayers. The minimum standing is defined as such that when one extends his hands, he does not reach his knees. For those unable to stand or prostrate, concessions apply. The text explains that the obligation of standing is linked to the ability to recite, and if recitation drops, the standing's duration is reduced. Standing on one foot is disliked unless excused. Finally, the passage addresses recitation (qira'ah) as an additional pillar. It is fard (obligatory) based on the Quranic command 'Recite what is easy' and the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation.' Recitation must be audible to oneself. It drops for the follower (muqtadi) and for one who catches the bowing (mudrik) by consensus. A verse of at least two words or a single word like 'Mudhammatan' suffices. The distinction between a basic pillar and an additional pillar is clarified: an additional pillar is one whose omission does not require repetition but may necessitate sajdah al-sahw, and it can drop without a substitute (la ila khalaf). The commentary also notes a difference with al-Ghaznawi who said recitation is fard but not a pillar, and with Abu Bakr al-Asamm who denied its obligation altogether—but these are not followed.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing erect as a pillar of prayer for those able
الركن الأصلي (al-rukn al-asli): Basic pillar that cannot drop without making the act invalid; it drops only to a successor (e.g., standing to sitting).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum definition of standing (qiyam) in prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Standing tall with hands at sides.
B) When you extend your hands, they do not reach your knees.
C) Being upright for at least one second.
D) Standing on both feet with feet together.

Key Takeaway
Standing is a basic agreed-upon pillar; its minimum is erect posture with specific hand-to-knee measure, and it drops only for valid excuse.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
8 min
Recitation (Qira'ah) in Prayer: An Additional Pillar
Commentary on recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that recitation is an additional pillar, distinguish it from a basic pillar, and state the evidence and exceptions.

Core Idea
Recitation is an additional pillar that drops for the follower without a substitute; it is obligatory based on Quran and hadith.

Recitation of the Quran in prayer is obligatory according to the Hanafi school, but it is classified as an 'additional pillar' (rukn za'id) rather than a basic pillar. This distinction means it can drop in certain situations without invalidating the prayer. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, and the concept of additional pillar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on recitation
Recitation is fard (obligatory) in prayer, based on the command 'Iqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' and the hadith 'La salata illa bi-qira'ah'.
The passage cites the Quranic verse and the hadith from Muslim.
2
Classify recitation as an additional pillar
Recitation is called a 'rukn za'id' (additional pillar) because it can drop in certain situations without invalidating the prayer (e.g., for the follower).
Al-Tahtawi explains: 'l-suqutiha bi-la darura' and distinguishes from basic pillar which drops only to a successor.
3
Identify when recitation drops
Recitation drops for the follower (muqtadi) and for the one who catches the bowing (mudrik) by consensus.
The text says: 'lisuqutiha bi-la darura 'an al-muqtadi 'indana, wa 'an al-mudrik fi al-ruku' ijma'an.'
4
Understand the distinction between fard and rukn
Some scholars (e.g., al-Ghaznawi) say recitation is fard but not a rukn, while the majority say it is an additional rukn. The difference affects whether sajdah al-sahw is needed.
The passage mentions al-Ghaznawi's view: 'anna al-qira'ata fardun wa lastu bi-rukn.'

وجب عليه سجود السهو. قوله: (لقوله تعالى: فاقرؤا ما تيسر من القرآن وجه الدلالة أن الأمر يقتضي الوجوب، والقراءة لا تجب خارج الصلاة بالإجماع فتعين الأمر في الصلاة، وقال: لا صلاة إلا بقراءة رواه مسلم من حديث أبي هريرة، وعليه إنعقد الإجماع ولا عبرة عن خرق الإجماع كأبي بكر الأصم بقوله القراءة في الصلاة ليست فرضاً أصلاً بل سنة. قوله: (وهي ركن زائد على قول الجمهور) وقال الغزنوي صاحب الحاوي القدسي أنها فرض، ولست بركن. قوله: لسقوطها بلا ضرورة أشار به إلى الفرق بين الركن الزائد، وغيره وهو الأصلي فإنه إنما يسقط في بعض الأحوال لضرورة لكن إلى خلف والزائد ما يسقط لا إلى خلف، وقال في الشرح: الزائد هو الجزء الذي إذا انتفى كان الحكم المركب باقياً بحسب إعتبار الشرع، وعلى هذا لو حلف لا يصلي فأحرم، وقام وركع وسجد بلا قراءة حنث. قال السيد: اعترض بأن في تسمية القراءة ركناً زائداً تدافعاً وأجيب بأنها ركن بإعتبار إنتفاء الماهية في حالة وزائد في أخرى فمن حيث فساد الصلاة بترك القراءة فيها حالة الإنفراد مع القدرة عليها تكون ركناً، ومن حيث صحة صلاة المقتدي مع ترك القراءة تكون زائداً. قوله: (وبالنص كانت الخ) النص هو الآية المتقدمة لأن المراد قراءة القرآن حقيقة.
He said: (And specification is not required in supererogatory [prayers]) even for the Fajr sunnah according to the most correct view, and similarly for Tarawih according to general scholars, and it is correct, and precaution is specification, so one intends considering its description. Then he said: (And specification is not required in supererogatory [prayers]) meaning it includes the sunan because their occurrence at their times suffices for specification, and by that they become sunnah not by specification, and there is no difference between intending prayer or prayer for Allah because the one praying prays only for Allah. He said: (And precaution is specification) said by the author of al-Munyah, and that is to exit from the disagreement of those who require intention for supererogatory acts. The author of al-Mughni said: In Tarawih, absolute intention does not suffice, nor intention of supererogation according to some later scholars, rather intention of Tarawih is required, and it was authenticated in al-Khaniyyah. Said al-Sayyid: He said: (Or the time sunnah meaning the sunnah of the obligatory time, so accordingly one should distinguish between before and after. He said: (And) standing (is obligatory) and it is a pillar agreed upon in obligatory prayers and wajib prayers, and the minimum of standing is such that if he extends his hands he does not reach his knees. And his statement: (in other than supererogatory) left ha and waw, and the meaning of al-hawi is the alif that arises with madd in the second lam of al-Jalalah, so if the swearer, slaughterer, or magnifier for prayer omits it, or omits the ha of al-Jalalah, there is disagreement about the validity of his oath, permissibility of his slaughtered animal, and correctness of his tahrimah, so one should not leave it out of precaution. He said: (mentioned this last one) the demonstrative pronoun refers to the last condition. He said: (Indeed His favors) is a reason for his statement 'by awakening me to compile it, and I have not seen it before compiled' and it is as if in answer to a question: how did you gather these conditions, not preceded by them. He said: (And not prevented) is repetition with what precedes. He said: And specification is not required in supererogatory... (repetition)... He said: (And standing is obligatory for one able to do it, and for bowing and prostration, and he does not lose by his standing a condition like purity, nor ability to recite. So if standing is difficult for him, or he is capable but unable to prostrate, it is not required but he has a choice in the second [rak'ah] between gesturing while standing or sitting, as if he had a wound that oozes when he prostrates, he has a choice similarly. And if when he stands he has urinary incontinence, or his private part is exposed preventing prayer, or he is unable to recite while standing but while sitting none of that occurs, sitting is obligatory. Similarly if he is such that if he prays sitting he can complete, but standing he cannot. And the obligatory, wajib, sunnah, and mustahabb of standing are according to the recitation therein as in Saki al-Anhur, and that is estimated for the illiterate as standing for three short verses according to them, or one long verse according to Imam for fulfilling the obligation. And when recitation drops, newness drops like standing in the second cycle of obligatory because there is no recitation therein, so the pillar is the origin of standing not its duration as in al-Qahistani. And it is disliked to stand on one foot except for an excuse. He said: (It is a basic agreed-upon pillar, and recitation is an additional pillar because it is the adornment of standing, and therefore the imam carries recitation but not standing, as stated in the Sharh. Necessarily. He said: (And) recitation (is obligatory) and it is only with hearing it as previously explained, because Allah says: 'Recite what is easy of the Quran', and it is an additional pillar according to the majority because it drops without necessity for the follower in our madhhab, and for the one who catches the bowing, by consensus. And by text, recitation was obligatory, even if one recites a short verse composed of two words like His statement 'then he looked' in the apparent narration, and as for a verse that is one word like 'Madhammatan' or a letter like 'Sad Noon Qaf' or two letters like 'Ha Meem Ta Seen'. He said: (And the obligations) apparently includes making up a supererogatory that one has spoiled, and likewise a vowed prayer even if standing was not stipulated therein according to one of two sayings. He said: (And the definition of standing) means its minimum, and its completion is with erectness like a spear, and this attribute brings humility in prayer as mentioned by the knower of Allah Sayyidi Ahmad Zarruq in his advice. He said: (Related to standing if it is obligatory which the Sharh estimated. He said: (As we will mention) that it is based on expansion. He said: (And it is only with hearing it except for an impediment like deafness or loud noises or similar hindrances that prevent the sense from hearing, and al-Karkhi relied on mere correct articulation of letters themselves because recitation is an action of the tongue and hearing is an action of the ear, not the tongue, so it is not from the domain of recitation. He said in al-Bada'i': al-Karkhi's view is more correct and more analogous, and some attributed it to Abu Yusuf, and the relied-upon is the first. And lowering his voice with some letters such that he does not hear himself alone does not invalidate the prayer according to the correct view due to general affliction as in al-Mudmarat from al-Dhakhirah. And its place is standing, even if de jure like sitting due to an excuse, or in supererogatory. So if one recites in bowing or prostration or sitting, it is not a substitute for standing, the obligation is not fulfilled by it, and it is prohibitively disliked because it changes what is legislated. And if he was forgetful, he must perform sajdah al-sahw. He said: (For His saying: 'Recite what is easy of the Quran') the aspect of evidence is that the command necessitates obligation, and recitation is not obligatory outside prayer by consensus, so the command is specified to prayer. And he said: 'No prayer except with recitation' narrated by Muslim from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and upon it consensus is formed, and no attention is paid to breaking consensus like Abu Bakr al-Asamm's statement that recitation in prayer is not obligatory at all but rather sunnah. He said: (And it is an additional pillar according to the majority) and al-Ghaznawi, author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, said it is fard but not a pillar. He said: 'Because it drops without necessity' he indicated by it the difference between an additional pillar and other than it, which is the basic pillar, for indeed it only drops in some situations due to necessity but to a successor, while the additional one drops without a successor. And he said in the Sharh: The additional is the part that if it is absent, the composite ruling remains according to the consideration of the Shari'ah. On this, if one swears not to pray, then enters ihram, stands, bows, and prostrates without recitation, he breaks his oath. Al-Sayyid said: It was objected that calling recitation an additional pillar is contradictory. And it was answered: It is a pillar with regard to the absence of the essence in a situation and additional in another, so from the perspective that the prayer is invalidated by leaving recitation when praying alone while able, it is a pillar, and from the perspective that the prayer of the follower is valid with leaving recitation, it is additional. He said: (And by text it was...) the text is the aforementioned verse because the intention is recitation of the Quran literally.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on Maraqi al-Falah critically refines the rulings on intention (niyyah), standing (qiyam), and recitation (qira'ah) in prayer, following the Hanafi school. The author begins by restating the matn: specification of intention is not required for supererogatory prayers (nafl), even for the sunnah of Fajr or Tarawih, according to the most correct view. The reason given is that the time itself designates the prayer, so a general intention suffices. However, precaution (ihtiyat) is to specify the intention to avoid disagreement with those who require it. The commentary then distinguishes between 'sunnah of the time' and other supererogatory prayers, noting that one should differentiate between before and after the obligatory prayer. Next, the passage discusses the pillar of standing (qiyam). It is an agreed-upon pillar in obligatory and wajib prayers. The minimum standing is defined as such that when one extends his hands, he does not reach his knees. For those unable to stand or prostrate, concessions apply. The text explains that the obligation of standing is linked to the ability to recite, and if recitation drops, the standing's duration is reduced. Standing on one foot is disliked unless excused. Finally, the passage addresses recitation (qira'ah) as an additional pillar. It is fard (obligatory) based on the Quranic command 'Recite what is easy' and the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation.' Recitation must be audible to oneself. It drops for the follower (muqtadi) and for one who catches the bowing (mudrik) by consensus. A verse of at least two words or a single word like 'Mudhammatan' suffices. The distinction between a basic pillar and an additional pillar is clarified: an additional pillar is one whose omission does not require repetition but may necessitate sajdah al-sahw, and it can drop without a substitute (la ila khalaf). The commentary also notes a difference with al-Ghaznawi who said recitation is fard but not a pillar, and with Abu Bakr al-Asamm who denied its obligation altogether—but these are not followed.

Key Terms
القراءة (al-qira'ah): Recitation of Quran in prayer; additional pillar
الركن الزائد (al-rukn al-za'id): Additional pillar that can drop without voiding the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on recitation for a person praying behind an imam?
A) He must recite al-Fatihah silently.
B) He must not recite; the imam's recitation suffices.
C) He may choose to recite or not.
D) He must recite if the imam is silent.

Key Takeaway
Recitation is an additional pillar: obligatory for the individual but drops for the follower; this distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation of Recitation: Proof and Classification
Proof and classification of recitation's obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and Hadith proofs for the obligation of recitation in prayer, explain why it is fard (not sunnah), and classify it as a rukn za'id (supernumerary pillar).

Core Idea
Recitation is fard, proven by Quran and Sunnah, but classified as a supernumerary pillar—essential for the individual but dropped for the follower.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling of recitation (qira'ah) in Hanafi fiqh. We will analyze the two primary proofs: the Quranic command 'faqra'ū mā tayassara' and the hadith 'lā ṣalāta illā bi qirā'ah.' Additionally, we will delve into the unique Hanafi concept of a supernumerary pillar (rukn zā'id), which explains why recitation is obligatory yet can be omitted without substitute in specific contexts, such as when following an imam.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Ruling and Its Proofs
Identify the statement 'al-qirā'atu farḍ' (recitation is obligatory) and note the two proofs cited: the Quranic verse (73:20) and the marfu' hadith from Muslim.
The proofs are both naqli (textual).
2
Analyze the Quranic Proof: 'faqra'ū'
Apply Hanafi usul: the imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). Since recitation is not wājib outside prayer by consensus (ijma'), the command is specifically for prayer. The phrase 'mā tayassara' (what is easy) indicates flexibility but not negation of obligation.
The verse is from Surah al-Muzzammil (73:20).
3
Analyze the Hadith Proof: 'Lā ṣalāta illā bi qirā'ah'
The negation (lā) with the indefinite noun (ṣalāta) indicates that prayer is invalid (bāṭil) without recitation. This hadith is sahih and supports the Quranic proof.
In Hanafi usul, ahad hadith is zanni al-thubut but is accepted for establishing obligation.
4
Understand the Classification as Rukn Zā'id
The text distinguishes between an original pillar (rukn asli) and a supernumerary pillar (rukn zā'id). An original pillar, if omitted, requires a substitute (e.g., sitting for ruku'). A supernumerary pillar can be dropped without substitute. Recitation is a pillar because its omission invalidates the prayer of one praying alone, but it is supernumerary because it is dropped for the follower (muqtadi) and for one who catches the rak'ah in bowing.
This classification is unique to the Hanafi school.
5
Dismiss the Dissenting Opinion of Abū Bakr al-Aṣamm
Al-Aṣamm claimed recitation is only sunnah. The text dismisses this as a breach of consensus (ijma'). Consensus is a strong authority, and the practice of the Muslims across generations confirms the obligation.
An outlier opinion does not affect the mainstream ruling.

The Book of Prayer. Related to standing (fi al-qiyam), so it is not obligatory in supererogatory prayer as we will mention, God willing. And recitation is obligatory. It is not considered recitation unless it is audible to the reciter, as previously stated, due to the Almighty's saying: 'So recite what is easy of the Qur'an.' It is a supernumerary pillar according to the majority because it is dropped without necessity from the follower according to us, and from the one who catches the bowing position by consensus. And by the text, recitation was obligatory. And if one recites a short verse composed of two words, like His saying... then he considered the apparent narration. As for a verse that is a single word like 'muddatan' or a letter like 'ṣ' or 'n' or 'q', or two letters like 'ḥā mīm'... His saying: 'And the obligations' apparently includes making up a supererogatory prayer that one has spoiled, and likewise a vowed prayer, even if it does not specify standing, according to one of two opinions. His saying: 'And the definition of standing' means the minimum of it, and its completion is by being upright like a cane; this quality induces humility in prayer, as mentioned by the knower of God, Sayyidī Aḥmad Zarūq in his advice. His saying: 'Related to standing'... His saying: 'As we will mention' is that its foundation is based on expansion. His saying: 'And it is not valid except by hearing it' except for an obstacle like deafness or loud noises or similar hindrances that prevent the correct sense of hearing. Al-Karkhī was satisfied with merely correcting the letters themselves because recitation is an act of the tongue while hearing is an act of the ear, not the tongue, so it is not a required element. Even if one does not hear it, recitation is valid. He said in al-Badā'i': The saying of al-Karkhī is more correct and more analogical, and some attribute it to Abū Yūsuf. The relied upon is the first opinion. And lowering one's voice with some letters such that he cannot hear himself is not invalidating of prayer according to the correct opinion due to general need, as in al-Mudmarāt from al-Dhakhīrah. Its place is standing, even if legally, like sitting due to an excuse, or in supererogatory prayer. So if one recites in bowing or prostration or sitting, it does not substitute for standing, the obligation is not fulfilled, and it is prohibitively disliked because it changes the legislated act. If it was done forgetfully, prostration of forgetfulness becomes obligatory. His saying: 'For His saying: So recite what is easy of the Qur'an. The indication is that the command necessitates obligation, and recitation is not obligatory outside prayer by consensus, so the command is specifically for prayer. And he said: There is no prayer except with recitation, reported by Muslim from the hadith of Abū Hurayra, and consensus was formed upon it. No attention is paid to one who breaks consensus like Abū Bakr al-Aṣamm, who said recitation in prayer is not obligatory at all, but only sunna.' His saying: 'And it is a supernumerary pillar according to the majority.' Al-Ghaznawī, author of al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī, said it is fard, not a pillar. His saying: 'Due to its being dropped without necessity' refers to the difference between the supernumerary pillar and the original one. The original one is only dropped in some circumstances due to necessity, but to a substitute, while the supernumerary is dropped without a substitute. And he said in the commentary: 'The supernumerary is the part which, if omitted, the composite ruling remains in consideration of the Lawgiver.' Based on this, if one swore not to pray and then entered the prayer, stood, bowed, and prostrated without recitation, he would break his oath. Al-Sayyid objected that calling recitation a supernumerary pillar is contradictory. The answer was that it is a pillar from the perspective that the reality of prayer is nullified without it in the case of one praying alone, but it is supernumerary from the perspective that the follower's prayer is valid without it. His saying: 'And by the text'... The text is the aforementioned verse because what is meant is the true recitation of the Qur'an. Or letters like ḥā mīm, 'ayn sīn qāf, kāf hā yā 'ayn ṣād. The scholars differed, and the correct opinion is that prayer is not valid with them. Al-Qudūrī said the correct is permissibility. Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad said the obligatory is a long verse or three short verses. Memorizing what suffices for prayer from the Qur'an is an individual obligation. Memorizing al-Fātiḥa and a sūra is wajib upon every Muslim. Memorizing the entire Qur'an is a collective obligation. When you know this, recitation is obligatory in two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer, meaning any two rak'ahs. It is not valid by reciting in only one rak'ah, contrary to Zufar and al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī, because the command does not necessitate repetition. We say yes, but it became necessary in the second because they are similar in every respect. So the first is by the wording of the text, and the second by its indication. And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer, because each pair is a separate prayer. And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of witr, as it is... Some commentators said what is meant by the verse is prayer due to context, but the first is more appropriate because taking the literal meaning is primary. His saying: 'And if one recites a verse...' Linguistically, 'āyah' is every sign. Technically, it is every sentence indicating a ruling of Allah's rulings, or every speech separated from what precedes and follows by a scriptural pause. His saying: 'In the apparent narration from the Imam, and in another narration from him, it is not limited to anything, rather the least that the name 'Qur'an' applies to suffices. Al-Qudūrī affirmed this. There is a third narration: three short verses or one long verse equivalent to them, which is the saying of the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad). Al-Khulāṣah and others made the first the relied upon. His saying: 'As for the verse that is a word'... Know that the Kufans count 'alif lām mīm' in its places, al-muṣ, kāf hā yā 'ayn ṣād, ṭā hā, ṭā sīn mīm, yā sīn, and ḥā mīm as one verse, and ḥā mīm 'ayn sīn qāf as two verses. Al-Bayḍāwī like al-Zamakhsharī said this specification has no room for opinion. As for non-Kufans, none of these are considered verses among them. His saying: 'Or a letter (ṣ)'... His saying: 'Or letters ḥā mīm 'ayn sīn qāf'... You already know that the Kufans count them as two verses. His saying: 'The scholars differed' means according to the saying of the Imam. His saying: 'And Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad said...' It was preferred in al-Asrār and caution is with their saying, and that is desirable especially in acts of worship. His saying: 'When you know that'... meaning the obligation of recitation and the disagreement, then recitation... i.e., know that it is only in two rak'ahs. His saying: 'In the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer' of two-, three-, or four-unit prayers. The place of performance is two unspecified rak'ahs as stated in the commentary. Al-Qahistānī said it is the saying of some, but the correct view is that the first two are specifically obligatory, such that if one omits them in the first two and performs them in the last two, it is a make-up (qaḍā') as in al-Tuḥfah. Ibn Amīr Ḥājj said it is the saying of the majority and the correct view, and it is the way in al-Dhakhīrah, Muḥīṭ Raḍī al-Dīn, and Qāḍīkhān in Sharḥ al-Jāmi' al-Ṣaghīr. His saying: 'Because they are similar in every respect' means the second rak'ah is like the first in obligation, dropping, loudness, and quietness. As for the last two, they differ from them in dropping in travel, quality of recitation, and its quantity, so they are not analogous to them. As for the difference between the first and second in regard to the takbīr of iḥrām, ta'awwudh, and thanā', it is not detrimental because similarity is only considered in what pertains to the prayer itself and its pillars. As for the takbīr, it is a condition and is supernumerary, and the ta'awwudh and thanā' are supernumerary.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah, addressing the ruling of recitation (qira'ah) in prayer. The commentator, al-Tahtawi, begins by affirming that recitation is fard (obligatory) in prayer, based on the Quranic command 'faqra'ū mā tayassara min al-Qur'an' (So recite what is easy of the Qur'an). He explains that the command indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul, and since recitation is not obligatory outside prayer by consensus, it must be specifically for prayer. The hadith 'La salata illa bi qira'ah' (No prayer without recitation) from Muslim further supports this, and consensus is claimed, dismissing the outlier opinion of Abu Bakr al-Asamm who considered it merely sunnah. The passage then delves into the nature of recitation as a 'supernumerary pillar' (rukn za'id): it is a pillar because omitting it invalidates prayer for one praying alone, but it is supernumerary because it is dropped without substitute for the follower (muqtadi) and for one who catches the rak'ah in bowing. This distinction is crucial for understanding why the follower's prayer is valid without recitation. The minimum recitation is discussed: the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) from Abu Hanifa is that a short verse of two words suffices, such as 'muddatan' in the Quran. There is a second narration that any amount qualifying as 'Qur'an' is enough, and a third from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad requiring a long verse or three short verses. Al-Tahtawi notes that caution leans toward the Sahibayn's view, especially in acts of worship. Recitation must be audible to the reciter (except for excuses like deafness), following the majority; al-Karkhi's view that merely moving the tongue suffices is deemed less reliable. Lowering the voice so that one cannot hear oneself is excused due to general need. Recitation must occur in the standing position (or its legal substitute like sitting for a valid excuse); reciting in bowing or prostration does not fulfill the obligation and is prohibitively disliked. In obligatory (fard) prayers, recitation is fard only in two rak'ahs—specifically the first two according to the correct view—while in supererogatory (nafl) prayers it is required in every rak'ah because each pair is a separate prayer, and similarly in witr. The passage concludes by clarifying that the two rak'ahs of recitation must be the first two; if one recites only in the last two, it counts as a make-up (qada'), and the recitation in the second rak'ah is established by the indication of the text (dalalah) due to the similarity between the first two rak'ahs. Al-Tahtawi draws on earlier authorities like al-Quduri, al-Karkhi, al-Bada'i', al-Dhakhirah, and later works like al-Tuḥfah to support his commentary.

Key Terms
قراءة (qirā'ah): Recitation of Quranic verses during prayer, which is fard (obligatory) in specific rak'ahs and positions.
ركن زائد (rukn zā'id): A supernumerary pillar: an integral part of prayer that can be omitted without substitute in specific circumstances (e.g., recitation for the follower), but its omission invalidates the prayer for one praying alone.
الفرض (al-farḍ): An obligatory act whose omission invalidates the prayer if done intentionally; derived from a qat'i (definitive) proof. Here, recitation is farḍ in the first two rak'ahs of farḍ prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the relied-upon ruling on recitation in prayer?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
B) It is fard (obligatory) and a supernumerary pillar.
C) It is wajib (obligatory) but not a pillar.
D) It is recommended but not required.

Key Takeaway
Recitation in prayer is fard (obligatory) based on Quran and Sunnah, and its classification as a supernumerary pillar explains why it is dropped for the follower but not for one praying alone.
