Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Minimum Recitation: Quantity and Location in Prayer
Minimum quantity of recitation and its required location in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum quantity of recitation that fulfills the obligation according to the Hanafi school, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue, and identify which rak'ahs require recitation in fard, nafl, and witr prayers.

Core Idea
The minimum recitation is a short verse of two words, but the Sahibayn require more; recitation is fard in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.

Having established the obligation of recitation, this lesson tackles two practical questions: how much Quran must one recite to fulfill the obligation, and in which rak'ahs must it be recited? The passage presents three narrations from Abu Hanifa and the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on the minimum quantity. It also clarifies that recitation is fard specifically in two rak'ahs of fard prayer—the first two according to the correct view—and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Narration's on Minimum Recitation
The passage mentions (1) a short verse of two words (e.g., 'muddatan'), (2) any amount that qualifies as Quran (even one letter), and (3) a long verse or three short verses (the view of Sahibayn). The relied-upon view is the first.
There is also a discussion on single letters like 'ṣ' or two letters like 'ḥā mīm'.
2
Understand the Dispute Between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa's apparent narration is that a short verse of two words suffices. The Sahibayn argue that a meaningful portion requires a long verse or three short verses. Al-Tahtawi notes that caution leans toward the Sahibayn's view, especially in acts of worship.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Determine Which Rak'ahs Require Recitation in Fard Prayer
The passage states recitation is fard in 'two rak'ahs of the fard prayer'. There is an internal dispute: some say any two unspecified rak'ahs suffice, but the correct view (mufta bihi) is that the first two rak'ahs are specifically obligatory. If one recites only in the last two, it counts as qada' (make-up).
The second rak'ah's obligation is derived by analogy (tashakul) to the first.
4
Apply the Ruling to Nafl and Witr Prayers
The passage explicitly says recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafl (supererogatory) prayer, because each pair (shaf') is a separate prayer. Similarly, it is fard in all rak'ahs of witr.
For nafl, the obligation is stronger per rak'ah compared to fard where only two rak'ahs are required.
5
Recall the Conditions of Recitation: Place and Audibility
Recitation must be performed in the standing position (qiyam) or its legal substitute (e.g., sitting due to excuse). Reciting in ruku' or sujud does not fulfill the obligation and is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi), requiring sajdah al-sahw if done forgetfully. Audibility to oneself is required except for excuses like deafness or noise.
The condition of hearing oneself is linked to the validity of the act of recitation.

The Book of Prayer. Related to standing (fi al-qiyam), so it is not obligatory in supererogatory prayer as we will mention, God willing. And recitation is obligatory. It is not considered recitation unless it is audible to the reciter, as previously stated, due to the Almighty's saying: 'So recite what is easy of the Qur'an.' It is a supernumerary pillar according to the majority because it is dropped without necessity from the follower according to us, and from the one who catches the bowing position by consensus. And by the text, recitation was obligatory. And if one recites a short verse composed of two words, like His saying... then he considered the apparent narration. As for a verse that is a single word like 'muddatan' or a letter like 'ṣ' or 'n' or 'q', or two letters like 'ḥā mīm'... His saying: 'And the obligations' apparently includes making up a supererogatory prayer that one has spoiled, and likewise a vowed prayer, even if it does not specify standing, according to one of two opinions. His saying: 'And the definition of standing' means the minimum of it, and its completion is by being upright like a cane; this quality induces humility in prayer, as mentioned by the knower of God, Sayyidī Aḥmad Zarūq in his advice. His saying: 'Related to standing'... His saying: 'As we will mention' is that its foundation is based on expansion. His saying: 'And it is not valid except by hearing it' except for an obstacle like deafness or loud noises or similar hindrances that prevent the correct sense of hearing. Al-Karkhī was satisfied with merely correcting the letters themselves because recitation is an act of the tongue while hearing is an act of the ear, not the tongue, so it is not a required element. Even if one does not hear it, recitation is valid. He said in al-Badā'i': The saying of al-Karkhī is more correct and more analogical, and some attribute it to Abū Yūsuf. The relied upon is the first opinion. And lowering one's voice with some letters such that he cannot hear himself is not invalidating of prayer according to the correct opinion due to general need, as in al-Mudmarāt from al-Dhakhīrah. Its place is standing, even if legally, like sitting due to an excuse, or in supererogatory prayer. So if one recites in bowing or prostration or sitting, it does not substitute for standing, the obligation is not fulfilled, and it is prohibitively disliked because it changes the legislated act. If it was done forgetfully, prostration of forgetfulness becomes obligatory. His saying: 'For His saying: So recite what is easy of the Qur'an. The indication is that the command necessitates obligation, and recitation is not obligatory outside prayer by consensus, so the command is specifically for prayer. And he said: There is no prayer except with recitation, reported by Muslim from the hadith of Abū Hurayra, and consensus was formed upon it. No attention is paid to one who breaks consensus like Abū Bakr al-Aṣamm, who said recitation in prayer is not obligatory at all, but only sunna.' His saying: 'And it is a supernumerary pillar according to the majority.' Al-Ghaznawī, author of al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī, said it is fard, not a pillar. His saying: 'Due to its being dropped without necessity' refers to the difference between the supernumerary pillar and the original one. The original one is only dropped in some circumstances due to necessity, but to a substitute, while the supernumerary is dropped without a substitute. And he said in the commentary: 'The supernumerary is the part which, if omitted, the composite ruling remains in consideration of the Lawgiver.' Based on this, if one swore not to pray and then entered the prayer, stood, bowed, and prostrated without recitation, he would break his oath. Al-Sayyid objected that calling recitation a supernumerary pillar is contradictory. The answer was that it is a pillar from the perspective that the reality of prayer is nullified without it in the case of one praying alone, but it is supernumerary from the perspective that the follower's prayer is valid without it. His saying: 'And by the text'... The text is the aforementioned verse because what is meant is the true recitation of the Qur'an. Or letters like ḥā mīm, 'ayn sīn qāf, kāf hā yā 'ayn ṣād. The scholars differed, and the correct opinion is that prayer is not valid with them. Al-Qudūrī said the correct is permissibility. Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad said the obligatory is a long verse or three short verses. Memorizing what suffices for prayer from the Qur'an is an individual obligation. Memorizing al-Fātiḥa and a sūra is wajib upon every Muslim. Memorizing the entire Qur'an is a collective obligation. When you know this, recitation is obligatory in two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer, meaning any two rak'ahs. It is not valid by reciting in only one rak'ah, contrary to Zufar and al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī, because the command does not necessitate repetition. We say yes, but it became necessary in the second because they are similar in every respect. So the first is by the wording of the text, and the second by its indication. And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer, because each pair is a separate prayer. And recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of witr, as it is... Some commentators said what is meant by the verse is prayer due to context, but the first is more appropriate because taking the literal meaning is primary. His saying: 'And if one recites a verse...' Linguistically, 'āyah' is every sign. Technically, it is every sentence indicating a ruling of Allah's rulings, or every speech separated from what precedes and follows by a scriptural pause. His saying: 'In the apparent narration from the Imam, and in another narration from him, it is not limited to anything, rather the least that the name 'Qur'an' applies to suffices. Al-Qudūrī affirmed this. There is a third narration: three short verses or one long verse equivalent to them, which is the saying of the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad). Al-Khulāṣah and others made the first the relied upon. His saying: 'As for the verse that is a word'... Know that the Kufans count 'alif lām mīm' in its places, al-muṣ, kāf hā yā 'ayn ṣād, ṭā hā, ṭā sīn mīm, yā sīn, and ḥā mīm as one verse, and ḥā mīm 'ayn sīn qāf as two verses. Al-Bayḍāwī like al-Zamakhsharī said this specification has no room for opinion. As for non-Kufans, none of these are considered verses among them. His saying: 'Or a letter (ṣ)'... His saying: 'Or letters ḥā mīm 'ayn sīn qāf'... You already know that the Kufans count them as two verses. His saying: 'The scholars differed' means according to the saying of the Imam. His saying: 'And Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad said...' It was preferred in al-Asrār and caution is with their saying, and that is desirable especially in acts of worship. His saying: 'When you know that'... meaning the obligation of recitation and the disagreement, then recitation... i.e., know that it is only in two rak'ahs. His saying: 'In the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer' of two-, three-, or four-unit prayers. The place of performance is two unspecified rak'ahs as stated in the commentary. Al-Qahistānī said it is the saying of some, but the correct view is that the first two are specifically obligatory, such that if one omits them in the first two and performs them in the last two, it is a make-up (qaḍā') as in al-Tuḥfah. Ibn Amīr Ḥājj said it is the saying of the majority and the correct view, and it is the way in al-Dhakhīrah, Muḥīṭ Raḍī al-Dīn, and Qāḍīkhān in Sharḥ al-Jāmi' al-Ṣaghīr. His saying: 'Because they are similar in every respect' means the second rak'ah is like the first in obligation, dropping, loudness, and quietness. As for the last two, they differ from them in dropping in travel, quality of recitation, and its quantity, so they are not analogous to them. As for the difference between the first and second in regard to the takbīr of iḥrām, ta'awwudh, and thanā', it is not detrimental because similarity is only considered in what pertains to the prayer itself and its pillars. As for the takbīr, it is a condition and is supernumerary, and the ta'awwudh and thanā' are supernumerary.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on Maraqi al-Falah, addressing the ruling of recitation (qira'ah) in prayer. The commentator, al-Tahtawi, begins by affirming that recitation is fard (obligatory) in prayer, based on the Quranic command 'faqra'ū mā tayassara min al-Qur'an' (So recite what is easy of the Qur'an). He explains that the command indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul, and since recitation is not obligatory outside prayer by consensus, it must be specifically for prayer. The hadith 'La salata illa bi qira'ah' (No prayer without recitation) from Muslim further supports this, and consensus is claimed, dismissing the outlier opinion of Abu Bakr al-Asamm who considered it merely sunnah. The passage then delves into the nature of recitation as a 'supernumerary pillar' (rukn za'id): it is a pillar because omitting it invalidates prayer for one praying alone, but it is supernumerary because it is dropped without substitute for the follower (muqtadi) and for one who catches the rak'ah in bowing. This distinction is crucial for understanding why the follower's prayer is valid without recitation. The minimum recitation is discussed: the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) from Abu Hanifa is that a short verse of two words suffices, such as 'muddatan' in the Quran. There is a second narration that any amount qualifying as 'Qur'an' is enough, and a third from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad requiring a long verse or three short verses. Al-Tahtawi notes that caution leans toward the Sahibayn's view, especially in acts of worship. Recitation must be audible to the reciter (except for excuses like deafness), following the majority; al-Karkhi's view that merely moving the tongue suffices is deemed less reliable. Lowering the voice so that one cannot hear oneself is excused due to general need. Recitation must occur in the standing position (or its legal substitute like sitting for a valid excuse); reciting in bowing or prostration does not fulfill the obligation and is prohibitively disliked. In obligatory (fard) prayers, recitation is fard only in two rak'ahs—specifically the first two according to the correct view—while in supererogatory (nafl) prayers it is required in every rak'ah because each pair is a separate prayer, and similarly in witr. The passage concludes by clarifying that the two rak'ahs of recitation must be the first two; if one recites only in the last two, it counts as a make-up (qada'), and the recitation in the second rak'ah is established by the indication of the text (dalalah) due to the similarity between the first two rak'ahs. Al-Tahtawi draws on earlier authorities like al-Quduri, al-Karkhi, al-Bada'i', al-Dhakhirah, and later works like al-Tuḥfah to support his commentary.

Key Terms
أقل القراءة (aqall al-qirā'ah): The minimum amount of Quranic recitation that satisfies the obligation in prayer. According to the mufta bihi, it is a short verse of at least two words.
التشاكل (al-tashākul): Similarity between two entities such that rules apply to both. Here, the second rak'ah is analogous to the first, thus it also requires recitation.
قضاء (qaḍā'): A make-up or compensatory performance. Here, if one recites only in the last two rak'ahs, it is considered a make-up (qada') for the omission in the first two, not a fulfillment of the original obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, what is the minimum recitation that fulfills the obligation in prayer?
A) Any amount that qualifies as Quran, even one letter.
B) A short verse of at least two words.
C) Three short verses or one long verse.
D) Al-Fatihah in its entirety.

Key Takeaway
The minimum recitation in fard prayer is a two-word verse, but caution recommends more; recitation must be in the first two rak'ahs of fard and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.

Definition of an Ayah and Ruling on Disconnected Letters in Prayer
Definition of ayah and ruling on huruf muqatta'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of an ayah and apply the ruling on reciting disconnected letters in prayer, distinguishing between the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
An ayah is a tawqifi unit of revelation; reciting only disconnected letters invalidates prayer according to the most correct Hanafi position.

This lesson examines the Hanafi definition of an 'ayah' and its impact on the validity of prayer. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies that an ayah is not merely any Quranic word but a divinely ordained segment. This directly affects whether reciting the opening letters (huruf muqatta'ah) fulfills the obligatory recitation in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Define 'ayah' linguistically and terminologically
Identify the two definitions: linguistic (sign) and terminological (a sentence conveying a divine ruling or a tawqifi speech segment). Understand that the terminological definition is preferred for fiqh rulings.
The hashiah states: 'وعرفاً كل جملة دالة على حكم من أحكام الله تعالى أو كل كلام منفصل عما قبله وبعده بفصل توقيفي لفظي'.
2
Identify the minimum quantity for a valid ayah according to the Hanafi school
Note the three positions: Abu Hanifa (any amount suffices), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (one long verse or three short verses), and a third narration (three short verses or one long verse). Recognize that the mufta bihi is the precautionary view of the Sahibayn.
The apparent narration from Abu Hanifa does not specify a quantity, but the preferred view requires a substantial segment.
3
Analyze the dispute over disconnected letters (huruf muqatta'ah)
Understand that the Kufan school (including Hanafis) counts certain disconnected letters as verses, while non-Kufans do not. The asahh view is that prayer is not valid if only these letters are recited, though al-Quduri permitted it.
The hashiah states: 'فقد اختلف المشايخ والأصح أنه لا تجوز بها الصلاة'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for prayer recitation
Conclude that for obligatory recitation, one should recite a long verse or three short verses to be safe (ihtiyat). The prayer is invalid if only disconnected letters are recited, according to the most correct view.
Al-Asrar prefers the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, especially in worship.

وقال بعض المفسرين : المراد من الآية الصلاة بدليل السياق والأوّل أولى لأن الحمل على الحقيقة أولى قوله : ( ولو قرأ آية هي لغة العلامة ،وعرفاً كل جملة دالة على حكم من أحكام الله تعالى أو كل كلام منفصل عما قبله وبعده بفصل توقيفي لفظي اهـ. قوله: (في ظاهر الرواية عن الإمام وفي رواية أخرى عنه هو غير مقدر بشيء، بل يكفي أدنى ما يتناوله إسم القرآن، وبه جزم القدوري، وعنه رواية ثالثة أنه ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة تعد لها وهو قولهما، وجعله في الخلاصة، وغيرها قوله الأول اهـ. قوله : (وأما الآية التي هي . كلمة) أعلم أن الكوفيين عذراً ألم في مواضعها والمص وكهيعص وطه وطسم ويس، وحم آية وحم عسق آيتين قال البيضاوي كالزمخشري وهذا التوقيف لا مجال للرأي فيه وأما غير الكوفيين، فليس شيء منها عندهم بآية. قوله : (أو حرف (ص) هو وما بعده على حذف كاف التمثيل. قوله : (أو حروف حم عسق) قد علمت أن الكوفيين عدوها آيتين قوله : (فقد اختلف المشايخ) أي على قول الإمام قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد الخ ) رجحه في الأسرار والإحتياط قولهما، وهو مطلوب لا سيما في العبادات
Or the letters Ha Mim 'Ayn Sin Qaf, Kaf Ha Ya 'Ayn Sad: the mashayikh differed, and the most correct is that prayer is not valid with them. Al-Quduri said: the correct view is permissibility. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: the obligatory recitation is a long verse or three short verses. Memorizing what makes prayer valid from the Quran is fard 'ayn, and memorizing al-Fatihah and a surah is wajib on every Muslim, and memorizing the entire Quran is fard kifayah. 

Some commentators said: what is meant by 'the verse' is prayer by context; but the first is better because taking the literal meaning is preferable. He said: (and if one recites a verse) linguistically it is a sign, and terminologically every sentence that conveys a ruling of Allah, or every speech that is separated from what is before and after by a tawqifi verbal division. He said: in the apparent narration from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is not defined by any quantity, but the least that the name Quran applies to suffices, and al-Quduri asserted this. There is a third narration: three short verses or one long verse counted as such, which is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement. He said: (as for the verse that is a word) know that the Kufans count Alif Lam Mim in its places, and Alif Lam Mim Sad, Kaf Ha Ya 'Ayn Sad, Ta Ha, Ta Sin Mim, Ya Sin, and Ha Mim as one verse, and Ha Mim 'Ayn Sin Qaf as two verses. Al-Baydawi like al-Zamakhshari said: this tawqif (stopping) has no room for opinion. As for non-Kufans, none of these count as verses. He said: (or a letter) (Sad) and what follows omit the letter of comparison Kaf. He said: (or the letters Ha Mim 'Ayn Sin Qaf) you know the Kufans counted them as two verses. He said: (the mashayikh differed) i.e. on the Imam's statement. He said: (and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said) the preference in al-Asrar is for precaution (ihtiyat) with their statement, and this is desirable especially in acts of worship.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling from the hashiah. It discusses the ruling on reciting the disconnected letters (huruf al-muqatta'ah) that appear at the beginning of some Quranic surahs during prayer. The author first states the matn: there is disagreement among the senior scholars (mashayikh) about whether prayer is valid if one recites these letters. The most authoritative position (al-asahh) is that it is not valid. However, al-Quduri reports that the correct view is permissibility. Then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the obligatory recitation in prayer can be fulfilled by a long verse or three short verses. The hashiah then defines what an 'ayah' is: linguistically a sign, terminologically a sentence that conveys a divine ruling or speech that is separated by a tawqifi division (meaning the division is divinely ordained, not by human convention). It also notes that according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) from Imam Abu Hanifa, the minimum quantity for an ayah is not defined; any amount that qualifies as Quran suffices. But there is another narration requiring three short verses or one long verse (which is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The Kufan school counts certain isolated letters as verses (e.g., Alif Lam Mim is one verse), whereas non-Kufans do not count them as verses. The hashiah then reports that the preference in al-Asrar is for ihtiyat (precaution) by adopting Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's view, especially in acts of worship. This lesson emphasizes that the definition of an ayah directly impacts the validity of prayer recitation in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
آية (āyah): A sentence conveying a ruling of Allah or speech separated by a tawqifi (divinely ordained) division; the minimum for valid recitation in prayer.
حروف مقطعة (ḥurūf muqaṭṭa‘ah): Disconnected letters that appear at the beginning of some Quranic surahs, such as Alif Lam Mim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct (asahh) view in this passage, what is the ruling on praying while reciting only disconnected letters like 'Alif Lam Mim'?
A) It is permissible and valid.
B) It is not valid.
C) It is recommended.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
An ayah is a tawqifi unit, and reciting only disconnected letters does not fulfill the obligation of Quran recitation in prayer according to the most correct Hanafi view.

Obligation of Recitation in Fard, Nafl, and Witr Prayers
Specifies obligation of qira'ah per prayer type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of rak'ahs requiring recitation in fard, nafl, and witr prayers according to the Hanafi school, and explain the reasoning based on tashakul and precaution.

Core Idea
Recitation is obligatory in only two rak'ahs of fard (the first two), all rak'ahs of nafl, and all rak'ahs of witr for precaution.

This passage from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies a key fiqh ruling: the number of rak'ahs in which Quranic recitation (qira'ah) is fard varies by prayer type. You will learn the precise ruling for fard, nafl, and witr prayers, along with the internal Hanafi debate about which two rak'ahs are meant in fard and how precaution resolves the difference over witr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling for recitation in fard? It is fard (obligatory) in two rak'ahs.
The passage specifies 'in two rak'ahs of the fard prayer'.
2
Locate the dalil
What Quranic verse is cited? The imperative 'اقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن' (Quran 73:20) is used as evidence.
The verse commands recitation of what is easy from the Quran.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the obligation? The imperative indicates wujub in Hanafi usul; the phrase 'what is easy' shows no specific amount is mandated, thereby allowing any portion of the Quran to fulfill the fard.
The verse does not specify a number of rak'ahs, so the number is derived from other evidence (tashakul).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Who disagrees on the number of rak'ahs? Zufar and al-Hasan al-Basri say one rak'ah suffices. The Hanafi response uses tashakul (complete similarity between the first two rak'ahs) to require repetition.
The first two rak'ahs are similar in obligation, travel concession, and loud/soft recitation; the last two differ.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which view is mufta bihi? The correct view is that the first two rak'ahs are specified as fard, as stated by al-Qahistani, Ibn Amir Haj, and adopted in major Hanafi texts.
If one recites only in the last two, it is considered qada (make-up).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا علمت ذلك فالقراءة فرض (في ركعتي الفرض) أي ركعتين كانتا ولا تصح بقراءته في ركعة واحدة فقط خلافاً لزفر والحسن البصري لأن لأمر لا يقتضي التكرار قلنا نعم لكن لزمت في الثانية لتشاكلهما من كل وجه فالأولى بعبارة النص، والثانية بدلالته (و) القراءة فرض في (كل) ركعات (النفل) لأن كل شفع منه صلاة على حدة (و) القراءة فرض في كل ركعات (الوتر) أما على كونه

قوله : (وإذا علمت ذلك أي افتراض القراءة، والخلاف فالقراءة الخ أي فاعلم أن ذلك إنما هو في ركعتين قوله : في ركعتي الفرض الثنائي، والثلاثي، والرباعي، ومحل الأداء ركعتان غير متعينتين كما قاله الشرح قال القهستاني : هو قول البعض، والصحيح أن الأوليين متعينتان على سبيل الفرض حتى لو تركها في الأوليين وأتى بها في الأخيرتين كان قضاء كما في التحفة، وقال ابن أمير حاج : وهو قول الجمهور، وهو الصحيح وعليه مشى في الذخيرة ومحيط رضي الدين وقاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير . قوله : لتشاكلهما من كل وجه) فإن الثانية مثل الأولى وجوباً، وسقوطاً وجهراً وإخفاء وأما الأخريان فيفارقانهما في حق السقوط بالسفر، وصفة القراءة، وقدرها فلا يلحقان بهما، وأما إفتراق الأولى والثانية في حق تكبيرة الأحرام والتعوّذ والثناء فليس بقادح لأن المشاكلة إنما تعتبر فيما يرجع إلى نفس الصلاة، وأركانها أما التكبيرة فشرط وهو زائد، والتعوذ والثناء زائدان

سنة فظاهر وعلى وجوبه للاحتياط ولم يتعين شيء من القرآن لصحة الصلاة) لإطلاق ما تلونا وقلنا بتعيين الفاتحة وجوباً كما سنذكره

قوله : ( في كل ركعات النفل) المراد به ما زاد على الفرائض، ولو كان مؤكداً. قوله : (صلاة على حدة) لتمكنه من الخروج على رأس الركعتين لأن الأصل في مشروعية الصلاة مثنى، ولزوم الزيادة إنما يظهر في الفرائض فيبقى النفل على أصل المشروعية. قوله : ( وعلى وجوبه) أي أو فرضيته كذا في الشرح قوله: (للإحتياط) لأن كونه فرضاً عملاً كما هو قول الإمام يوجب القراءة في الأوليين فقط، وكونه سنة مؤكدة كما هو قولهما يوجبها في الجميع فعملنا بالإحتياط لأنّ ترك القراءة في ركعة من السنة يفسدها ولأن يؤدي المكلف ما ليس عليه أولى من تركه ما عليه ذكره ابن أمير حاج . قوله: (لإطلاق ما تلونا) وهو الآية السابقة فإن المأمور به قراءة ما تيسر والتعين ينفي التيسر قوله: (كما سنذكره) من قوله : الا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب ولا تجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب لأنه خبر يثبت الوجوب دون الركنية
And when you know that, then recitation is fard in two rak'ahs of the fard prayer, meaning in any two rak'ahs, and it is not valid by reciting in only one rak'ah, contrary to Zufar and al-Hasan al-Basri, because the command does not necessitate repetition. We say: yes, but it becomes necessary in the second because of their complete similarity, so the first is by explicit text, the second by implication. And recitation is fard in all rak'ahs of nafl, because each pair (shaf') is a separate prayer. And recitation is fard in all rak'ahs of witr, based on its being...

He said: (And when you know that) i.e. the obligation of recitation and the difference, then recitation... i.e. know that it is in two rak'ahs. He said: in the two rak'ahs of fard for two-rak'ah, three-rak'ah, and four-rak'ah prayers, and the place of performance is two unspecified rak'ahs as al-Sharh said. Al-Qahistani said: that is the view of some, and the correct view is that the first two are specified as fard, such that if one recites in the last two instead, it is considered qada (make-up). Ibn Amir Haj said: that is the view of the majority and it is correct, and it is followed in al-Dhakhirah, Muhit Radi al-Din, and Qadikhan in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. He said: (because of their complete similarity) for the second resembles the first in obligation, dropping (in travel), loudness, and softness. As for the last two, they differ in dropping due to travel, quality of recitation, and quantity, so they are not analogous. The difference between the first and second regarding takbirat al-ihram, ta'awwudh, and thana' is not harmful because similarity is considered only in matters pertaining to the prayer itself and its pillars; takbir is a condition and extra, ta'awwudh and thana' are extra.

...it is apparent, and on its obligation for precaution, and nothing specific from the Quran is required for the validity of the prayer, due to the generality of what we recited. And we say that al-Fatihah is designated as wajib, as we will mention later.

He said: (in all rak'ahs of nafl) meaning what is in addition to the fara'id, even if it is mu'akkad. He said: (a separate prayer) because one can exit after two rak'ahs, since the original pattern for prayer is pairs, and the necessity of increase appears only in fard prayers; nafl remains on the original pattern. He said: (and on its obligation) i.e. its fardiyyah. He said: (for precaution) because considering it as fard (as is the Imam's view) necessitates recitation only in the first two, and considering it as sunnah mu'akkadah (as is their view) necessitates recitation in all; so we follow precaution because omitting recitation in a rak'ah of sunnah invalidates it, and it is better for the mukallaf to do what is not required of him than to omit what is required. He said: (due to the generality of what we recited) which is the previous verse, for what is commanded is recitation of what is easy, and specification negates ease. He said: (as we will mention) from his statement: 'There is no prayer except with the Fatihah of the Book' and it is not valid to add something from the Book, because this hadith establishes obligation without integral nature (rukn).
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof that explains the obligation of Quranic recitation in different prayer types. The matn states: recitation is fard in two rak'ahs of fard prayer (any two rak'ahs, but the hashiah clarifies that the correct view is the first two are specified), in every rak'ah of nafl, and in every rak'ah of witr. The hashiah then comments in detail. 

First, it rejects the view of Zufar and al-Hasan al-Basri that recitation is fard in only one rak'ah, because the command does not imply repetition. The Hanafi response is that repetition is required due to the complete similarity (tashakul) between the first two rak'ahs; the first is mandated by explicit text, the second by implication. 

Then there is an internal Hanafi dispute: some say any two rak'ahs suffice, but the correct (sahih) view per al-Qahistani and Ibn Amir Haj (and adopted by major texts) is that the first two are specified as fard. If one recites only in the last two, it is considered qada (make-up). The reason for specifying the first two is that they are similar in obligation, dropping in travel, and manner of recitation (loud/soft), unlike the last two which differ in dropping, quality, and quantity. 

For nafl, recitation is fard in every rak'ah because each pair (shaf') is an independent prayer; one can exit after two rak'ahs. The original pattern of prayer is two-by-two, and the obligation of adding more only applies to fard. 

For witr, there is a difference: some consider it fard (Abu Hanifa's view) and some consider it sunnah mu'akkadah (the Sahibayn). The hashiah says we follow precaution (ihtiyat) by reciting in all rak'ahs. If we consider it fard, recitation is only in the first two; if sunnah, in all. Precaution dictates reciting in all to avoid missing anything. The proof is the general command to recite 'what is easy' (from Quran 73:20), but the hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatihah' indicates that al-Fatihah is wajib (not fard). Therefore, no specific verse is required for validity, but al-Fatihah is obligatory.

Key Terms
ركعتا الفرض (rak‘atā al-farḍ): The two obligatory rak'ahs in which recitation (qira'ah) is fard; the correct view specifies the first two.
تشاكلهما (tashākuluhumā): Complete similarity between the first two rak'ahs in all aspects (obligation, dropping in travel, loud/soft recitation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah fard prayer, according to the correct Hanafi view, in which rak'ahs is recitation obligatory?
A) All four rak'ahs.
B) The first two rak'ahs only.
C) The last two rak'ahs only.
D) Any two rak'ahs, unspecified.

Key Takeaway
Recitation is fard in the first two rak'ahs of every fard prayer, and in every rak'ah of nafl and witr.

Ruling on Follower’s Recitation Behind the Imam
Prohibits follower recitation with proofs and internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower’s recitation behind the imam, identify the Quranic proof, and explain the internal Hanafi dispute and the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The follower must not recite behind the imam; recitation is makruh tahriman, and the imam’s recitation suffices.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a critical issue in congregational prayer: may the follower (muqtadi) recite Qur’an behind the imam? Drawing on the Quranic command to listen and be silent, the Hanafi school establishes a clear ruling that prohibits such recitation. However, there is an internal disagreement among the early Hanafi authorities. This lesson unpacks the proof, the dispute, and the final relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its reason
The passage begins with the ruling: the follower does not recite. Note the two scenarios: loud (jahr) and silent (sirr) recitation by the imam. Explain that the follower must listen during loud recitation and be silent during quiet recitation.
2
Examine the primary proof
The Quranic verse (7:204) is cited. Analyze how it commands listening (istima‘) and silence (insat) when the Quran is recited. Understand why the Hanafis interpret this as proof for the follower's obligation to refrain from recitation.
The verse: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent.'
3
Note the agreement of early scholars
The passage mentions agreement among Abu Hanifa, his companions, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad that the follower's prayer is valid without recitation. This consensus strengthens the Hanafi position.
4
Explore the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf (makruh in all prayers) and Muhammad al-Shaybani (initially recommended in silent prayers). The hashiah reports that Muhammad later retracted, as seen in his books and the practice of 'Alqamah ibn Qays.
Key source: al-Kamal ibn al-Humam's rejection of Muhammad's initial view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that recitation is makruh tahriman in all prayers. Precaution (ihtiyat) is to abstain entirely. Some early authorities said it invalidates prayer, but the mufta bihi is that the prayer remains valid but sinful.

And the follower (muqtadi) does not recite, rather he listens when the imam recites aloud, and remains silent when the imam recites quietly, due to the saying of Allah: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent.' And it is said: the recitation of the imam suffices for you, whether he recites aloud or softly. Then al-Kamal rejected this, saying: what is narrated from Muhammad that he recommended it by precaution is weak; the truth is that Muhammad's statement is like theirs. Muhammad in his books is against recitation behind the imam, after he attributed to 'Alqamah ibn Qays that he never recited. He said: and we adopt this; we do not see recitation behind the imam in any loud prayer. And al-Sarkhasi said: his prayer is invalidated by recitation according to several Companions. And it is said in al-Kafi: prohibiting the follower from recitation is transmitted from eighty senior Companions including al-Murtada and the 'Abadilah (Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn Mas'ud). The hadith scholars have compiled their names. Then al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam said: it is not hidden that precaution is in NOT reciting behind the imam, because precaution is to act on the stronger of two proofs, and the implication of their statements is not recitation, rather prohibition. And it would entail invalidation of prayer by someone who is many degrees better than a mujtahid who said so, and precaution cannot be taken in a way that necessitates...
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof covering the recitation of the follower (muqtadi) behind the imam. The matn states: the follower does not recite; he listens when the imam recites aloud and remains silent when the imam recites quietly, based on the Quranic verse (7:204). The Hanafi school, along with Malik and Ahmad, agree that the follower's prayer is valid without any recitation. If the follower does recite, it is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked). The hashiah then elaborates on the internal Hanafi dispute regarding the follower's recitation. 

There is a difference among the Hanafi imams: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, recitation behind the imam is makruh in both loud and quiet prayers. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, in loud prayers it is makruh, but in quiet prayers it is mustahabb (recommended) as a precaution, based on a narration from him. However, the author of the hashiah (al-Tahtawi) reports that al-Kamal ibn al-Humam rejected this narration, stating that Muhammad's final position is the same as the two (i.e., makruh), as evidenced by his books and his reliance on the practice of 'Alqamah ibn Qays. The hashiah also cites al-Sarkhasi that recitation invalidates the prayer, and al-Kafi that prohibition is from eighty Companions. Ibn al-Humam concludes that the stronger proof is for not reciting, and that precaution (ihtiyat) is to abstain. Therefore, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the follower does not recite in any prayer, whether loud or quiet; if he does, it is makruh tahriman, and according to some, the prayer may be invalidated.

Key Terms
مؤتم (mu‘tamm): The follower in congregational prayer who is led by the imam.
إنصات (inṣāt): Silent listening, specifically when the imam recites quietly, as opposed to istimā‘ (listening when recitation is loud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is wajib (obligatory).
D) It is haram and invalidates prayer.

Key Takeaway
The follower must listen silently and refrain from recitation; doing so is makruh tahriman, but the prayer remains valid.

The Ma'mum Must Listen, Not Recite Behind the Imam
States ruling and proofs for ma'mum's silence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the ma'mum's recitation, identify the Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain why the Shafi'i objection is rejected.

Core Idea
The ma'mum must listen and be silent; reciting behind the Imam is makruh tahrimi.

In congregational prayer, the ma'mum follows the Imam. A key question is whether the ma'mum must recite al-Fatihah or remain silent. The Hanafi school, based on clear textual proofs, holds that the ma'mum should not recite at all—neither aloud nor silently—and that doing so is prohibitively disliked. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the school’s response to opposing views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the ma'mum reciting any part of the Quran (including al-Fatihah) behind the Imam. The ruling: makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
Makruh tahrimi means sinful but not as severe as haram.
2
Locate the primary dalil from the Quran
The author cites Qur'an 7:204: 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent.' This is taken as a general command applicable even in prayer.
The verse is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala regarding its application in prayer.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet said: 'Let none of you recite when I recite aloud.' This directly prohibits recitation behind the Imam.
This hadith specifies the general command of the Quran.
4
Note the consensus and intra-Hanafi variations
The author mentions consensus of Abu Hanifa, his companions (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), Malik, and Ahmad. There is a weak narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani suggesting istihbab, but it is dismissed.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is prohibition.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-argument and Hanafi response
Shafi'is argue from the hadith 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Fatihah.' The Hanafi response: that hadith is specified by the Quranic command to listen and the Prophetic prohibition for the ma'mum. The Imam's recitation suffices.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference): Hanafis remain silent, Shafi'is recite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل يستمع حال جهر الإمام وينصت حال إسراره لقوله تعالى: (وإذا قرىء القرآن فاستمعوا له وأنصتوا) وقال : يكفيك قراءة الإمام جهر أم خافت واتفق الإمام الأعظم وأصحابه والإمام مالك، والإمام أحمد بن حنبل على صحة صلاة المأموم من غير قراءته شيئاً، وقد بسطته بالأصل (و) قلنا (إن قرأ) المأموم الفاتحة، أو غيرها (كره) ذلك (تحريماً) للنهي عنه بقوله : «لا يقرأ أحد منكم شيئاً من القرآن إذا جهرت بالقرآن» ولا نقول بمفهوم المخالفة، ويقول زيد بن ثابت : لا قراءة مع الإمام في شيء، وروي من كان له إمام فقراءة الإمام له قراءة، وروي عن ليث في فم الذي يقرأ خلف الإمام حجراً، وروى عنه : من قرأ خلف الإمام ففي فيه جمرة» وقال : من قرأ خلف الإمام فقد أخطأ الفطرة
Rather, he listens during the Imam's loud recitation and is silent during his quiet recitation, due to His statement (If the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent). And he (the Prophet) said: 'The Imam's recitation suffices for you, whether he recites loudly or quietly.' The Great Imam (Abu Hanifa) and his companions, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal agreed upon the validity of the ma'mum's prayer without him reciting anything. And I have elaborated on it in the original. And we do not accept the concept of the opposite meaning. Zayd ibn Thabit says: 'No recitation with the Imam in anything.' And it is narrated: 'Whoever has an Imam, the Imam's recitation is his recitation.' And it is narrated from Layth: 'In the mouth of the one who recites behind the Imam is a stone.' And it is narrated from him: 'Whoever recites behind the Imam has a burning coal in his mouth.' And he said: 'Whoever recites behind the Imam has missed the innate disposition.'

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the obligation of the ma'mum to listen and be silent during the Imam's recitation, and the prohibition of reciting behind the Imam. The author begins by stating the general duty: the ma'mum listens when the Imam recites aloud and is silent when the Imam recites quietly. The proof is the Quranic verse (7:204) which commands listening and silence when the Quran is recited. The Prophet's hadith confirms that the Imam's recitation suffices. The author then notes the consensus of the four major Imams (Abu Hanifa, his students, Malik, and Ahmad) that the ma'mum's prayer is valid without any recitation. Then the ruling is given: if the ma'mum recites (even al-Fatihah), it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The proof is the hadith where the Prophet explicitly forbade reciting when he recites aloud. The author clarifies that they do not apply the opposite meaning (i.e., that when the Imam recites silently, the ma'mum should recite). Additional narrations from Zayd ibn Thabit and others emphasize the prohibition. The strong language ('stone in mouth', 'burning coal') indicates the severity. The ruling is based on the principle that the ma'mum's obligation is to listen, and reciting would violate that.

Key Terms
المأموم (al-ma'mum): The person praying behind the Imam in congregational prayer.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A prohibition that is not established by qat'i evidence; it is forbidden to do it, but the doer is not an unbeliever.
الاستماع (al-istima'): Listening attentively to the Quran recitation, as commanded in Surah al-A'raf.

Key Takeaway
The ma'mum must listen and be silent; reciting behind the Imam is makruh tahrimi, supported by Quran, hadith, and consensus of the four Imams.

The Obligation of Ta'dil in Ruku': An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'dil's obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the legal status of ta'dil in Hanafi fiqh, distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ta'dil is wajib not fard: the prayer is valid without it but the worshipper is sinful.

This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute: is the pause after bowing (ta'dil) a fard or a wajib? While the outward definition of ruku' is clear, the scholarly disagreement on ta'dil reveals the Hanafi school's nuanced approach to evidence and the distinction between fard and wajib. Understanding this ikhtilaf will sharpen your ability to trace how a ruling is determined within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Locate the act in question: ta'dil (posture moderation) after ruku'. Note that the passage contrasts two positions: one calling it fard, the other implying it is not.
The passage explicitly names Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i as advocates of fardiyyah.
2
Distinguish the two Hanafi views
Abu Yusuf (and al-Shafi'i) hold ta'dil to be fard. Abu Hanifa's view, transmitted by his student Abu Mut'i al-Balkhi, indicates that omitting it invalidates the prayer according to a Companion, but this is interpreted as making it a condition (wajib) rather than a rukn.
The key is whether the evidence is considered qat'i (certain) or zanni (probable).
3
Analyze the proofs for each position
For Abu Yusuf: consistent practice of the Prophet implies fard. For Abu Hanifa: the literal meaning of the command to bow does not require a pause; the Companion's report is zanni and thus supports wujub (necessity) not fard.
The definition of ruku' itself (bending) does not include pausing.
4
Apply the Hanafi hierarchy of evidence
Fard is established only by qat'i evidence (Quran or mutawatir sunnah). Wajib is established by zanni evidence (ahad hadith or qiyas). Since the proof for ta'dil is zanni, it is classified as wajib.
This is a core usul principle in the Hanafi school.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: if one omits ta'dil intentionally, according to Abu Yusuf the prayer is invalid; according to the relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa), the prayer is valid but the person is sinful (makruh tahrimi). The mufta bihi is that ta'dil is wajib.
This position is upheld in later works like al-Hidayah and is the standard for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى اركعوا وهو الانحناء بالظهر والرأس جميعاً وكماله بتسوية الرأس بالعجز وأما التعديل فقال أبو يوسف والشافعي بفرضيته وقال أبو مطيع البلخي تلميذ الإمام أبي حنيفة عمر [؟] عن ذلك فساد صلاته عند واحد من الصحابة أفاده في الشرح
He said: 'Bow' and it is the bending of the back and the head together, and its perfection is making the head level with the buttocks. As for ta'dil (posture moderation), Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said it is obligatory. Abu Mut'i al-Balkhi, a student of Imam Abu Hanifa, said: '...about that, the invalidity of his prayer according to one of the Companions.' It was mentioned in the commentary.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling statement. It defines ruku' (bowing) as the bending of the back and head together, with its perfection being the leveling of the head with the buttocks. Then it addresses ta'dil (also called tumaninah/posture moderation) – the brief pause after bending. The text reports that Abu Yusuf (a leading Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i consider ta'dil obligatory (fard). In contrast, Abu Mut'i al-Balkhi, a prominent student of Abu Hanifa, transmits a view that omitting ta'dil invalidates the prayer according to one Companion, implying it is a condition. The commentator (al-Tahtawi) notes that this was stated in the Sharh (commentary on Maraqi al-Falah). This illustrates a difference within the Hanafi school: the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that ta'dil is wajib (necessary), not fard, based on the principle that the proof is zanni. However, the text presents the stronger view of Abu Yusuf. The passage also shows the Hanafi method of citing Companions' opinions as supporting evidence.

Key Terms
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bowing in prayer: bending the back and head together. Its perfection is leveling the head with the buttocks.
التعديل (al-ta'dil): Posture moderation: the pause after bowing until the limbs settle. Also called tumaninah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi position on ta'dil (posture moderation) in ruku'?
A) It is fard (obligatory) as stated by Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.
B) It is sunnah, and omitting it does not affect the prayer.
C) It is wajib (necessary) but not fard; omitting it makes the prayer valid but sinful.
D) It is not required at all in ruku'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds ta'dil in ruku' as wajib, not fard; omitting it is sinful but the prayer remains valid.

Ruku' in Hanafi Fiqh: Minimum Bending, Tasbihat, and Tranquility
Commentary on the obligation and minimum of ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum requirements for ruku' according to the Hanafi school and identify the conditions that affect its validity.

Core Idea
Ruku' is valid with mere bending of the back; reaching the knees is sunnah, not obligatory.

Ruku' (bowing) is a key posture in prayer. This passage from al-Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies its definition, proof of obligation, and the minimum bending required. It also addresses the role of tasbihat (glorifications) and tranquility (tamninah), and provides an exception for the physically unable. Understanding these nuances helps ensure that your prayer is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Establish the obligation of ruku'
Identify that ruku' is wajib (obligatory) in prayer, supported by the Quranic command 'irka'u' (bow), the Sunnah, and Ijma (consensus).
Hanafi usul: the imperative indicates wujub (obligation), but the proof is zanni al-dalala, hence ruku' is wajib, not fard.
2
Define the minimum ruku'
The minimum ruku' is bending the back enough that the hands could reach the knees if extended. Actual touching of the knees is not required for validity.
Multiple sources (al-Bada'i', al-Siraj, al-Hawi, al-Tuhfah) confirm that mere bending suffices, though the complete form is recommended.
3
Understand the ruling on tasbihat
The sunnah is to recite three tasbihat ('Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim') in ruku'. Reducing them intentionally may invalidate the prayer according to some Hanafi authorities, though there is difference.
Imam Muhammad held that reducing from three invalidates; others consider it makruh but not invalidating. The text emphasizes precaution.
4
Recognize the tranquility issue
Tranquility (tamninah) in ruku' to the extent of one tasbihah is considered wajib by Abu Yusuf, but others consider it sunnah. The text advises precaution to adopt Abu Yusuf's view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is that tamninah is sunnah, but observing it is safer.
5
Apply the exception for the hunchback
A hunchback whose hump is at the level of ruku' must indicate with his head for ruku', even slightly. His hump does not substitute for ruku' because he is like one standing.
The principle: the physically unable must do what is possible (la yukallifu Allahu nafsan illa wus'aha).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رحمه الله تعالى : لو نقص من ثلاث تسبيحات الركوع والسجود لم تجز صلاته والأحدب إذا بلغت حدوبته الركوع يشير برأسه للركوع لأنه عاجز عما هو أعلى (و) يفترض (الركوع) لقوله تعالى : (اركعوا) ولورود السنة به وللإجماع عليه قوله : (وهو الإنحناء بالظهر، والرأس جميعاً) هذا معناه الشرعي، ومعناه لغة مطلق الإنحناء، والميل يقال : ركعت النخلة إذا مالت، وأدناه شرعاً إنحناء الظهر بحيث لو مد يديه ينال ركبتيه، وفي البدائع روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة فيمن لم يقم أي يعدل صلبه في الركوع إن كان إلى القيام أقرب من تمام الركوع لم يجزه وإن كان أقرب إلى تمام الركوع من القيام أجزأه إقامة للأكثر مقام الكل اهـ، ومثله في السراج عن الكرخي قال المحقق ابن أمير حاج وذلك لأنّ الركوع إنحناء الظهر كما تقدم وإذا وجد بعض الإنحناء دون البعض ترجح الأكثر وصارت العبرة له ،اهـ وإنما يكون إلى تمام الركوع أقرب إذا كان بحيث تنال يداه ركبتيه، وتمامه هو أن يبسط ظهره، ويساوي رأسه بعجزه، ولا يكون أقرب إلى هذه الحالة بدون ما ذكرنا وفي شرح المختار الركوع يتحقق بما ينطلق عليه الإسم لأنه عبارة عن الإنحناء، وفي الحاوي فرض الركوع إنحناء الظهر وفي التحفة قدر المفروض في الركوع هو أصل الإنحناء اهـ وعلى ما في هذه المعتبرات يصح الركوع وإن لم تنل يداه ركبتيه، والاحتياط الأول وفي الحموي : فإن ركع جالساً ينبغي أن تحاذي جبهته ركبتيه ليحصل الركوع اهـ، ولعل مراده إنحناء الظهر عملاً بالحقيقة لا أنه يبالغ فيه حتى يكون قريباً من السجود. قوله: (وأما التعديل) أي الطمأنينة بمقدار تسبيحة واحدة، وصحح قول أبي يوسف بعض أهل المذهب فالإحتياط في مراعاته كما أنّ الإحتياط في مراعاة قول أبي مطيع البلخي في التسبيح . قوله: (لم تجز صلاته قاس الركوع على القيام فوجب أن يحله ذكر مفروض كما أن القراءة تحل بالقيام أفاده في الشرح قوله : ( يشير برأسه للركوع) ولو قليلاً تحقيقاً للإنتقال فإنه القدر الممكن في حقه، ولا يلزمه غير ذلك، ولا تجزيه حدوبته عن الركوع لأنه كالقائم ذكره الحدادي والحلبي قوله عما هو أعلى أي من الإشارة، وهو بسط الظهر والأولى في التعليل ما قدمناه
May Allah have mercy on him: If one reduces from three tasbihat of ruku' and sujud, his prayer is not valid. And the hunchback whose hump reaches the level of ruku' indicates with his head for ruku' because he is incapable of what is higher. And ruku' is obligatory by His saying: 'Bow' and by the Sunnah and consensus. He said: 'It is bending of the back and head together.' This is its legal meaning; its linguistic meaning is absolute bending and inclining: it is said 'the palm tree bowed' when it inclines. Its least legally is bending the back such that if he extends his hands he reaches his knees. In al-Bada'i', al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa regarding one who did not straighten his spine in ruku': if he is closer to standing than to complete ruku', it does not suffice; if he is closer to complete ruku' than standing, it suffices him, adopting the majority as the whole. The same is in al-Siraj from al-Karkhi; al-Muhaqqiq Ibn Amir Haj said: That is because ruku' is bending the back as previously, and when some bending is found but not all, the majority preponderates and consideration is given to it. It is only closer to complete ruku' when his hands reach his knees; its completion is to spread his back and equalize his head with his buttocks, and he is not closer to this state without what we mentioned. In Sharh al-Mukhtar, ruku' is realized by whatever the name applies to because it is an expression for bending. In al-Hawi, the obligatory part of ruku' is bending the back, and in al-Tuhfah, the measure of the obligatory in ruku' is the origin of bending. According to these reliable sources, ruku' is valid even if his hands do not reach his knees, but precaution is the first. In al-Hamawi: If he bows while sitting, his forehead should face his knees to achieve ruku'. Perhaps his intent is bending the back in accordance with the reality, not that he exaggerates until he is close to prostration. His statement: 'As for the modification' i.e., tranquility to the extent of one tasbihah; some scholars of the madhhab corrected the saying of Abu Yusuf, so precaution is to observe it just as precaution is to observe the saying of Abu Muti' al-Balkhi regarding tasbih. His statement: 'His prayer is not valid.' He analogized ruku' to standing, so an obligatory dhikr must occupy it just as recitation occupies standing. This was benefited from al-Sharh. His statement: 'He indicates with his head for ruku' even slightly, effecting the transition, for it is the extent possible for him; nothing else is required of him, and his hump does not suffice for ruku' because he is like one standing, mentioned by al-Hadadi and al-Halabi. His statement: 'than what is higher' i.e., than indication, and it is spreading the back; the better explanation is what we presented.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the obligations and minimum requirements of ruku' in prayer. The text begins by stating the ruling of Imam Muhammad that reducing the tasbihat from three to less invalidates the prayer. It then addresses the hunchback, who must indicate with his head for ruku' because he cannot bend his back. The legal definition of ruku' is bending the back and head together, with the minimum being bending enough that the hands could reach the knees. However, the author clarifies from multiple sources that actual knee-touching is not obligatory; the original bending suffices, and validity is achieved even without reaching the knees. The precaution is to aim for the complete form. The text also addresses tranquility (tamninah) as obligatory to the extent of one tasbihah, citing Abu Yusuf's view. The proof for the obligation of dhikr in ruku' is analogized from standing, where recitation is obligatory. The commentary emphasizes that the hunchback must still make some motion (head indication) to transition, and his hump does not substitute for ruku'.

Key Terms
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bending of the back and head together, with the minimum being enough bending that the hands would reach the knees if extended.
الطمأنينة (al-tamninah): Tranquility and stillness in a posture to the extent of at least one tasbihah.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): The utterance of 'Subhana Rabbiyal-'Azim' in ruku' and 'Subhana Rabbiyal-A'la' in sujud, three times as sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum required for ruku' to be valid according to the text?
A) Placing the palms on the knees
B) Bending the back such that the hands could reach the knees
C) Reciting three tasbihat
D) Touching the head to the back

Key Takeaway
Ruku' is wajib with a minimum of bending the back, and the sunnah includes three tasbihat and tranquility, but the school accommodates physical limitations.

The Obligations and Minimal Conditions of Sujud in the Hanafi School
Commentary on the obligation and minimal conditions of sujud with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory parts of sujud (forehead, palms, knees, feet) and explain which part of the face must be placed, distinguishing between the forehead and nose according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Core Idea
Sujud requires placing the forehead; the nose alone suffices only with excuse, and at least one toe from one foot must touch the ground.

In this lesson, we examine the obligations (fara'id) of sujud (prostration) as established by the Quranic command, Sunnah, and Ijma'. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the minimal requirements: the forehead must be placed, the nose alone does not suffice without an excuse, and the feet must touch the ground with at least the tips of the toes. We will also explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the nose can substitute and the evidence from the hadith of the seven limbs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sujud is fard (obligatory) based on the Quranic command 'bow and prostrate' (22:77) and Ijma'.
It is a devotional act whose wisdom is not fully known.
2
Locate the primary required limb
The forehead must be placed on the ground; at least a part of it suffices.
The hadith mentions 'face', which primarily means the forehead.
3
Analyze the nose dispute
Understand the difference between Abu Hanifa (nose alone invalid without excuse) and the two companions (nose alone valid even without excuse in one narration). The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa.
The nose is part of the face, but the stronger narration requires the forehead.
4
Determine the foot requirement
At least one finger from one foot must be placed; both feet are obligatory but one suffices (though disliked). Placing the top of the foot or tips of toes without reliance is invalid.
Whatever is necessary to fulfill the obligation is itself obligatory.
5
Appreciate the underlying principle
The principle that whatever is necessary to fulfill an obligation becomes obligatory applies to the feet: you must place at least part of the sole/toes to achieve contact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويفترض السجود) المراد منه الجنس أي السجدتان وكونه كذلك ثبت بالسنة والإجماع، وهو أمر تعبدي لم يطلع على حكمته كعدد الركعات، وذكر بعضهم له حكماً عديدة ، وستأتي ويحتمل أن المراد السجدة الأولى لما يأتي متناً من قوله، ويفترض العود إلى السجود قوله : ( واسجدوا) قيل : كان الناس أوّل ما أسلموا يسجدون بلا ركوع، ويركعون بلا سجود، فنزل يا أيها الذين آمنوا اركعوا واسجدوا [الحج/ 22] . قوله: (وبالسنة والإجماع الأولى التعبير باللام كما في الشرح . قوله: (إنما تتحقق بوضع الجبهة) قال في المجتبى ولو سجد على طرف من أطراف الجبهة جاز، وفي ظاهر من الأرض، وإلا فلا وجود لها ومع ذلك البعض تصح على المختار . قوله : (لا الأنف وحده) أي بغير عذر، وأما به فيجوز وهذه رواية عن الإمام، وبها أخذ الصاحبان وأما الإقتصار على الجبهة فيصح مطلقاً بالإتفاق وفي رواية عن الإمام يصح الإقتصار على أدنى جزء من أحدهما مطلقاً بعذر وبدونه وهو الصحيح من مذهب الإمام كما في العيني على البخاري له ما في السنن الأربعة عن العباس عم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه سمع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «إذا سجد العبد سجد معه سبعة آراب وجهه وكفاه وركبتاه وقدماه اهـ. قال في الكافي : والسجود بكل الوجه متعذر فكان المراد بعضه والأنف وسط الوجه فإذا سجد عليه كان ممتثلاً كما لو سجد على الجبهة لأنه إنما جاز الإقتصار على الجبهة لأنها بعض الوجه وهو المأمور به والأنف بعضه أيضاً فجاز الإقتصار عليه كما في ابن أمير حاج قال في الفتح وجعل بعض المتأخرين الفتوى على الرواية الموافقة لقولهما لم يوافقه دراية ولا القوى من الرواية كما علمته اهـ ومن ثم قال في الهداية : والوجه ظاهر للإمام .اهـ. قوله : (وشيء من أطراف أصابع إحدى القدمين) يصدق ذلك بإصبع واحدة قال في الخلاصة، وأما وضع القدم على الأرض في الصلاة حال السجدة ففرض فلو وضع إحداهما دون الأخرى تجوز صلاته، كما لو قام على قدم واحد ووضع القدم موضع أصابعه، ويكفي وضع إصبع واحدة وفي الفتح عن الوجيز، وضع القدمين فرض فإن وضع إحداهما دون الأخرى جاز، ويكره فإن وضع ظاهر قدميه، أو رؤس الأصابع لا يصح لعدم الإعتماد على شيء من رجليه وما لا يتوصل للفرض إلا به فهو فرض وهذا مما يجب التنبه له، وأكثر الناس عنه غافلون، وهذا هو الموافق لما في مختصر الكرخي معللاً بأن الوضع بدون توجيه وضع لظاهر القدم، وهو غير معتبر وفي خزانة المفتين أنّ ذلك مكروه . قوله عن نصير في نسخة عن ابن نصير اهم مصححه
His statement: 'And sujud is obligatory' means the genus, i.e., the two prostrations. That it is so is established by Sunnah and Ijma', and it is a devotional act whose wisdom is not known like the number of rak'ahs. Some have mentioned many wisdoms for it, and they will come. It is possible that the intended meaning is the first prostration because of what will come in the text: 'And returning to sujud is obligatory.' His statement: 'And prostrate' – it is said that people when they first embraced Islam used to prostrate without bowing and bow without prostrating, so was revealed: 'O you who have believed, bow and prostrate' [22:77]. His statement: 'By Sunnah and Ijma' – it is better to express with the lam as in al-Sharh. His statement: 'It is only realized by placing the forehead' – it is said in al-Mujtaba: If he prostrates on a part of the edges of his forehead, it is permissible, and on the apparent surface of the ground, otherwise it does not exist; yet that part suffices according to the chosen view. His statement: 'Not the nose alone' i.e., without an excuse, but with an excuse it is permissible. This is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, and the two companions adopted it. As for limiting to the forehead, it is valid absolutely by agreement. And in a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, limiting to the smallest part of either (forehead or nose) is valid absolutely with or without excuse, and this is the correct view of the madhhab as in al-'Ayni on al-Bukhari. There is in the four Sunan from al-'Abbas, the uncle of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), that he heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'When the slave prostrates, seven limbs prostrate with him: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet.' It is said in al-Kafi: Prostration with the entire face is impossible, so the intended is part of it, and the nose is the middle of the face; so if he prostrates on it, he is compliant just as if he prostrated on the forehead, because it is only permissible to limit to the forehead because it is part of the face which is commanded, and the nose is also part of it, so it is permissible to limit to it. As in Ibn Amir Haj, it is said in al-Fath: Some later scholars made the fatwa on the narration agreeing with the two companions, but it is not sound in knowledge nor in the stronger narration as you have learned. Hence it is said in al-Hidayah: 'The face is apparent for the Imam.' His statement: 'And something from the tips of the toes of one of the feet' – this is true of one finger. It is said in al-Khulasa: As for placing the foot on the ground during prayer in the state of sujud, it is obligatory. So if he places one (foot) without the other, his prayer is permissible, just as if he stood on one foot and placed the foot in the place of his toes. One finger suffices. In al-Fath from al-Wajiz: Placing both feet is obligatory. If he places one without the other, it is permissible but disliked. If he places the top of his feet or the tips of the toes, it is not valid because of lack of reliance on anything from his legs, and whatever is necessary to fulfill the obligation is itself obligatory. This is something that must be noticed, and most people are heedless of it. This agrees with what is in Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, explaining that placing without directing is placing the top of the foot, which is not considered. In Khizanat al-Muftin, that is disliked. His statement: 'from Nasir' – in a copy 'from Ibn Nasir' – the corrector omitted.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the obligations and minimal conditions of sujud. It begins by establishing that sujud (the two prostrations) is obligatory based on the Quranic command, Sunnah, and Ijma', and it is a devotional act whose exact wisdom is not known, like the number of rak'ahs. The text then details the required parts: the forehead must be placed on the ground, and at least a part of it suffices. The nose alone is not sufficient without an excuse, but with an excuse it is permissible according to a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) adopt this. However, the stronger narration is that only the forehead suffices alone; the nose does not substitute except with excuse. The proof quoted is the hadith of the seven limbs (face, palms, knees, feet). The text then discusses the feet: at least one finger from one foot must be placed on the ground; placing both feet is obligatory, but one suffices, though it is disliked. Placing the top of the foot or tips of toes is invalid because there is no actual reliance. The commentary emphasizes that whatever is necessary to fulfill the obligation (like placing at least one finger from each limb) is itself obligatory. The passage also notes a textual variant: 'from Nasir' or 'from Ibn Nasir'.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration, a devotional act requiring placement of the forehand (and other limbs) on the ground in a state of humility.
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The forehead, the primary part of the face required for sujud.
الآراب (al-ar'ab): The seven limbs that prostrate: face, palms, knees, feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Forehead
B) Knees
C) Elbows
D) Palms

Key Takeaway
Sujud requires placing the forehead on the ground; the nose alone suffices only with excuse, and at least one toe from one foot must touch the ground.

Conditions for Valid Sujood: The Seven Bones and Hanafi Rulings
Explains conditions and rulings for valid prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid sujood in the Hanafi school and apply the hadith of the seven bones to derive the operative ruling.

Core Idea
Only the forehead is obligatory for sujood; the other six bones are sunnah but recommended.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details the conditions (shurut) for a valid prostration in salah. It is built around the famous hadith 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones,' but the Hanafi interpretation distinguishes between obligatory and recommended parts. Understanding these conditions is essential for correct prayer and for appreciating how the Hanafi school uses textual indications (dalala) to derive fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions listed in the passage
Scan the Arabic text and list all conditions mentioned for valid sujood: firm surface, forehead contact, elevation limit, required body parts (forehead, one hand, one knee, some toes), and order (bowing before sujood).
The conditions are introduced by phrases like 'من شروط صحة السجود'.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the hadith quoted: 'أمرت أن أسجد على سبعة أعظم على الجبهة واليدين والركبتين وأطراف القدمين'. Note its source (Muttafaqun 'alayh).
The hadith is given as proof for the places of sujood.
3
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation
Understand that the Hanafi school interprets the hadith as defining the mahall (locations) for prostration, not as a requirement to place all seven simultaneously. Hence the forehead is obligatory, and the rest are sunnah.
This interpretation is key to distinguishing what is fard/wajib versus sunnah.
4
Apply the conditions to scenarios
Use the conditions to determine the validity of sujood in various cases: on soft materials, on garments, on another's back during crowding, etc.
Practical application ensures comprehension of the shurut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة

۲۳۱

فإن إقتصر عليها لا يجوز إجماعاً كما في السراج عن المستصفي. قوله: (في عدم جواز الشروع في الصلاة (بالفارسية نقل في الدر عن التتارخانية أنّ الشروع بالفارسية كالتلبية يجوز إتفاقاً أي لغير العاجز فظاهره رجوعهما إليه لا هو إليهما، وهذا عكس القراءة فإنه رجع إليهما . قوله : (وعدم جواز الإقتصار في السجود على الأنف (الخ قد علمت ما قاله الكمال، وصاحب الهداية. قوله : (الحديث أمرت الخ) روي الحديث بروايات عديدة منها رواية العباس، وفيها ذكر الوجه لا الجبهة وقد سبق قوله والإرتفاع (القليل) وهو ما كان نصف ذراع فأقل قوله : على ظهر مصل صلاته (الخ وشرط في الكفاية كون ركبتي الساجد على الأرض، وشرط في المجتبى سجود المسجود عليه على الأرض، فحملة الشروط خمسة، بل ستة بزيادة الزحام لكن في القهستاني عن الأصل أنه يجوز ولو على ظهر غير المصلي، ونقل الزاهدي جوازه على ظهر كل مأكول، وفي القهستاني عن صدر القضاة أنه يجوز وإن كان سجود الثاني على ظهر الثالث، وفيه أنه في هذه الحالة يكون الساجد الثالث في صفة الراكع، أو أزيد، ونقل عن أنه الجلابي يستحب التأخير حتى يزول الزحام اهـ قوله: (وهو اختيار الفقيه) وقيل إن وضع اليدين والركبتين سنة، وعليه يقال أن الحديث يقتضي وجوب السجود على الأعضاء السبعة المصرح بها فيه، ولم يقولوا به، والجواب أن الإستدلال بهذا الحديث إنما هو على أن محل السجود هذه الأعضاء لا أن وضع جميعها لازم لا محالة، فوضع اليدين، والركبتين سنة عندنا
Book of Prayer. The completion of sujood is by performing what is obligatory in it, and it is realized by placing both hands, both knees, both feet, the forehead, and the nose, as stated by al-Kamal and others. Among the conditions for validity of sujood is that it be on something that finds for the prostrator its volume, such that if he were to press his head it would not sink further than it was at placement. So sujood is not valid on cotton, snow, straw, rice, corn, flaxseed, wheat, and barley unless his forehead rests upon it, because the grains settle on each other due to roughness and softness. The forehead is the name for what touches the ground from above the eyebrows to the hairline during sujood. Sujood is valid even if upon his palm, according to the correct view, or upon the edge of his garment, but it is disliked without an excuse, like sujood on the coil of his turban if the place of placement is pure, on the most correct view, because of its connection to him. And he must prostrate with the hard part of his nose, because the tip is not a place of prostration. Since it is a condition... He said: and he prostrates with his forehead and not only the nose on the most correct view, except due to an excuse in the forehead, because the most correct is that the Imam returned to agreeing with his two companions regarding the impermissibility of starting prayer in Persian for one not incapable of Arabic, and the impermissibility of reciting in Persian etc., and the impermissibility of limiting sujood to the nose without an excuse in the forehead, due to the hadith: 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones, on the forehead...' the hadith. And among the conditions for validity of sujood is that the place of prostration not be more than half a cubit above the place of the feet, so that the characteristic of the prostrator is realized. A slight elevation does not harm. If it exceeds half a cubit, the prostration is not valid, i.e., it is not considered. If he performed it considering it valid, it is valid; but if he leaves his prayer without repeating it, it becomes invalid. Except if due to crowding he prostrates on the back of a person who is in prayer out of necessity. If that person being prostrated upon is not in prayer, or is in another prayer, then it is not permissible. And among the conditions of validity of sujood is placing one hand and one knee in the correct view, as we have mentioned, and placing some of the toes directed with the inner side towards the qibla during sujood on the ground. Placing the outer side of the foot is not sufficient, because it is not the place, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones: the forehead, both hands, both knees, and the tips of the feet.' Agreed upon, and it is the choice of the Faqih. There is disagreement regarding permissibility with placing one foot. And it is required for the validity of bowing and prostration to precede bowing before prostration, just as it is required to precede recitation before bowing, after which there is no standing in which recitation is valid. If he limits to it [i.e., recitation after bowing], it is not permissible by consensus, as in al-Siraj from al-Mustasfi.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
The passage discusses the conditions (shurut) for the validity of sujood (prostration) in prayer. It begins by stating that the completion of sujood is achieved by performing its obligatory elements (wajib), which includes placing both hands, both knees, both feet, the forehead, and the nose. This is based on the hadith 'I was commanded to prostrate on seven bones.' The commentator then details the conditions: the place of prostration must be firm such that the forehead does not sink into it; thus sujood is invalid on soft materials like cotton, snow, or grains that do not pack firmly. Sujood is valid on one's palm or the edge of one's garment, though disliked without excuse. The forehead must touch the ground; the nose alone is insufficient unless there is an excuse. Elevation of the prostration site more than half a cubit above the feet invalidates sujood, except in cases of crowding where prostrating on the back of another person in prayer is permitted. The required body parts are the forehead (or nose in excuse), one hand, one knee, and some toes (inner side facing qibla). The passage also mentions the order: bowing must precede prostration. The hadith is cited as proof that these are the places of prostration, though the Hanafi school holds that placing both hands and both knees is sunnah, not obligatory, because the hadith indicates the location of prostration, not the necessity of placing all seven simultaneously.

Key Terms
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The part of the face between the eyebrows and the hairline that touches the ground during sujood.
السجود (al-sujood): Prostration; placing the forehead (and optionally other specified parts) on the ground in a specific manner during prayer.
الأنف (al-anf): The nose; only the hard part (the bridge) is considered the place of prostration, not the tip (arnabah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on sujood limited to the nose without an excuse?
A) Valid
B) Valid but disliked
C) Invalid
D) Invalid unless the nose touches

Key Takeaway
Valid sujood requires a firm surface, the forehead touching the ground, and at least one hand, one knee, and some toes, with bowing preceding it.
