The Intention for Fard and Sunnah in Prayer
Explains the condition of distinguishing fard from sunnah in prayer intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the required intention when performing a prayer that includes both fard and sunnah components, and explain why detailed distinction is not required.

Core Idea
One must intend the prayer as obligatory (fard), but it is not necessary to distinguish each sunnah act from the fard.

In performing the daily prayers, a worshipper may combine sunnah and fard acts, such as in the Fajr prayer which consists of two sunnah rak'ahs followed by two fard rak'ahs. How should one intend these? The Hanafi school holds that a general intention that the entire prayer is obligatory suffices, and detailed distinction is not required. This passage from al-Tahtawi explains the reasoning and consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
The text addresses whether a worshipper must distinguish each sunnah act from the fard during prayer.
Focus on the phrase 'ليس المراد ولا الشرط أن يميز'
2
Understand the Condition
The condition is that one must believe the entire prayer (e.g., four rak'ahs in Fajr) is obligatory (fard), and pray each two rak'ahs separately.
Example given for Fajr and Maghrib
3
Recognize the Distinction Not Required
It is not required to differentiate the specific fard and sunnah components (e.g., knowing that standing is fard and thana is sunnah).
The text explicitly says 'ليس المراد ولا الشرط'
4
Apply the Consequence
If one intends the supererogatory as obligatory, it becomes valid; the opposite does not hold.
The principle: 'النفل يتأدى بنية الفرض'
5
Note the Source
The ruling is supported by references to al-Tajnīs, al-Mazīd, and al-Khulāṣa.
These are key Hanafi texts

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن كتاب الصلاة الفجر وأربع الظهر وهكذا باقي الصلوات (المفروضة) فيكون ذلك على وجه (يميزها الخصال) أي الصفات (المسنونة) كالسنن الرواتب وغيرها باعتقاد سنية ما قبل الظهر وما بعده، وهكذا، وليس المراد ولا الشرط أن يميز ما اشتملت عليه صلاة الصبح من الفرض، والسنة مثل اعتقاد فرضية القيام وسنة الثناء والتسبيح (أو اعتقاد) المصلي (أنها أي أن ذات الصلوات التي يفعلها كلها (فرض) كاعتقاده أن الأربع في الفجر فرض ويصلي كل ركعتين بانفرادهما، ويأتي بثلاث ثم ركعتين في المغرب معتقداً فرضية الخمس (حتى لا يتنفل بمفروض) لأنّ النفل يتأدى بنية الفرض أما الفرض فلا يتأدى بنية النفل كما في التجنيس والمزيد والخلاصة، ثم نبه على الأركان وغيرها فقال : ( والأركان) المتفق عليها (من المذكورات التي علمتها فيما قدمناه بأكثر من سبعة وعشرين (أربعة) وهي (القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود وقيل القعود الأخير مقدار التشهد) ركن أيضاً، وقيل: شرط وقد بينا ثمرة الخلاف فيه وقيل التحريمة ركن أيضاً (وباقيها) أي المذكورات شرائط بعضها شرط لصحة الشروع في الصلاة وهو ما كان خارجها وهو الطهارة من الحدث والخبث وستر العورة واستقبال القبلة، والوقت، والنية، والتحريمة وغيره) شرط لدوام صحتها) وقد علمت ذلك بفضل الله ومنه وله الشكر على التوفيق لجمعها بعد التفريق .
From the Book of Prayer: The dawn prayer and four of the noon, and so on for the rest of the obligatory prayers. So that is in a manner that distinguishes the characteristics, i.e. the supererogatory attributes, like the regular supererogatory prayers and others, by believing the supererogatory nature of what is before noon and after, etc. And the intent nor the condition is to distinguish what the morning prayer includes of the obligatory and the sunnah, such as believing the obligation of standing and the sunnah of the thanā' and tasbīḥ. Or the worshipper's belief that the very prayers he performs are all obligatory, like his belief that the four in the dawn are obligatory and he prays every two rak'ahs separately, and he comes with three then two in the maghrib believing the obligation of five, so that he does not perform supererogatory with an obligatory act. For the supererogatory is performed with the intention of the obligatory, while the obligatory is not performed with the intention of the supererogatory, as in al-Tajnīs, al-Mazīd, and al-Khulāṣa. Then he drew attention to the pillars and others and said: 'The pillars agreed upon from the mentioned actions which you learned in what we presented earlier as more than twenty-seven are four: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. And it is said that the final sitting to the extent of the tashahhud is also a pillar, and it is said it is a condition, and we have explained the fruit of the dispute in it. And it is said that the takbīrat al-taḥrīma is also a pillar. And the rest of the mentioned actions are conditions; some of them are conditions for the validity of commencing prayer, which are those outside it: purification from impurity and filth, covering the nakedness, facing the qibla, the time, the intention, and the takbīrat al-taḥrīma; and others are conditions for the continuity of its validity.' And you have known that by the grace of Allah and His bounty, and thanks to Him for enabling the gathering of them after dispersal.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies a key point about the intention in prayer: one must intend whether an act is fard or sunnah, but it is not required to distinguish every detail. For example, when praying Fajr, one must believe that the four rak'ahs are obligatory (fard), even though two are sunnah, and pray each two separately. The author then lists the four (or five) pillars of prayer agreed upon: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration, with a difference of opinion on the final sitting. The remaining actions—like purification, covering the awrah, etc.—are conditions (shuroot) for the prayer's validity. This passage is particularly important for understanding the Hanafi position on intention and the structure of prayer.

Key Terms
الخصال المسنونة (al-khiṣāl al-masnūna): The recommended attributes or supererogatory acts associated with the obligatory prayers, such as the regular sunnah prayers (rawātib).
الفرض (al-farḍ): That which is obligatory by definitive evidence (Quran or mutawatir Sunnah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required regarding the intention of the worshipper during the prayer's sunnah acts?
A) He must specifically intend each sunnah act separately.
B) He must have a general belief that the prayer is obligatory (fard), and the sunnah acts are performed as part of it.
C) He must intend the sunnah acts as voluntary, not obligatory.
D) He must intend both the fard and sunnah acts simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
It is sufficient to believe the entire prayer is fard; detailed distinction of sunnah acts is not required for validity.

The Pillars and Conditions of Prayer in the Hanafi School
Enumerates the pillars and conditions of prayer with disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four agreed-upon pillars of prayer, identify the disputed pillars, and distinguish between conditions for commencing prayer and conditions for its continuity.

Core Idea
Prayer rests on four pillars: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration; all other actions are conditions, some for starting, some for staying valid.

In the Hanafi school, the structure of prayer is defined by pillars (arkān) which are integral, and conditions (shurūṭ) which are external requirements. This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya enumerates the four agreed pillars and notes disagreements about whether the final sitting and opening takbīr are pillars or conditions. It also categorizes conditions into those for commencing prayer and those for its continuity, providing a clear framework for understanding prayer validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Agreed Pillars
The text lists standing (qiyām), recitation (qirā’ah), bowing (rukū‘), and prostration (sujūd) as the pillars unanimously agreed upon.
These are the essential integral parts.
2
Note the Disputed Elements
The final sitting (al-qu‘ūd al-ākhir) and the opening takbīr (taḥrīma) are said by some to be pillars, by others to be conditions.
The text explicitly mentions the dispute for both.
3
Categorize Conditions
Conditions are divided into two types: conditions for the validity of commencing prayer (shurūṭ al-shurū‘) which are external prerequisites, and conditions for the continuity of validity (shurūṭ al-dawām) which must be maintained.
The text lists the commencement conditions: purification, covering, qibla, time, intention, opening takbīr.
4
Understand the Practical Difference
If a disputed element is a pillar, omitting it invalidates the prayer; if it is a condition, the consequence differs (e.g., requiring sujūd al-sahw or invalidating).
The text mentions 'thamar al-khilāf' (fruit of the dispute).
5
Appreciate the Compilation
The author thanks Allah for gathering these scattered points into one summary.
Indicates the comprehensive nature of this enumeration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن كتاب الصلاة الفجر وأربع الظهر وهكذا باقي الصلوات (المفروضة) فيكون ذلك على وجه (يميزها الخصال) أي الصفات (المسنونة) كالسنن الرواتب وغيرها باعتقاد سنية ما قبل الظهر وما بعده، وهكذا، وليس المراد ولا الشرط أن يميز ما اشتملت عليه صلاة الصبح من الفرض، والسنة مثل اعتقاد فرضية القيام وسنة الثناء والتسبيح (أو اعتقاد) المصلي (أنها أي أن ذات الصلوات التي يفعلها كلها (فرض) كاعتقاده أن الأربع في الفجر فرض ويصلي كل ركعتين بانفرادهما، ويأتي بثلاث ثم ركعتين في المغرب معتقداً فرضية الخمس (حتى لا يتنفل بمفروض) لأنّ النفل يتأدى بنية الفرض أما الفرض فلا يتأدى بنية النفل كما في التجنيس والمزيد والخلاصة، ثم نبه على الأركان وغيرها فقال : ( والأركان) المتفق عليها (من المذكورات التي علمتها فيما قدمناه بأكثر من سبعة وعشرين (أربعة) وهي (القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود وقيل القعود الأخير مقدار التشهد) ركن أيضاً، وقيل: شرط وقد بينا ثمرة الخلاف فيه وقيل التحريمة ركن أيضاً (وباقيها) أي المذكورات شرائط بعضها شرط لصحة الشروع في الصلاة وهو ما كان خارجها وهو الطهارة من الحدث والخبث وستر العورة واستقبال القبلة، والوقت، والنية، والتحريمة وغيره) شرط لدوام صحتها) وقد علمت ذلك بفضل الله ومنه وله الشكر على التوفيق لجمعها بعد التفريق .

So that is in a manner that distinguishes the characteristics, i.e. the supererogatory attributes, like the regular supererogatory prayers and others, by believing the supererogatory nature of what is before noon and after, etc. And the intent nor the condition is to distinguish what the morning prayer includes of the obligatory and the sunnah, such as believing the obligation of standing and the sunnah of the thanā' and tasbīḥ. Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies a key point about the intention in prayer: one must intend whether an act is fard or sunnah, but it is not required to distinguish every detail. Key Terms
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of prayer whose omission invalidates the prayer entirely.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition external to the prayer that must exist for validity; its absence prevents correctness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT listed as one of the four agreed-upon pillars of prayer?
A) Standing (qiyam).
B) Recitation (qira'ah).
C) Final sitting (al-qu'ud al-akhir).
D) Bowing (ruku').

Key Takeaway
Prayer has four agreed pillars; the final sitting and opening takbīr are disputed between pillar and condition; conditions are divided into those for commencement and those for continuity.

Prayer on Mixed Purity Surfaces: The Felt Ruling
Ruling on the permissibility of praying on a thick substance with mixed purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on a thick substance with mixed purity and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Prayer on a thick substance with a clean top and impure bottom is valid because thickness makes it like two garments.

This lesson explores a practical scenario in prayer: what if the surface you pray on has an impure bottom but a clean top? The Hanafi school has internal disagreement on this, rooted in whether a thick substance is considered one unit or two. By examining the rationale and the opinions of the three senior Hanafi imams, you will understand how the school resolves such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific act being ruled upon (prayer on a felt with a pure top and impure bottom). State the initial ruling: it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The ruling applies to any thick substance that can be split into two halves.
2
Locate the disagreement
Identify that Abu Yusuf disagrees. He holds that the prayer is invalid because the substance is a single object, not two independent layers.
The disagreement is between the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf vs. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) – an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Trace the rationale
Understand the legal reasoning: due to its thickness, the felt is treated like two separate garments (ka thobayni). Therefore, only the top layer's purity matters.
This is based on the concept that a thick object can be physically separated, making it analogous to two independent surfaces.
4
Apply to related cases
The same reasoning extends to similar cases: non-quilted garments with impure linings (valid), moving parts of mats (valid if not in contact), and turbans with discarded impure ends (valid if the impure part does not move with the wearer).
The key distinction is whether the impure part is 'worn' (multabis) or separate in effect.
5
Note the practical consequence
Under the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, a person may pray directly on such a surface without removing the impurity from the bottom. Under Abu Yusuf's view, the impurity must be removed or a separate pure barrier used.
Both views are considered relied-upon by later scholars; some early authorities gave fatwa with Abu Hanifa, others with Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter on matters related to conditions and their branches. 'Prayer is valid on a felt (libd) with the top surface pure and the bottom impure, because due to its thickness it is like two garments. Similarly, a thick clod that can be split into two halves: if its bottom is impure, prayer on its pure top is valid according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf, because it is like two things one above the other. Prayer is valid on a garment whose outer is pure and lining is impure if it is not quilted, because it is like two garments on top of each other. Prayer is valid on a pure corner of a garment even if the impure corner moves due to its movement, because he is not wearing it, according to the correct view. If one end of his turban becomes impure, and he discards it and keeps the pure part on his head, and the impure part does not move with his movement, his prayer is valid because he is not in contact with it. If it moves, from a mat or matting.' Commentary: 'His saying: (and other than it is a condition for the continuity of its validity, like placing the recitation in the standing, and the bowing after it, and the prostration after it, and being awake, and Allah knows best. Chapter on matters related to conditions and its branches: the connection of the branches to what precedes is from the connection of the specific to the general. His saying: (i.e. becomes valid) there is no reason to change the meaning of permissibility because there is no prohibition in that. His saying: (on a felt etc.) meaning every substance that has a thick body suitable to be split into two halves, like stone, brick, and mat, as in al-Badā'i', al-Khāniyya, and Muniya al-Muṣallī and others. His saying: (and a clod) is a conjunction to felt, and the kāf is a noun meaning 'like', and like what is mentioned if the stuffing is impure and both sides are pure, and likewise the skin of a sheep with its wool having excessive impurity, as in al-Badā'i' and al-Khulāṣa. His saying: (according to them contrary to Abu Yusuf) with the first view, Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Iskāfī gave the fatwa, and with the second, Shaykh Abu Hafs al-Kabīr gave the fatwa, so they are two preferred opinions. His saying: if it is not quilted, this detail is followed by the author of al-Majma', and he mentioned that it is correct. The meaning of 'makhīt' (stitched) is non-quilted, and 'muḍarrab' (quilted) is that whose sides are sewn and its middle is sewn quiltedly. In al-Qahistānī: 'It is preferable that he prays with purity on a garment like a cloak whose lining is impure, and he stands on its back prostating on its tail.' End. His saying: (because he is not in contact with it) and because the mat and the like are like the ground, so only the purity of the place of the worshipper is required, as in al-Khāniyya.'
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This section of al-Tahtawi's Hashiya addresses a practical issue: whether prayer is valid on a surface that is partially impure. The key principle is that if the impurity is on a separate layer that does not come into contact with the worshipper, it is excused. The rule is built on the analogy to two separate garments. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that prayer is valid; Abu Yusuf disagrees. The commentary explains that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) varies—some early scholars preferred Abu Hanifa's view, others Abu Yusuf's. The passage also covers cases like clothing with impure lining, moving parts, and turbans. The distinction between quilted (muḍarrab) and non-quilted (ghayr muḍarrab) garments is important: a quilted garment is treated as a single unit, so impurity in the lining affects the prayer; a non-quilted garment is like two separate layers, so only the layer in contact matters.

Key Terms
اللبد (al-libd): Felt, a thick matted fabric used as a prayer mat.
المضرب (al-muḍarrab): A quilted garment, with stitches through both layers, making it effectively one layer.
غير المضرب (ghayr al-muḍarrab): Non-quilted garment, where layers are separate, like two independent garments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the impurity is not in contact with the worshipper's body.
B) Because felt absorbs impurity and neutralises it.
C) Because the thickness makes it like two separate garments, so only the top layer matters.
D) Because the impurity is on the bottom, which is not considered part of the prayer space.

Key Takeaway
Prayer on a thick substance with a pure top and impure bottom is valid because the thickness creates a functional separation, making it analogous to two garments, and this principle extends to various related cases.

Rulings for a Naked Person's Salah
Explains recommended and valid postures for a naked prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended and valid postures for a naked person performing salah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A naked person's salah is valid standing or sitting, but the recommended posture is sitting with gestures and legs extended.

In the Hanafi school, necessity (darurah) allows flexibility in prayer postures when one is unable to cover properly. This lesson addresses the case of a person who has no clothing and must pray naked. The text from Maraqi al-Falah outlines which postures are valid and which is recommended, along with the reasoning behind the preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended posture
Read the first part: it is recommended (nudiba) for the naked person to pray sitting with gesture (ima') and legs extended towards the qibla.
This is the preferred view.
2
Identify valid alternative postures
The text states that if he prays standing with gesture, or standing with actual bowing and prostration, it is valid (sahh) because the essential pillars are performed.
Any posture that includes the pillars is valid.
3
Understand the reasoning for the recommendation
The recommendation of sitting with legs extended is for better covering. Alternative postures may expose more or conflict with other sunan (e.g., hand placement under navel).
The commentary refines this by discussing the merits of different sitting positions.
4
Note the exceptional case of forgetfulness
If a person prays naked while forgetting that a covering is available, there is a difference of opinion about validity.
This is a separate ruling not fully detailed here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة يستتر بالإليتين وفيه تأمل لأنه يستتر بالفخذين ووضع اليدين فوقهما (وندب صلاة العاري جالساً بالإيماء ماداً رجليه نحو القبلة لما فيه من الستر (فإن صلى) العاري (قائماً بالإيماء أو) قائماً آتياً بالركوع والسجود (صح) لإتيانه بالأركان فيميل إلى أيهما شاء، والأفضل الأول، ولو صلى عارياً ناسياً ساتراً اختلف في صحتها قوله : (يستتر بالإليتين) قيل يستر القبل قال في النهر والظاهر أن الخلاف في الأولوية. قوله : (وفيه تأمل أي في التعليل الثاني. قوله : (لأنه يستتر بالفخذين الخ) يمكن أن يقال معنى كونه لا يستتر بغيره أنه لا يستتر بغير مشقة أي، وستره بالفخذين فيه عسر، وستره باليدين يفوّت عبادة أخرى وهي وضعهما حال القيام الحكمي تحت السرة، فتأمل. قوله : (ماداً رجليه نحو القبلة) هذا ما في الذخيرة، وفي منية المصلي يقعد كما يقعد في الصلاة حال التشهد وعليه ليختلف فيه حال الرجل والمرأة قال في البحر: والذي يظهر ترجيحه وأنه أولى لأنه يحصل به المبالغة في الستر ما لا يحصل بالهيئة الثانية مع خلوها عن فعل ما ليس بأولى. وهو مد رجليه إلى القبلة من غير ضرورة اهـ، والخلاف في الأولوية قوله: (فإن صلى العاري الخ) بقي أمر رابع ذكره في البحر، والنهر، عن ملتقى البحار، وهو الصلاة قاعداً يركع ويسجد .
Book of Prayer: He covers himself with the two buttocks, and there is contemplation because he covers himself with the two thighs and placing the hands above them. (And it is recommended for a naked person to pray sitting with gesture, extending his legs towards the qibla because of the covering it contains. (If) the naked person (prays standing with gesture or standing performing bowing and prostration, it is valid) because he performs the pillars; so he inclines to whichever he wishes, and the first is better. And if a naked person prayed forgetfully while having a covering, there is disagreement about its validity. He said: (He covers himself with the two buttocks); it is said: he covers the private part; he said in al-Nahr: apparently the difference is about priority. He said: (And in it there is contemplation) meaning in the second reasoning. He said: (Because he covers himself with the thighs etc.) It can be said that the meaning of his not covering with other than them is that he does not cover without difficulty, i.e., covering with the thighs involves hardship, and covering with the hands forfeits another act of worship, which is placing them during the standing in the ruling position under the navel, so contemplate. He said: (Extending his legs towards the qibla); this is what is in al-Dhakhira, and in Munyat al-Musalli he sits as one sits in prayer during the tashahhud; and regarding it, there is a difference concerning the case of a man and a woman; he said in al-Bahr: What appears is its preference and that it is more appropriate because it achieves a greater degree of covering that is not achieved by the second posture, and it is free from doing something that is not preferable, namely extending his legs to the qibla without necessity. And the difference is about priority. He said: (If the naked person prays, etc.) There remains a fourth matter mentioned in al-Bahr and al-Nahr from Multaqa al-Bihar, which is praying sitting while bowing and prostrating.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, with commentary (hashiya) by al-Tahtawi. It addresses the prayer of a person who is naked and has no covering. The matn states that such a person should cover himself with his buttocks and thighs, placing his hands over them. However, the commentator notes that there is contemplation about this reasoning. The recommended posture for a naked person is to pray sitting with gestures (ima') while extending his legs towards the qibla, as this provides better covering. If he prays standing with gestures, or standing while performing actual bowing and prostration, the prayer is valid because the essential pillars are performed. The first option (sitting with gestures) is considered better. If a person prays naked but forgets that a covering is available, there is disagreement about the validity of his prayer. The commentary explains various points: the difference of opinion about covering the private part is one of priority; the 'contemplation' refers to the second reasoning; the meaning of not covering with other than the thighs is that covering with the thighs is not difficult, whereas covering with the hands would remove the hands from their recommended position under the navel; there is a difference of opinion about whether the legs should be extended or crossed like in tashahhud, with the preferred view being extension for more covering; and a fourth option is added: praying sitting with actual bowing and prostration.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head or body to indicate bowing and prostration when unable to perform them fully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Lying down with gestures

Key Takeaway
A naked person's salah is valid in multiple postures, but the recommended one is sitting with gestures and legs extended for optimal covering.

Man's 'Awrah: Between Navel and Knee
Ruling with proof defining man's 'awrah and its limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a man's 'awrah, identify the hadith proof for including the knee, and apply the varying levels of strictness for uncovering different body parts.

Core Idea
A man's 'awrah is from navel to knee—the knee is included by precaution and explicit hadith.

The concept of 'awrah is fundamental to salah and everyday conduct. This lesson examines the Hanafi definition of a man's 'awrah, its proofs, and the practical gradient of strictness for different body parts. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the limits and the evidence, including the famous hadith 'The knee is from the 'awrah'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the 'awrah (parts to cover) of a man. The ruling is that covering it is obligatory (fard).
The text specifies that this applies whether the man is free or slave.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Two proofs: a general hadith (or Quranic reference) that 'awrah is between navel and knee, and a specific hadith: 'The knee is from the 'awrah'.
The second hadith is explicit about the knee.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the inclusion of the knee? The phrase 'min al-'awrah' (is from the 'awrah) directly places the knee within the category. Also, the word 'to' (ila) in the limit may include or exclude; here precaution requires inclusion.
The commentator explains that even without the explicit hadith, precaution would include the knee.
4
Note the practical differences (thamarah)
The text describes a gradient of strictness: uncovering the knee requires gentle advice; the thigh requires harsh advice; the private parts require discipline; the area between navel and pubic area is disputed.
This shows that the ruling on 'awrah is not monolithic; different parts have different levels of severity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعورة الرجل) حراً كان أو به رق (ما بين السرة ومنتهى الركبة في ظاهر الرواية سميت عورة لقبح ظهورها وغض الأبصار عنها في اللغة وفي الشريعة ما افترض ستره وحده الشارع بقوله : عورة الرجل ما بين سرته إلى ركبته وبقوله عليه السلام: «الركبة من العورة وتزيد عليه) أي على الرجل الركبة، ثم الباقي على السواء كما في سكب الأنهر وغيره قوله : (وقيل يستر القبل) قال في النهر والظاهر أن الخلاف في الأولوية. قوله : (ما بين السرة) أي ما يحاذي ذلك من سائر الجوانب، وقيل ابتداؤها من السرة، وقيل من المنبت، وفي لفظ الرجل إشارة إلى ان الصبي لميس كذلك. قال في السراج الصغير جداً لا تكون له عورة، ولا بأس بالنظر إليها، ومسها لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقبل ذكري الحسن والحسين في صغرهما، وكان يأخذ أحدهما من ذكره، ويجره والصبي يضحك كذا في الفتاوى اهـ وفي البحر عن الظهيرية، وحكم العورة في الركبة أخف منه في الفخذ وثمرته أنه لو رأى غيره مكشوف الركبة ينكر عليه برفق، ولا ينازعه أن ألح، وان رآه مكشوف الفخذ ينكر عليه بعنف، ولا يضر به إن ألح وإن رآه مكشوف السواة أمره بسترها، وأدبه على ذلك ان ألح وإن رآه مكشوف ما بين السرة إلى العانة ينكر عليه برفق، وينازعه إن ألح ولا يؤدبه فإنه مجتهد فيه لقول الفضلي: إن ذلك ليس بعورة لتعامل العمال بإبداء ذلك وإن كان ضعيفاً قوله : (لقبح ظهورها فهي من العور، وهو النقص، والقبح، والعيب. قوله : (إلى ركبتيه) وجه الإستدلال منه أن كلمة إلى للغاية فالركبة غاية، والغاية قد تدخل، وقد تخرج والموضع موضع احتياط فحكمنا بدخولها احتياطاً ولأن الغاية تدخل في المغيا [؟] بالي كما هو في آية الوضوء وهذا بقطع النظر عما يؤخذ من الحديث الثاني، وإلا فهو صريح في دخولها .
And the 'awrah of a man, whether free or slave, is between the navel and the end of the knee in the apparent narration. It is called 'awrah because of the ugliness of its appearance and the lowering of gazes from it in language, and in Shariah it is that which the Lawgiver has made obligatory to cover, delimiting it by His saying: 'The 'awrah of a man is between his navel and his knee' and by his statement, peace be upon him: 'The knee is from the 'awrah.' And it adds to him, i.e., to the man, the knee, then the rest is the same as in Saka al-Anhur and others. He said: (And it is said: he covers the private part). He said in al-Nahr: apparently the difference is about priority. He said: (Between the navel) meaning what is opposite that from all sides, and it is said its beginning is from the navel, and it is said from the hairline, and in the word 'man' there is an indication that a young boy is not like that. He said in al-Siraj: a very young boy has no 'awrah, and there is no harm in looking at it or touching it because the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to kiss the private parts of al-Hasan and al-Husayn when they were small, and he would take one of them by his private part and pull him while the boy laughed, as in al-Fatawa. And in al-Bahr from al-Zahiriyya: the ruling of the 'awrah regarding the knee is lighter than regarding the thigh, and its fruit is that if he sees another person with his knee uncovered, he advises him gently, and does not contend if he persists; if he sees him with his thigh uncovered, he advises him harshly, and it does not harm him if he persists; if he sees him with his private part (anus) uncovered, he orders him to cover it and disciplines him if he persists; if he sees him with what is between the navel and the pubic area uncovered, he advises him gently and contends if he persists but does not discipline him, because there is ijtihad in it due to the statement of al-Fadli: 'That is not 'awrah because of the workers' dealing with exposing it,' although it is weak. He said: (Because of the ugliness of its appearance) so it is from al-'awr, which is defect, ugliness, and fault. He said: (To his knees) The face of reasoning from it is that the word 'to' (ila) indicates a limit, so the knee is the limit, and the limit may be included or excluded, and this is a place of precaution, so we ruled for its inclusion as a precaution, and because the limit is included in the limited according to the [؟] as in the verse of wudu, and this is regardless of what is taken from the second hadith, otherwise it is explicit in its inclusion.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage defines the 'awrah (private parts) of a man from the Hanafi perspective. It is a ruling with proof from both the Quran and Hadith. The matn states that the 'awrah is between the navel and the end of the knee, which is the position in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The commentator explains that the term 'awrah is derived from ugliness and defect. The proof includes a saying of the Prophet: 'The knee is from the 'awrah.' The commentary then discusses the inclusion of the knee: because the word 'to' (ila) in the limit may include or exclude, precaution requires inclusion. The hadith shows that the knee is part of the 'awrah. The commentator also discusses degrees of strictness: uncovering the knee is less severe than the thigh; uncovering the private part (anus) requires harsh action; uncovering between navel and pubic area requires gentler action because some scholars did not consider it 'awrah due to custom. The passage also notes that a very young boy has no 'awrah, citing the Prophet's practice. The overall ruling is that man's 'awrah includes the navel to the knee, with the knee being included as a precaution.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): In this text, the part of the body that must be covered in prayer and outside it, defined as between navel and knee for men.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Quranic verse on covering
B) The hadith 'The knee is from the 'awrah'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Custom of the workers

Key Takeaway
The knee is part of the man's 'awrah in Hanafi school, supported by explicit hadith and precautionary principle.

The ‘Awrah of Women: Slave and Free – Hanafi Definition
Defines 'awrah for slave and free women with intra-madhhab refinements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ‘awrah of a free woman and a slave woman according to the Hanafi school, and identify the most sound view regarding face, hands, forearm, feet, and hair.

Core Idea
A free woman’s ‘awrah is all but face and hands; a slave woman’s ‘awrah is only the belly and back.

This lesson examines the Hanafi definition of ‘awrah for women, both free and slave, as elaborated in Hashiya al-Tahtawi. The passage clarifies disputed points within the school, such as the status of the forearms, feet, and hair, and establishes the mufta bihi positions. Understanding these distinctions is essential for valid prayer and correct rulings on covering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Note the distinction between free woman (hurra) and slave woman (ama) – their ‘awrah differ significantly.
The text lists types of slaves: qinn, umm walad, mudabbara, makataba, mustasa'a.
2
State the ruling for each
Free woman: all body except face and hands (most sound). Slave woman: belly and back only.
The text says 'in the most sound' for free woman; for slave it is from Abu Hanifa.
3
Identify disputed points
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on forearms (not ‘awrah according to Abu Hanifa, but ‘awrah in apparent narration) and feet (two narrations; most sound: not ‘awrah in prayer). Hair: ‘awrah even if hanging.
The text cites Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and later authorities.
4
Locate the evidence
The author references the practice of ‘Umar (hitting slave women to uncover) and the wudu verse (for face and hands).
The dalil is implicit; the commentary uses qiyas and practice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text marks 'in the most sound' and 'upon it is the fatwa' for free woman's face/hands exception, hair as ‘awrah, and feet not ‘awrah in prayer.
For slave women, the position is from Abu Hanifa with no dispute on the basic ruling.

He said: (and it is not permissible to look at it when cut off from her in the most sound view) and it is said: it is permissible, just as it is permissible to look at her saliva and blood.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage defines the 'awrah (private parts) for two categories of women: slave women (ama) and free women (hurra). For a slave woman, the 'awrah is only her belly and back. Her chest, breasts, and other parts are not 'awrah due to hardship, as she often works and serves. This is the view of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider her free regarding debt. The commentator notes that the side is considered part of the belly. For a free woman, all of her body is 'awrah except her face and hands (including both sides). The most sound view is that the face and hands are not 'awrah, though it is recommended for a young woman to cover her face if there is fear of temptation. There is a difference of opinion about the forearm: in the apparent narration it is 'awrah, but Abu Hanifa said it is not, and some chose his view due to need. The feet are not 'awrah in the most sound view due to necessity, but they are 'awrah outside prayer in some narrations. A free woman's hair is 'awrah, and uncovering a quarter of it invalidates prayer. Looking at a cut-off part of her is not allowed in the most sound view. The commentary discusses various details: the beard? (not present), the case of an ambiguous hermaphrodite, the change in ruling for covering slave women in modern times due to corruption, and the distinction between 'awrah and permissibility of looking. The overall ruling: free woman's 'awrah is all except face and hands; slave woman's 'awrah is belly and back only.

Key Terms
أمة (ama): A female slave, includes qinn, umm walad, mudabbara, makataba, mustasa'a.
حرة (hurra): A free woman; her entire body except face and hands is 'awrah.
عورة (awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer and before non-mahram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between free and slave women in 'awrah, with the most relied-upon position being that a free woman's 'awrah excludes her face and hands, while a slave woman's 'awrah is limited to the belly and back.

The Female Voice: ‘Awrah or Not?
Critical refinement of the female voice ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the female voice as ‘awrah and distinguish between normal speech and modulated voice, and evaluate the effect on salah.

Core Idea
A woman's voice is not ‘awrah in itself; only softening and prolonging it to attract men is prohibited.

This passage clarifies a common misunderstanding: when earlier scholars said 'a woman's voice is ‘awrah,' they did not mean normal speech. Rather, they referred to a deliberately alluring tone. The commentary presents two views—one that such recitation invalidates prayer, and another that it is merely forbidden but does not invalidate. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the rules of covering and prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim
The matn states that her voice is ‘awrah, referencing the adhan section.
2
Recognize the clarification
The author explains that the intended meaning is not mere speech, but softening and prolonging the voice (tamteet and taleen).
This distinction is critical.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf
Al-Fath suggests that if a woman recites loudly in prayer, the prayer becomes invalid. Ibn Amir Haj counters that the voice is not ‘awrah but leads to fitna, and this view is relied upon in al-Nahr.
Both views are within the Hanafi school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that normal speech is permissible; raising the voice in an alluring manner is haram but does not invalidate prayer by itself (though it may lead to fitna).
The prayer is valid but the act is sinful.
5
Apply to prayer context
If a woman recites aloud with a sweet, prolonged tone deliberately to attract men, her prayer is still valid according to the preponderant view, but she commits a sin.
The invalidating view is cautionary but not the madhhab position.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it has preceded in the Adhan that her voice is 'awrah, and the intended meaning is not merely her speech, but what results from its softening and prolongation, it is not permissible to hear it. And uncovering a quarter of a limb from the 'awrah limbs, whether thick or thin, from a man or woman, prevents the validity of prayer with the presence of a covering, not less than a quarter. And the knee with the thigh is one limb in the soundest opinion. And the ankle of a woman with her shin, and her ear separately from her head, and her breast that is sagging, but if it is prominent, it follows her chest. And the penis by itself and the testicles without being attached to it in the correct opinion. And what is between the navel and the pubis is a complete limb with the sides of the body. And every buttock is 'awrah. His saying: (that her voice (is 'awrah) is what is in al-Nawazil, and he followed it in al-Muhit and al-Kafi where they reasoned that she does not raise voice in talbiyah because her voice is 'awrah. He said in al-Fath: and on this, if it is said that if she raises voice in recitation in prayer, the prayer becomes invalid, it would be plausible, but Ibn Amir Haj said: the more correct is that it is not 'awrah, but rather it leads to fitna, and he relied on it in al-Nahr... (the commentary continues). His saying: (and uncovering a quarter of a limb etc.) this is with regard to prayer, otherwise the prohibition of uncovering and looking is not restricted to a quarter of a limb, but little and much are the same as in Tuhfat al-Akhyar. His saying: (thick or thin) this division is with regard to looking, otherwise the ruling in prayer is uniform. His saying: (prevents the validity of prayer) i.e., if it is the duration of performing a rukn according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, they consider the actual performance of the rukn, and the chosen is the saying of Abu Yusuf for caution as in al-Halabi. In Munyat al-Musalli, he added considering the performance of the rukn with its sunnah. Its commentator Burhan al-Halabi said: that is the measure of three glorifications. Ibn Amir Haj said: this is a strange restriction, but its reasoning is close. Some restricted the uncovering to be without his action, but if he uncovers it by his action, it invalidates immediately without dispute, Qahistani from al-Munya, and al-Bahr attributed it to al-Quniya, and the author of al-Durr followed it. He said in al-Bahr: this is a strange restriction, and the school's position is absolute. And know that much uncovering in a short time does not prevent, like little in much, and much in much prevents. And the consideration of a quarter of a limb is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Abu Yusuf considered the uncovering of the majority, and regarding half there are two narrations from him as in al-Multaqa. His saying: (with the presence of a covering) he restricted it because one who lacks it prays naked. His saying: (and the knee with the thigh is a limb) and it is not a separate limb in reality, as it is the joint of the thigh and shin bones. I say: and similarly the elbow should follow the upper arm, and the wrist follow the forearm, said by some virtuous scholars. His saying: (and the ankle of a woman with her shin) i.e., a limb, and so on for what follows. His saying: (and the testicles without being attached to it) for they together are one limb, and the correct is al-unthayan with alif. His saying: (and every buttock is 'awrah).
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct but related rulings. First, the revocalization of the matn's statement that a woman's voice is 'awrah. The author clarifies that this does not mean normal speech, but rather when the voice is softened and prolonged (tamteet and taleen). The commentary cites sources that state her voice is 'awrah, and extends that if she recites loudly in prayer, her prayer would become invalid. However, Ibn Amir Haj argued it is not 'awrah but leads to fitna, and this view was relied upon in al-Nahr. The practical consequence is that normal speech is permissible, but raising the voice in a alluring manner is not. The second ruling is on uncovering a quarter of a limb in prayer. The matn states that uncovering a quarter of an 'awrah limb invalidates prayer, provided a covering is available (otherwise one prays naked). The commentary explains that the definition of 'what is a limb' includes: the knee and thigh together as one limb, a woman's ankle with her shin, the ear separately from the head, a sagging breast (but a prominent breast follows the chest), the penis alone and the testicles without the penis are one limb in the correct view. The area between navel and pubis is a complete limb including the sides. Every buttock is 'awrah. The commentary then discusses the quantity: the invalidation occurs if the uncovering lasts for the duration of a rukn (estimated as three tasbihat, according to Abu Yusuf's view which is chosen for caution). If the uncovering is by one's own action, it invalidates immediately. The author also notes that uncovering a small amount in a short time does not invalidate, but much in much does. There is also discussion on the difference between the ruling for prayer and for looking: outside of prayer, even a small amount is forbidden to look at.

Key Terms
صوت المرأة (sawt al-mar'ah): The female voice considered 'awrah only when modulated in a way that attracts men.
تمطيط وتليين (tamteet wa taleen): Prolonging and softening the voice to make it attractive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view, what is the ruling on a woman reciting Quran aloud in prayer with a soft, sweet voice?
A) Her prayer is invalid and she commits a sin.
B) Her prayer is valid but she commits a sin.
C) Her prayer is valid and she does not sin.
D) Her prayer is invalid but she does not sin.

Key Takeaway
A woman's voice is not inherently 'awrah; only an alluring tone is prohibited, and prayer remains valid.

Uncovering a Quarter of a Limb in Salah
Ruling with proof and limb definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that uncovering a quarter of an ‘awrah limb for the duration of a rukn invalidates prayer, and identify which body parts constitute a single limb.

Core Idea
Uncovering a quarter of a limb for the time of three tasbihat invalidates prayer.

The second part of this passage details a key condition for the validity of prayer: covering the ‘awrah. The matn states that uncovering a quarter of a limb (rub‘ ‘udw) invalidates prayer, provided a covering is available. The commentary then defines what constitutes one limb for this ruling—knee and thigh together, ankle with shin, etc.—and discusses the required duration. There is also an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the exact threshold. Mastering these details is crucial for correctly assessing when prayer becomes invalid due to exposure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn says: 'uncovering a quarter of a limb from the ‘awrah limbs prevents the validity of prayer with the presence of a covering, not less than a quarter.'
This is the general rule.
2
Understand the duration condition
The commentary explains that the uncovering must last for the duration of performing a rukn (approx. three tasbihat). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require the actual performance; the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is Abu Yusuf's opinion for caution.
Three tasbihat is the measure.
3
Define what constitutes a limb
The text gives specific rulings: knee+thigh is one limb; a woman's ankle+shin; ear separately; sagging breast (prominent breast follows chest); penis alone (testicles with it or separate? The sound opinion: penis alone and testicles alone? Actually 'al-dhakr bi-infiraadihi wa al-unthayayn bi-la dammihi ilayhi' means penis by itself and testicles without being attached to it are considered? The commentary says testicles together are one limb. Also area between navel and pubis is one complete limb including sides; each buttock is ‘awrah.
These definitions affect the quarter calculation.
4
Account for exceptional cases
If the uncovering is by one's own action, it invalidates immediately. If a large area is uncovered briefly, it does not invalidate; if a large area for long, it does. The quarter rule applies to passive uncovering.
Self-caused exposure is more severe.

And it has preceded in the Adhan that her voice is 'awrah, and the intended meaning is not merely her speech, but what results from its softening and prolongation, it is not permissible to hear it. And uncovering a quarter of a limb from the 'awrah limbs, whether thick or thin, from a man or woman, prevents the validity of prayer with the presence of a covering, not less than a quarter. And the knee with the thigh is one limb in the soundest opinion. And the ankle of a woman with her shin, and her ear separately from her head, and her breast that is sagging, but if it is prominent, it follows her chest. And the penis by itself and the testicles without being attached to it in the correct opinion. And what is between the navel and the pubis is a complete limb with the sides of the body. And every buttock is 'awrah. His saying: (that her voice (is 'awrah) is what is in al-Nawazil, and he followed it in al-Muhit and al-Kafi where they reasoned that she does not raise voice in talbiyah because her voice is 'awrah. He said in al-Fath: and on this, if it is said that if she raises voice in recitation in prayer, the prayer becomes invalid, it would be plausible, but Ibn Amir Haj said: the more correct is that it is not 'awrah, but rather it leads to fitna, and he relied on it in al-Nahr... (the commentary continues). His saying: (and uncovering a quarter of a limb etc.) this is with regard to prayer, otherwise the prohibition of uncovering and looking is not restricted to a quarter of a limb, but little and much are the same as in Tuhfat al-Akhyar. His saying: (thick or thin) this division is with regard to looking, otherwise the ruling in prayer is uniform. His saying: (prevents the validity of prayer) i.e., if it is the duration of performing a rukn according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, they consider the actual performance of the rukn, and the chosen is the saying of Abu Yusuf for caution as in al-Halabi. In Munyat al-Musalli, he added considering the performance of the rukn with its sunnah. Its commentator Burhan al-Halabi said: that is the measure of three glorifications. Ibn Amir Haj said: this is a strange restriction, but its reasoning is close. Some restricted the uncovering to be without his action, but if he uncovers it by his action, it invalidates immediately without dispute, Qahistani from al-Munya, and al-Bahr attributed it to al-Quniya, and the author of al-Durr followed it. He said in al-Bahr: this is a strange restriction, and the school's position is absolute. And know that much uncovering in a short time does not prevent, like little in much, and much in much prevents. And the consideration of a quarter of a limb is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Abu Yusuf considered the uncovering of the majority, and regarding half there are two narrations from him as in al-Multaqa. His saying: (with the presence of a covering) he restricted it because one who lacks it prays naked. His saying: (and the knee with the thigh is a limb) and it is not a separate limb in reality, as it is the joint of the thigh and shin bones. I say: and similarly the elbow should follow the upper arm, and the wrist follow the forearm, said by some virtuous scholars. His saying: (and the ankle of a woman with her shin) i.e., a limb, and so on for what follows. His saying: (and the testicles without being attached to it) for they together are one limb, and the correct is al-unthayan with alif. His saying: (and every buttock is 'awrah).
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct but related rulings. First, the revocalization of the matn's statement that a woman's voice is 'awrah. The author clarifies that this does not mean normal speech, but rather when the voice is softened and prolonged (tamteet and taleen). The commentary cites sources that state her voice is 'awrah, and extends that if she recites loudly in prayer, her prayer would become invalid. However, Ibn Amir Haj argued it is not 'awrah but leads to fitna, and this view was relied upon in al-Nahr. The practical consequence is that normal speech is permissible, but raising the voice in a alluring manner is not. The second ruling is on uncovering a quarter of a limb in prayer. The matn states that uncovering a quarter of an 'awrah limb invalidates prayer, provided a covering is available (otherwise one prays naked). The commentary explains that the definition of 'what is a limb' includes: the knee and thigh together as one limb, a woman's ankle with her shin, the ear separately from the head, a sagging breast (but a prominent breast follows the chest), the penis alone and the testicles without the penis are one limb in the correct view. The area between navel and pubis is a complete limb including the sides. Every buttock is 'awrah. The commentary then discusses the quantity: the invalidation occurs if the uncovering lasts for the duration of a rukn (estimated as three tasbihat, according to Abu Yusuf's view which is chosen for caution). If the uncovering is by one's own action, it invalidates immediately. The author also notes that uncovering a small amount in a short time does not invalidate, but much in much does. There is also discussion on the difference between the ruling for prayer and for looking: outside of prayer, even a small amount is forbidden to look at.

Key Terms
ربع عضو (rub‘ ‘udw): A quarter of a limb (of the 'awrah) is the threshold that, if uncovered for the duration of a rukn, invalidates prayer.
أداء ركن (ada' rukn): The duration of performing a pillar of prayer, including its sunnah, estimated as three tasbihat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
During a woman's prayer, a quarter of her ankle (with shin) becomes exposed for the length of two tasbihat. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) Prayer is invalid because a quarter of a limb is exposed.
B) Prayer is invalid because the ankle and shin are separate limbs.
C) Prayer is valid because the exposure lasted less than a rukn.
D) Prayer is valid because the ankle is not 'awrah.

Key Takeaway
Prayer becomes invalid only when a quarter of an ‘awrah limb is uncovered for the duration of a rukn (three tasbihat).

Rukhsah of Not Facing Qibla: Excuses and the Qadir bi Qudrat al-Ghayr Dispute
Ruling on exemptions from facing qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the valid excuses for not facing the qibla in prayer, explain the concept of qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr, and state the mufta bihi position on whether such a person must face the qibla with help.

Core Idea
Genuine hardship excuses facing qibla; getting help to face it is disputed.

This lesson examines the specific scenarios where the obligation to face the qibla is lifted. The Hanafi school provides detailed excuses ranging from illness to fear of an enemy. We also explore an intra-madhhab dispute about a person who can only face the qibla with assistance—does that ability count? The mufta bihi position is that such a person must seek help and face the qibla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Facing qibla is wajib in prayer. The text lists conditions under which this obligation is lifted.
The excuses are all cases of genuine hardship.
2
List the specific excuses
From the text: illness, fear of drowning on a plank, inability to dismount from an unruly animal, old age requiring help to mount, fear of human or beast enemy for self/property, intense fear in battle, fleeing from enemy while riding.
These excuses allow praying towards the direction of ability.
3
Understand 'qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr'
This is a person who can face qibla only with another's help. Imam Abu Hanifa says such a person is not considered able; the Sahibayn say he is able.
If no helper is found, all agree the prayer is valid without facing qibla.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa: the person does not have to seek help. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: he must seek help and face qibla.
The dispute is based on different interpretations of 'ability'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn: the person must face qibla with help, for caution.
No explicit tarjih in the text, but later Hanafi works adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجز عن استقبال القبلة) بنفسه (لمرض) أو خشية غرق، وهو على خشبة (أو عجز عن النزول) بنفسه (عن دابته) وهي سائرة أو كانت جموحاً، أو كان شيخاً كبيراً لا يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين (أو خاف عدوا) آدمياً، أو سبعاً على نفسه أو دابته أو ماله أو أمانته أو اشتد الخوف لقتال، أو هرب من عدو راكباً فقبلته جهة قدرته للضرورة (و) قبلة الخائف جهة (أمنه) ولو خاف أن يراه العدو إن صلى مضطجعاً بالإيماء إلى جهة أمنه والقادر بقدرة الغير ليس قادراً عند الإمام خلافاً لهما وإذا لم يجد أحداً فلا خلاف في الصحة ومن اشتبهت عليه جهة (القبلة ولم يكن عنده مخبر من أهل المكان ولا ممن له علم أو سأله فلم يخبره (ولا محراب) بالمحل (تحرى) أي اجتهد وهو بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود ولو سجدة تلاوة ولا يجوز التحري مع
صوابه عضو كما قاله السيد قوله : (أو خشية غرق أو حصول ضرر شديد عند الإستقبال أفاد الشرح قوله : (وهي سائرة قيد اتفاقي ولذا لم يذكره السيد قوله : (لا يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين) راجع إلى المسألتين. قوله : (أو) هرب من عدوّ راكباً قيد بقوله راكباً لأن لو هرب ماشياً لا تجوز صلاته قوله فقبلته جهة قدرته فيومي على الدابة واقفة ان قدر وإلا فسائرة، ويتوجه إلى القبلة إن قدر وإلا فلا وهذا في الفرض قوله : (والقادر الخ) قال في الشرح ، وقيدنا بالعجز عن الاستقبال، والنزول بنفسه لأن القادر الخ فهو بمنزلة التعليل لقوله ومن عجز إلخ المقيد بقوله بنفسه. قوله : (ومن اشتبهت عليه (القبلة بأن انطمست أعلامها وأما إذا كانت السماء مصحية مثلاً، وهو لا يعرف الأدلة مع ظهورها فهل يجوز له التحري، ويعذر بالجهل، قال بعضهم: لا، ولا وقال ظهير الدين المرغيناني: يجوز قال في الجوهر وظاهر كلام القدوري يشير إليه .ا.هـ. قوله: (ولم يكن عنده مخبر) قال في الجوهرية وحد الحضرة أي المعبر عنها هنا بعند أن يكون بحيث لو صاح سمعه ويقبل فيها قول العدل ذكره ابن أمير حاج، ولو كان عبداً أو أمة ويتحرى في خبر الفاسق والمستور ثم يعمل بغالب ظنه كما في حظر الدر المختار قوله : (أو سأله فلم يخبره) الذي هو من أهل المكان أو الذي عنده علم وإن لم يكن من أهله. قوله: (ولو سجدة تلاوة أي ولو كان المتحري فيه سجدة تلاوة، ومثلها صلاة الجنازة كما في الجوهرة، ويجب الأخذ بقول المخبر العدل، وإن خالف رأيه لأن الأخبار أعلى من الحري، وفي غاية البيان والعناية أنه يستحب الأخبار قوله : (ولا يجوز التحري مع وضع المحاريب) لأنها من جملة الأدلة خصوصاً محراب المدينة الشريفة لأنه موضوع بالوحي،
And the one who is incapable of facing the qibla by himself due to illness, or fear of drowning while on a plank, or is incapable of descending by himself from his riding animal while it is moving or is unruly, or is a very old man who cannot mount except with assistance, or fears an enemy, human or beast, for himself, his riding animal, his property, or his trust, or fear becomes intense due to fighting, or flees from an enemy while riding, then his qibla is the direction of his ability due to necessity. And the qibla of the fearful person is the direction of his safety, even if he fears that the enemy will see him if he prays lying down, gesturing toward the direction of his safety. The one who is able through the ability of another is not considered able according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions. And if he does not find anyone, there is no disagreement on validity. And the one for whom the direction of the qibla is ambiguous, and he has no informant from the people of the place nor from those who have knowledge, or he asks and they do not inform him, and there is no mihrab in the location, then he performs ijtihad (tahari), which is exerting effort to achieve the goal, even if it is for a prostration of recitation. And ijtihad is not permissible when mihrabs are present. ... His statement: (or fearing drowning or severe harm when facing the qibla) the sharh explained. His statement: (while it is moving) is an accidental restriction, hence al-Sayyid did not mention it. His statement: (cannot mount except with assistance) refers to both issues. His statement: (or) flees from an enemy while riding, restricted by 'while riding' because if he flees on foot, his prayer is not valid. His statement: 'then his qibla is the direction of his ability' so he gestures on the riding animal while stationary if possible, otherwise while moving, and he faces the qibla if possible, otherwise not, and this is in the obligatory prayer. His statement: (and the able etc.) He said in the sharh: We restricted by inability to face and descend by himself because the one able... so it is like a reasoning for the statement 'and the one who is incapable' restricted by 'by himself'. His statement: (and the one for whom the qibla is ambiguous) because its signs are obliterated. As for when the sky is clear for example, and he does not know the evidence despite their appearance, is ijtihad permissible for him and is he excused due to ignorance? Some said no, and no. Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani said: it is permissible. He said in al-Jawhar: And the apparent statement of al-Quduri indicates it. End quote. His statement: (and he has no informant) He said in al-Jawhariyyah: The limit of presence, i.e., what is expressed here by 'with him', is that he would hear him if he called out. The statement of a just person is accepted in it, as Ibn Amir Haj mentioned, even if he is a slave or a slave girl. And he performs ijtihad regarding the report of a sinful or inconspicuous (mastur) person, then acts on his predominant opinion, as in Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar. His statement: (or he asks and they do not inform him) who is from the people of the place or who has knowledge, even if not from its people. His statement: (even if it is a prostration of recitation) meaning even if what is being investigated by ijtihad is a prostration of recitation, and similarly the funeral prayer, as in al-Jawharah. And it is obligatory to accept the statement of a just informant, even if it contradicts his own opinion, because reports are higher than ijtihad. In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Inayah, it is recommended to inform. His statement: (and ijtihad is not permissible when mihrabs are placed) because they are among the pieces of evidence, especially the mihrab of the noble city (Medina) because it is established by revelation.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi deals with the rukhsah (concession) of not facing the qibla due to genuine incapacity, and the method of determining the qibla when its direction is unknown. The matn lists excuses: illness, fear of drowning, inability to dismount from an unruly animal, old age requiring help, fear of enemy (human or beast), intense fear in battle, or fleeing from an enemy while riding. In such cases, the person prays facing whatever direction they can manage. If fleeing, one gestures towards the direction of safety, even if lying down. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa says that one who can only face qibla with another's help is not considered able (so he prays toward his ability), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider him able and require him to face qibla with help. If no helper exists, all agree on validity without facing qibla. The second part deals with ambiguity of the qibla: if one cannot determine the direction (no signs, no informant, no mihrab), he must perform ijtihad (tahari) by exerting effort. This applies even for a sajdah tilawah or janazah prayer. If a just informant is available, his statement must be accepted over one's own ijtihad. If the informant is sinful or of unknown reliability, one may still perform ijtihad but acts on predominant opinion. The commentary notes an exception: if mihrabs (prayer niches) are present, especially in Medina's mosque, ijtihad is not allowed because they are established by revelation or strong evidence. There is also a discussion about whether ijtihad is allowed when the sky is clear (and thus qibla can be determined by celestial signs) but the person is ignorant of the signs; Marghinani permits it, while others say no.

Key Terms
تحري (tahari): Ijtihad to determine qibla direction when ambiguous.
قادر بقدرة الغير (qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr): One who can only face qibla with another's help.
محراب (mihrab): Niche in mosque indicating qibla. Prevents ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is a valid excuse to not face the qibla in prayer?
A) Being in a slow-moving vehicle
B) Fear of an enemy for one's property
C) Dislike of turning around
D) The presence of a mihrab

Key Takeaway
Genuine hardship from specific excuses lifts the obligation to face qibla; the mufta bihi on qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr requires seeking help.

Ijtihad for Qibla: Conditions and Method
Ruling on ijtihad for qibla when direction is ambiguous

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make ijtihad for qibla obligatory, explain why ijtihad is prohibited when a mihrab or reliable informant is present, and apply the ruling to cases of sajdah tilawah and janazah.

Core Idea
Ijtihad for qibla is only when all reliable means fail.

When the direction of the qibla is unknown, a person must exert effort to determine it. This lesson explains the conditions under which ijtihad becomes obligatory, the types of informants whose reports are accepted, and the rule that ijtihad is not permitted when a mihrab or a just informant is available. The Hanafi school also clarifies that ijtihad is required even for prostration of recitation and funeral prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify when ijtihad is required
Ijtihad is wajib when the qibla is ambiguous and there is no informant from the local people or a knowledgeable person, and no mihrab.
The text says: 'wa man ishtabahat alayhi al-qibla... tahara'.
2
Define the informant conditions
A reliable informant is one who is just ('adl) and present within earshot. If the informant is sinful (fasiq) or of unknown status (mastur), one may still perform ijtihad and act on predominant opinion.
The report of a just person must be accepted over one's own ijtihad.
3
Understand the role of the mihrab
If a mihrab exists, ijtihad is not allowed because it is a definitive indicator, especially in Medina's mosque based on revelation.
Mihrabs are considered stronger than one's ijtihad.
4
Note the scope of ijtihad
Ijtihad applies even for sajdah tilawah and janazah prayer, not only for obligatory prayers.
The text explicitly says 'even if it is for a prostration of recitation'.
5
Consider the dispute on clear skies
If the sky is clear but the person does not know the celestial signs, some scholars say ijtihad is not allowed, but al-Marghinani permits it.
The mufta bihi is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجز عن استقبال القبلة) بنفسه (لمرض) أو خشية غرق، وهو على خشبة (أو عجز عن النزول) بنفسه (عن دابته) وهي سائرة أو كانت جموحاً، أو كان شيخاً كبيراً لا يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين (أو خاف عدوا) آدمياً، أو سبعاً على نفسه أو دابته أو ماله أو أمانته أو اشتد الخوف لقتال، أو هرب من عدو راكباً فقبلته جهة قدرته للضرورة (و) قبلة الخائف جهة (أمنه) ولو خاف أن يراه العدو إن صلى مضطجعاً بالإيماء إلى جهة أمنه والقادر بقدرة الغير ليس قادراً عند الإمام خلافاً لهما وإذا لم يجد أحداً فلا خلاف في الصحة ومن اشتبهت عليه جهة (القبلة ولم يكن عنده مخبر من أهل المكان ولا ممن له علم أو سأله فلم يخبره (ولا محراب) بالمحل (تحرى) أي اجتهد وهو بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود ولو سجدة تلاوة ولا يجوز التحري مع
صوابه عضو كما قاله السيد قوله : (أو خشية غرق أو حصول ضرر شديد عند الإستقبال أفاد الشرح قوله : (وهي سائرة قيد اتفاقي ولذا لم يذكره السيد قوله : (لا يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين) راجع إلى المسألتين. قوله : (أو) هرب من عدوّ راكباً قيد بقوله راكباً لأن لو هرب ماشياً لا تجوز صلاته قوله فقبلته جهة قدرته فيومي على الدابة واقفة ان قدر وإلا فسائرة، ويتوجه إلى القبلة إن قدر وإلا فلا وهذا في الفرض قوله : (والقادر الخ) قال في الشرح ، وقيدنا بالعجز عن الاستقبال، والنزول بنفسه لأن القادر الخ فهو بمنزلة التعليل لقوله ومن عجز إلخ المقيد بقوله بنفسه. قوله : (ومن اشتبهت عليه (القبلة بأن انطمست أعلامها وأما إذا كانت السماء مصحية مثلاً، وهو لا يعرف الأدلة مع ظهورها فهل يجوز له التحري، ويعذر بالجهل، قال بعضهم: لا، ولا وقال ظهير الدين المرغيناني: يجوز قال في الجوهر وظاهر كلام القدوري يشير إليه .ا.هـ. قوله: (ولم يكن عنده مخبر) قال في الجوهرية وحد الحضرة أي المعبر عنها هنا بعند أن يكون بحيث لو صاح سمعه ويقبل فيها قول العدل ذكره ابن أمير حاج، ولو كان عبداً أو أمة ويتحرى في خبر الفاسق والمستور ثم يعمل بغالب ظنه كما في حظر الدر المختار قوله : (أو سأله فلم يخبره) الذي هو من أهل المكان أو الذي عنده علم وإن لم يكن من أهله. قوله: (ولو سجدة تلاوة أي ولو كان المتحري فيه سجدة تلاوة، ومثلها صلاة الجنازة كما في الجوهرة، ويجب الأخذ بقول المخبر العدل، وإن خالف رأيه لأن الأخبار أعلى من الحري، وفي غاية البيان والعناية أنه يستحب الأخبار قوله : (ولا يجوز التحري مع وضع المحاريب) لأنها من جملة الأدلة خصوصاً محراب المدينة الشريفة لأنه موضوع بالوحي،
And the one who is incapable of facing the qibla by himself due to illness, or fear of drowning while on a plank, or is incapable of descending by himself from his riding animal while it is moving or is unruly, or is a very old man who cannot mount except with assistance, or fears an enemy, human or beast, for himself, his riding animal, his property, or his trust, or fear becomes intense due to fighting, or flees from an enemy while riding, then his qibla is the direction of his ability due to necessity. And the qibla of the fearful person is the direction of his safety, even if he fears that the enemy will see him if he prays lying down, gesturing toward the direction of his safety. The one who is able through the ability of another is not considered able according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions. And if he does not find anyone, there is no disagreement on validity. And the one for whom the direction of the qibla is ambiguous, and he has no informant from the people of the place nor from those who have knowledge, or he asks and they do not inform him, and there is no mihrab in the location, then he performs ijtihad (tahari), which is exerting effort to achieve the goal, even if it is for a prostration of recitation. And ijtihad is not permissible when mihrabs are present. ... His statement: (or fearing drowning or severe harm when facing the qibla) the sharh explained. His statement: (while it is moving) is an accidental restriction, hence al-Sayyid did not mention it. His statement: (cannot mount except with assistance) refers to both issues. His statement: (or) flees from an enemy while riding, restricted by 'while riding' because if he flees on foot, his prayer is not valid. His statement: 'then his qibla is the direction of his ability' so he gestures on the riding animal while stationary if possible, otherwise while moving, and he faces the qibla if possible, otherwise not, and this is in the obligatory prayer. His statement: (and the able etc.) He said in the sharh: We restricted by inability to face and descend by himself because the one able... so it is like a reasoning for the statement 'and the one who is incapable' restricted by 'by himself'. His statement: (and the one for whom the qibla is ambiguous) because its signs are obliterated. As for when the sky is clear for example, and he does not know the evidence despite their appearance, is ijtihad permissible for him and is he excused due to ignorance? Some said no, and no. Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani said: it is permissible. He said in al-Jawhar: And the apparent statement of al-Quduri indicates it. End quote. His statement: (and he has no informant) He said in al-Jawhariyyah: The limit of presence, i.e., what is expressed here by 'with him', is that he would hear him if he called out. The statement of a just person is accepted in it, as Ibn Amir Haj mentioned, even if he is a slave or a slave girl. And he performs ijtihad regarding the report of a sinful or inconspicuous (mastur) person, then acts on his predominant opinion, as in Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar. His statement: (or he asks and they do not inform him) who is from the people of the place or who has knowledge, even if not from its people. His statement: (even if it is a prostration of recitation) meaning even if what is being investigated by ijtihad is a prostration of recitation, and similarly the funeral prayer, as in al-Jawharah. And it is obligatory to accept the statement of a just informant, even if it contradicts his own opinion, because reports are higher than ijtihad. In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Inayah, it is recommended to inform. His statement: (and ijtihad is not permissible when mihrabs are placed) because they are among the pieces of evidence, especially the mihrab of the noble city (Medina) because it is established by revelation.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi deals with the rukhsah (concession) of not facing the qibla due to genuine incapacity, and the method of determining the qibla when its direction is unknown. The matn lists excuses: illness, fear of drowning, inability to dismount from an unruly animal, old age requiring help, fear of enemy (human or beast), intense fear in battle, or fleeing from an enemy while riding. In such cases, the person prays facing whatever direction they can manage. If fleeing, one gestures towards the direction of safety, even if lying down. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa says that one who can only face qibla with another's help is not considered able (so he prays toward his ability), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider him able and require him to face qibla with help. If no helper exists, all agree on validity without facing qibla. The second part deals with ambiguity of the qibla: if one cannot determine the direction (no signs, no informant, no mihrab), he must perform ijtihad (tahari) by exerting effort. This applies even for a sajdah tilawah or janazah prayer. If a just informant is available, his statement must be accepted over one's own ijtihad. If the informant is sinful or of unknown reliability, one may still perform ijtihad but acts on predominant opinion. The commentary notes an exception: if mihrabs (prayer niches) are present, especially in Medina's mosque, ijtihad is not allowed because they are established by revelation or strong evidence. There is also a discussion about whether ijtihad is allowed when the sky is clear (and thus qibla can be determined by celestial signs) but the person is ignorant of the signs; Marghinani permits it, while others say no.

Key Terms
تحري (tahari): Ijtihad exerted to determine the qibla direction when ambiguous.
محراب (mihrab): Niche in mosque indicating qibla; prevents ijtihad.
مخبر عدل (mukhbir 'adl): A just, reliable informant whose report must be accepted about qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on ijtihad for qibla when a just informant is present?
A) Ijtihad is still permitted but not required.
B) Ijtihad is prohibited; one must follow the informant's report.
C) Ijtihad is required and the informant's report is optional.
D) Ijtihad is only allowed if the informant is unreliable.

Key Takeaway
Ijtihad for qibla is wajib only when all reliable means (informant, mihrab) are absent; the mufta bihi allows ijtihad even in clear skies if the person is ignorant of signs.

Exposure of Awrah and Its Effect on Prayer Validity
Ruling on minimal 'awrah exposure and its invalidation of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi conditions under which exposure of the 'awrah invalidates prayer and apply them to determine the validity of a prayer scenario.

Core Idea
Scattered exposure sums to quarter of smallest limb; if lasting a rukn, prayer invalid.

A common concern during prayer is whether small, brief exposures break the prayer. The Hanafi school provides a precise threshold: not every slip invalidates. This lesson unpacks the two conditions—minimum area and minimum duration—that must both be met for invalidity. Understanding these rules prevents both over-cautious repetition and invalid continuation of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exposed limbs and their areas
Look at all body parts that became uncovered during prayer. Note which limbs are involved and estimate the exposed area on each.
The 'awrah includes the anus; the smallest limb is the one with the least total surface area among those partially exposed.
2
Calculate the total scattered exposure
Sum the exposed areas from all limbs. Do not treat each limb separately; the total is compared to the smallest exposed limb's full area.
For example, 10 cm² on forearm + 15 cm² on thigh = 25 cm² total.
3
Check the area condition
Determine if the total scattered exposure equals or exceeds one quarter (25%) of the smallest exposed limb's total area.
If yes, the area condition is satisfied. If not, prayer remains valid regardless of duration.
4
Check the duration condition
Assess how long the exposure continued. It must last for the time it takes to perform one complete integral (rukn) of prayer, such as one bowing or one prostration.
Brief exposure (e.g., a few seconds) that is shorter than a rukn does not invalidate, even if area condition is met.
5
Apply the ruling
If both conditions are met (area ≥ quarter of smallest limb AND duration ≥ one rukn), the prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated. Otherwise, the prayer remains valid.
The rule applies equally to rich and poor; it is based on the nature of exposure, not financial status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدبر ثالثهما في الصحيح ولو تفرق الانكشاف على أعضاء من العورة وكان جملة ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغر الأعضاء المنكشفة يعني التي انكشف بعضها (منع) صحة الصلاة إن طال زمن الانكشاف بقدر أداء ركن (وإلا ) أي وإن لم يبلغ ربع أصغرها أو بلغ ولم يطل زمن الانكشاف (فلا) يمنع الصحة للضرورة سواء الغني والفقير
And the anus is a third of them in the correct opinion. And if the exposure is scattered over parts of the 'awrah and the total of what was scattered reaches a quarter of the smallest of the exposed limbs (meaning those of which some was exposed), it prevents the validity of the prayer if the time of exposure lasts the duration of performing a rukn. And otherwise (i.e., if it does not reach a quarter of the smallest limb, or reaches it but the exposure time is not long), it does not prevent validity due to necessity, equally for the rich and the poor.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on when the exposure of the 'awrah invalidates prayer. The 'awrah includes the anus as part of it. If the exposed area, even if scattered across multiple limbs, totals at least one-quarter of the smallest limb that was partially uncovered, and this exposure continues for the time it takes to perform one integral (rukn) of prayer (e.g., one bowing or prostration), then the prayer is invalid. Otherwise, the prayer remains valid due to the difficulty of avoiding brief or minimal exposure. This applies to both wealthy and poor individuals, as the ruling is based on the nature of exposure, not financial status.

Key Terms
العورة (al-'awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer; includes the anus.
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of prayer, such as bowing or prostration.
الانكشاف (al-inkishaf): Exposure of the 'awrah during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
