A) Any exposure of the 'awrah
B) Exposure of a quarter of any limb for the duration of a rukn
C) Exposure of the entire 'awrah
D) Exposure lasting more than one minute

Key Takeaway
The validity of prayer after 'awrah exposure depends on two cumulative conditions: total scattered area reaching a quarter of the smallest exposed limb and duration equaling or exceeding one rukn.

Facing Qibla When Incapacitated: Intent and the Helper
Ruling on facing qibla when incapacitated and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Imam Abu Hanifa's view that one who can only face qibla with help is not truly capable, and distinguish it from the Sahibayn's contrary position.

Core Idea
One who can face qibla only with others' help is not truly capable — necessity permits deviation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on facing qibla when genuinely incapacitated, such as due to illness, fear, or inability to dismount. It also explores an internal dispute: does reliance on someone else to face the qibla count as true capacity? The answer affects whether the prayer will be valid without facing qibla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grounds for abandoning qibla
List the scenarios mentioned in the passage: illness, fear of drowning, inability to dismount, fear of enemy or beast, fleeing while riding, etc. Recognize that these are all cases of genuine necessity (darurah).
2
Note the general ruling
For all these cases, the qibla is the direction the person is able to face. The fearful person prays toward his safe direction, even if using gestures while lying down.
3
Focus on the phrase 'al-qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr'
This refers to a person who can only face qibla with the help of another. Understand that this is an edge case: the person is not completely incapacitated but cannot do it alone.
4
State the dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa says such a person is not considered capable (qadir), so he may pray without facing qibla. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is capable, so he must face qibla if help is available.
The root of the disagreement is whether capability through another's power is true capability.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text presents Imam's view first and then says 'khilafan lahuma' (contrary to the two). This suggests the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Imam's view. If no helper is found, all agree the prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجز عن استقبال القبلة بنفسه لمرض أو خشية غرق، وهو على خشبة أو عجز عن النزول بنفسه عن دابته وهي سائرة أو كانت جموحاً، أو كان شيخاً كبيراً لا يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين أو خاف عدوا آدمياً، أو سبعاً على نفسه أو دابته أو ماله أو أمانته أو اشتد الخوف لقتال، أو هرب من عدو راكباً فقبلته جهة قدرته للضرورة و قبلة الخائف جهة أمنه ولو خاف أن يراه العدو إن صلى مضطجعاً بالإيماء إلى جهة أمنه والقادر بقدرة الغير ليس قادراً عند الإمام خلافاً لهما وإذا لم يجد أحداً فلا خلاف في الصحة
And whoever is unable to face the qibla by himself due to illness, or fear of drowning while on a plank, or is unable to dismount by himself from his riding animal while it is moving or is restive, or is a very old man who cannot ride except with help, or fears a human enemy or a predatory animal for himself, his animal, his wealth, or his trust, or fear intensifies for fighting, or flees from an enemy while riding, then his qibla is the direction he is able [to face] due to necessity. And the qibla of the fearful person is the direction of his safety, even if he fears the enemy might see him if he prays lying down with gestures toward his safe direction. And one who is capable through the capability of another is not considered capable according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And if he does not find anyone, then there is no dispute on validity.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage explains when a person may abandon facing the qibla due to genuine incapacity. Grounds include illness, fear of drowning, inability to dismount, fear of an enemy or beast, or fleeing from an enemy while riding. In such cases, one prays toward whatever direction is possible. The fearful person prays toward the direction he feels safe, even if using gestures while lying down. The passage then records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that a person who can only face qibla with the help of another is not considered capable (i.e., he may pray without facing qibla), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider him capable and thus required to face qibla. If no helper is found, all agree that prayer without facing qibla is valid.

Key Terms
القادر بقدرة الغير (al-qadir bi qudrat al-ghayr): One who can face qibla only with the assistance of another person.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity that permits deviation from normal practice.
الخائف (al-kha'if): One in fear of an enemy or danger; may pray toward direction of safety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the status of a person who can only face qibla with the help of another?
A) He is considered capable and must face qibla
B) He is not considered capable and may pray without facing qibla
C) He must postpone prayer until he can face qibla
D) He must pray sitting

Key Takeaway
Necessity permits deviation from facing qibla, but whether reliance on help counts as necessity depends on the imam's definition of capability.

The Validity of Prayer with Taharri and the Hadith Proof
Ruling and evidence for no i'adah after taharri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that no i'adah is required after taharri even if error is discovered later, and explain the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Prayer with taharri is valid even if wrong — no repetition, because qibla admits ijtihad.

The source passage concludes with a powerful legal principle: once you have exerted your best effort (taharri) to find the qibla, your prayer is valid and does not require repetition even if you later discover you were mistaken. This is supported by a specific hadith and a key distinction from taharri in matters of purity. Let us unpack the evidence and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the last part of the passage: 'لا إعادة عليه لو علم بعد فراغه أنه أخطأ الجهة'. What is the ruling after the prayer ends?
The ruling is: no i'adah (no repetition).
2
Locate the proof
Find the hadith of 'Amir ibn 'Uqba. What event does it describe and what was the Prophet's response?
The Companions prayed in different directions on a dark night; the Prophet did not order repetition, and the verse 2:115 was revealed.
3
Understand the dalala
Explain how the hadith proves that no i'adah is required. Which word or action indicates validity?
The Prophet's silence and the verse show that the prayer was accepted; ijtihad in qibla is valid.
4
Contrast with taharri for purity
Why does the text say taharri for qibla is unlike taharri for wudu? How does the example of the change of qibla (from Jerusalem to Ka'bah) support this?
Purity does not admit change; qibla does, as it was changed by revelation.
5
Apply the rule about turning during prayer
If one's ijtihad changes during the prayer, what should he do? Why turn from the right?
He turns to the correct direction from the right, not the left, based on fiqh etiquette.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة ولم يكن عنده مخبر من أهل المكان ولا ممن له علم أو سأله فلم يخبره ولا محراب بالمحل تحرى أي اجتهد وهو بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود ولو سجدة تلاوة ولا يجوز التحري مع وضع المحاريب لأن وضعها في الأصل بحق ومن ليس من أهل المكان والعلم لا يلتفت إلى قوله وإن أخبره إثنان ممن هو مسافر مثله لأنهما يخبران عن اجتهاد ولا يترك اجتهاده باجتهاد غيره وليس عليه قرع الأبواب للسؤال عن القبلة ولامس الجدران خشية الهوام وللإشتباه بطاق غير المحراب وإذا صلى الأعمى ركعة لغير القبلة فجاءه رجل وأقامه إليها واقتدى به فإن لم يكن حال افتتاحه عنده مخبر فصلاة الأعمى صحيحة لأنه لا يلزمه مس الجدران وإلا فهي فاسدة ولا يصح اقتداء الرجل به في الصورتين لقدرته في الأولى وعلم في الثانية ولا إعادة عليه لو علم بعد فراغه أنه أخطأ الجهة لقول عامر بن عقبة رضي الله عنه كنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في ليلة مظلمة فلم ندر أين القبلة فصلي كل رجل منا على حياله فلما أصبحنا ذكرنا ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنزلت: فأينما تولوا فشم وجه الله وليس التحري للقبلة مثل التحري للتوضؤ والساتر فإنه إذا ظهر نجاسة الماء أو الثوب أعاد لأنه أمر لا يحتمل الإنتقال والقبلة تحتمله كما حولت عن المقدس إلى الكعبة وإن علم بخطئه أو تبدل اجتهاده في صلاته استدار من جهة اليمين لا اليسار
And whoever is uncertain about the qibla direction, and has no informant from the people of that place nor anyone who has knowledge, or he asked but was not told, and there is no mihrab in that location, then he makes taharri (i.e., exerts effort), which is the exertion of one's utmost to achieve the goal, even if it be for a prostration of recitation. And taharri is not permissible when mihrabs are present because they were originally placed correctly. And one who is not from that place or knowledgeable is not to be heeded. And if two people who are travelers like him inform him, they report based on their own ijtihad, and he should not abandon his ijtihad for another's. He is not required to knock on doors to ask about the qibla, nor to touch walls for fear of insects or due to confusion with a non-mihrab arch. And if a blind man prays one rak'ah facing other than the qibla, then a man comes and straightens him toward it, and he follows him: if at the beginning he had no informant, his prayer is valid because he is not required to touch walls; otherwise it is invalid. And the man's following him is not valid in either case because of his capability in the first and knowledge in the second. And there is no repetition upon him if he learns after completion that he was mistaken, due to the saying of 'Amir ibn 'Uqba (may Allah be pleased with him): 'We were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on a dark night and we did not know where the qibla was, so each man prayed in his own direction. In the morning we mentioned that to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and the verse was revealed: 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.' And taharri for qibla is not like taharri for ablution and covering; for if the impurity of water or garment becomes apparent, he repeats because that matter does not admit of change, while the qibla admits it, as it was changed from Jerusalem to the Ka'bah. And if he learns of his mistake or his ijtihad changes during his prayer, he turns from the right direction, not the left.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage details the rules for taharri (estimation) of the qibla direction when one is uncertain. Taharri is required when there is no reliable informant or mihrab. The hadith from 'Amir ibn 'Uqba (or 'Amir ibn Rabi'a) recounts that the Companions prayed in different directions on a dark night, and the verse 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' was revealed, establishing that no repetition is required if one later realizes the direction was wrong. This is because qibla determination involves ijtihad, and subsequent discovery does not invalidate the past prayer. The passage contrasts this with taharri for purity, where if impurity is discovered, repetition is needed because purity is not subject to change. It also addresses specific cases: a blind person's prayer is valid if he had no informant, but his following by a sighted person is invalid; if one's ijtihad changes during prayer, he should turn to the correct direction from the right side.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharri): Exerting one's best effort to determine the qibla direction when uncertain.
المخبر (al-mukhbir): A reliable informant who can point out the qibla direction.
المحراب (al-mihrab): A niche in the wall indicating the qibla direction, especially in mosques.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone prays with taharri and later discovers they faced the wrong direction?
A) They must repeat the prayer
B) They do not need to repeat, based on the hadith
C) They must repeat only if they were negligent
D) They must repeat only if they are certain

Key Takeaway
Prayer with proper taharri is valid and does not require repetition even if the actual qibla was missed, due to the prophetic precedent and the changeable nature of qibla.

Conditions and Special Cases in Taharri for Qibla
Conditions and rules for taharri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when taharri is required, who can be a reliable informant, and the ruling for a blind person's prayer and following him.

Core Idea
Taharri is only valid when no reliable informant or mihrab exists; blind persons have special rules.

The beginning of the source passage lays out the preconditions for taharri: you must be genuinely uncertain and lack any clear indicator. It also discusses who can serve as an informant and what to do if a blind person prays. Understanding these conditions ensures that taharri is applied correctly and not used carelessly.

Guided Path
1
Identify when taharri is required
Read the first sentence. What must be absent for taharri to be permissible?
No informant from the locality, no knowledgeable person, no mihrab.
2
Define 'informant'
Who qualifies as a reliable informant? Are travellers acceptable?
An informant must be from the place or have knowledge; two travellers' advice is not binding because it's based on their own ijtihad.
3
Understand what is NOT required
What is the person not required to do? How does this protect from hardship?
Not required to knock on doors or touch walls due to fear of insects; shows taharri is based on reasonable effort.
4
Analyse the blind person case
When is a blind person's prayer valid? When invalid?
Valid if he had no informant initially; invalid if he had an informant.
5
Determine the ruling on following a blind imam
Why is it not valid for a sighted person to follow a blind imam in both situations?
In the first case, the sighted person is capable of finding the qibla himself; in the second, he has knowledge that the blind person is wrong.

Rulings on Qibla Determination and Taharri
This passage rules on following mihrab, testimony, and blind person's prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taharri for qibla, apply the exception for blind persons, and distinguish it from taharri for purity.

Core Idea
Once you have done your best, no repetition is required — the qibla admits transfer.

Determining the qibla when uncertain requires careful reasoning. This passage from the Hanafi tradition lays out key rules: following an established mihrab is obligatory, but if you must do taharri (estimation), your prayer is valid even if you later discover you were wrong. The text also addresses special cases like the blind person and the testimony of others. Let's walk through the rulings step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of authority
The passage begins by affirming that mihrabs are placed correctly. Note that we do not accept the claim of a non-local person who says otherwise.
This establishes that the mihrab is generally reliable.
2
Evaluate testimony
When two travelers inform you of the qibla, you may accept their report, but you are not required to abandon your own ijtihad.
This shows the importance of personal ijtihad when possible.
3
Examine the blind person's case
If he had no informer at the start of prayer, his prayer is valid when corrected; otherwise invalid. The follower's prayer is invalid in both cases.
The blind person is excused from touching walls.
4
Trace the dalil for no repetition
The hadith of 'Amir ibn 'Uqbah shows that the Companions prayed without knowing the qibla on a dark night, and the verse 'wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah' (2:115) was revealed, indicating that no repetition is required.
The hadith is a proof for the validity of taharri.
5
Apply the distinction
Taharri for qibla is unlike taharri for purity because the qibla can change (as it was changed from Jerusalem to Mecca), so it admits of transfer, while purity does not.
This distinction explains why no repetition is needed for qibla error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤٤
كتاب الصلاة
وضع المحاريب لأن وضعها في الأصل بحق ومن ليس من أهل المكان، والعلم لا يلتفت إلى قوله : وإن أخبره إثنان ممن هو مسافر مثله لأنهما يخبران عن اجتهاد، ولا يترك اجتهاده باجتهاد غيره، وليس عليه قرع الأبواب للسؤال عن القبلة، ولامس الجدران خشية الهوام وللإشتباه بطاق غير المحراب، وإذا صلى الأعمى ركعة لغير القبلة فجاءه رجل، وأقامه إليها واقتدى به فإن لم يكن حال افتتاحه عنده مخبر فصلاة الأعمى صحيحة لأنه لا يلزمه مس الجدران، وإلا فهي فاسدة ولا يصح اقتداء الرجل به في الصورتين لقدرته في الأولى وعلم في الثانية (ولا إعادة عليه أي المتحري (لو) علم بعد فراغه أنه (أخطأ) الجهة لقول عامر بن عقبة رضي الله عنه كنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في ليلة مظلمة فلم ندر أين القبلة فصلي كل رجل منا على حياله فلما أصبحنا ذكرنا ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنزلت: فأينما تولوا فشم وجه الله وليس التحري للقبلة مثل التحري للتوضؤ والساتر فإنه إذا ظهر نجاسة الماء، أو الثوب أعاد لأنه أمر لا يحتمل الإنتقال والقبلة تحتمله كما حولت عن المقدس إلى الكعبة (وإن علم بخطئه) أو تبدل اجتهاده في صلاته (استدار من جهة اليمين لا اليسار (ويني) على خطئه، يجب إتباع المحراب ولا يجوز له التحري كما في التبيين وذكر في الخانية جوازه معها. قوله : (وأن أخبره إثنان الخ إن وصلية. قوله : (وإقتدى به الأولى حذفه لأن المقصود إفادة عدم صحة إقتدائه به وقد أفاده بعد قوله : (فصلاة الأعمى صحيحة) نظيره ما إذا دخل المسجد رجل وهو مظلم، وصلى المغرب فلما فرغ من صلاته جيء بالسراج، فإذا هو صلى إلى غير القبلة أن صلاها بالتحري جاز ولا إعادة عليه عن التجنيس، والمزيد الأعمى إذا صلى ركعة إلى غير القبلة فجاء رجل وسواه وأقامه إلى القبلة، واقتدى به فهذا على وجهين أما أن يجد عند الافتتاح إنساناً يسأله أو لم يجد ففي الوجه الأول لا تجوز صلاته ولا الاقتداء به لأنه قادر على أداء الصلاة إلى جهة الكعبة وفي الوجه الثاني تجوز صلاة الإمام أي الأعمى، لأنه عاجز، ولاتجوز صلاة المقتدى لأن عنده صلاة إمامه على الخطأ اهـ . وهي عبارة لا غبار عليها قوله: (ولا) إعادة عليه لو أخطأ ولو بمكة والمدينة على الأصح قوله : (عامر بن عقبة) الذي في الشرح ابن ربيعة قوله: (على حياله) أي على قوله: (كما حولت عن المقدس) بصيغة اسم المفعول من قدس، أو على وزن مجلس، وهو على تقدير مضاف أي بيت المقدس قوله: (أو تبدل اجتهاده) ولو إلى الجهة الأولى على الأوجه كما في سكب الأنهر قوله : ( من جهة اليمين ينبغي أن يكون ذلك على وجه الاستحباب لا الوجوب كذا بحثه بعضهم، ومحله ما لم يكن العمل من جهة اليمين أكثر، وإلا حدته .
Book of Prayer. Placing of mihrabs because their placement originally is correct, and one who is not from the people of the place, his knowledge is not heeded. And if two people who are travelers like him inform him, because they inform based on ijtihad, and one does not abandon his own ijtihad for the ijtihad of others. And it is not required of him to knock on doors to ask about the qibla, nor to touch walls for fear of insects or confusion with a niche other than the mihrab. And if a blind person prays one rak'ah towards other than the qibla, then a man comes and corrects him to face the qibla, and he follows him, if at the time of his opening takbir he had no informer, then the prayer of the blind person is valid because he is not required to touch walls. Otherwise, it is invalid, and the followership of the man is not valid in both cases due to his ability in the first and his knowledge in the second. And there is no repetition upon the mutaharrī if he knows after finishing that he erred from the direction, due to the saying of 'Amir ibn 'Uqbah... And taharri for the qibla is not like taharri for wudu and the covering; when impurity of water or garment is revealed, he repeats, because that matter does not admit of transfer, while the qibla admits it... And if he knows his error or his ijtihad changes during his prayer, he turns from the right side, not the left, and he builds upon his error. It is obligatory to follow the mihrab and it is not permissible for him to do taharri...
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah addresses several rulings related to determining the qibla. The author begins by stating that the placement of mihrabs in mosques is based on correctness (haqq), and one who is not from that locality cannot override that. If two trustworthy travelers (who are themselves engaged in taharri) inform a person of the qibla, their testimony is accepted because they are reporting their ijtihad, but one does not have to abandon his own ijtihad for another's. The passage then covers the case of a blind person: if he had no one to inform him at the start of his prayer, his prayer is valid when corrected by someone who sets him straight, because he was excused from touching walls. However, if he had an informer initially, his prayer becomes invalid. Two men cannot follow him in prayer in either case because the follower knows the imam is in error. The hadith of 'Amir ibn 'Uqbah (or Ibn Rabi'ah) is cited to show that taharri is valid and no repetition is required if error is discovered after completion, as the Companions did on a dark night. The passage distinguishes taharri for qibla from taharri for purity: if impurity is found in water or clothing, repetition is required because those matters do not admit of transfer, whereas the qibla was transferred from Jerusalem to Mecca, showing it is subject to change. Finally, if one realizes his error during prayer or his ijtihad changes, he should turn towards the correct qibla from the right side, not the left, and he continues his prayer building upon what he has already done (he does not restart). The commentary notes that this turning is recommended (mustahabb) rather than obligatory, unless the work on the left is greater.

Key Terms
محراب (mihrab): The niche in a mosque indicating the direction of the qibla.
تحري (taharri): The process of using ijtihad to estimate the direction of the qibla when it is uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a blind person who had no informer at the start of his prayer is corrected by someone facing the qibla, is his prayer valid?
A) Yes, because he was excused from touching walls.
B) No, because he should have asked.
C) Yes, but only if he turns and continues.
D) No, his prayer is invalid because he was corrected.

Key Takeaway
For qibla taharri, the prayer is valid even if the direction turns out wrong, but for purity, any error requires repetition; the difference is that the qibla direction can change by divine command.

Starting Prayer Without Taharri: Suspended Validity and the Timing of Knowledge
Detailed ruling on starting prayer without taharri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the three outcomes when a person prays without taharri and explain why knowledge during prayer invalidates it according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Starting prayer without taharri is suspended; valid only if correct direction is known after finishing, not during.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a nuanced situation: when a person is uncertain of the qibla and begins praying without any estimation (taharri). The Hanafi school treats this action as suspended until the outcome is known. We will explore the three possible outcomes and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default status
The act is starting prayer without taharri when the qibla is uncertain. The default ruling is that the prayer is invalid (fasid) because the condition of facing the qibla is not met by certainty or estimation.
2
Distinguish the three possible outcomes
(a) After finishing, he knows he faced the qibla → valid. (b) During prayer, he knows → invalid. (c) He never knows → invalid.
3
Understand the legal basis: istishab al-hal
The invalidity is presumed to continue (istishab al-hal) unless overridden by evidence. Knowing after completion provides evidence that the condition was met, so validity is established. Knowing during prayer does not override because it would require building a strong state on a weak foundation.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that knowing during prayer validates it because if he stopped and restarted he would face the same direction. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it invalid because one cannot build a strong state on a weak one.
5
Note the adjacent rulings
The passage also touches on change of ijtihad (like naskh) and the Quba precedent, and the case of missing an obligatory sajdah after turning. These reinforce the principle that an action cannot serve two different qiblas.

ما أداه بالتحري لأن تبدل الاجتهاد كالنسخ، وأهل قباء استداروا في الصلاة إلى الكعبة حين بلغهم النسخ، واستحسنه النبي وإن تذكر سجدة صلبية بطلت صلاته (وإن شرع) من اشتبهت عليه بلا) (تحر كان فعله موقوفاً فلو أتمها (فعلم بعد فراغه) من الصلاة (أنه أصاب صحت) لأنه بتبين الصواب بطل الحكم بالاستصحاب وثبت الجواز من الصلاة (وإن علم بإصابته فيها) ولو بغالب الظن (فسدت) لأن حالته قويت به فلا يبني قوياً على ضعيف خلافاً لأبي يوسف رحمه الله (كما) فسدت فيما لو لم يعلم إصابته أصلا لأن الفساد ثابت باستصحاب الحال، ولم يرتفع بدليل فتقرر الفساد لأن المشروط لم يحصل حقيقة ولا حكماً وإذا وقع تحريه إلى جهة فصلى إلى غيرها لا تجزيه لتركه الكعبة حكماً في حقه،

(لأنه
كان المستحب التوجه إلى ما هو قليل العمل. قوله : ( كالنسخ) فلا يبطل العمل السابق، وإنما يمتنع العمل به في المستقبل. قوله : (وأهل قباء بالضم والدقرية من قرى المدينة يصرف، ولا يصرف كما في المغرب، ومن العرب من يقصره ويصرفه، ويجعله مذكراً ومنهم من يؤنثه، فلا يصرفه. قوله : (وإن تذكر سجدة (صلبية أي بعد الاستدارة أي انه تركها. قوله: (بطلت) وجهه أنه إذا أذاها في وجهة ركعتها التي تحول عنها فقد أداها إلى غير القبلة الآن وإن أداها إلى جهة تحريه الآن إداها إلى غير القبلة التي كانت لركعتها، والركعة الواحدة لا تكون لقبلتين. قوله : بتبين الصواب الخ) ولأن ما فرض لغيره يراعى حصوله لا تحصيله كالسعي إلى الجمعة بيانه أن جهة التحري وإن كانت هي القبلة حال الإشتباه لكن التحري لم يقصد لذاته، وإنما قصد للإصابة، فإذا حصلت أغنت عنه قوله : (بطل الحكم بالاستصحاب) أي استصحاب الحال أي حال الذي اشتبه عليه القبلة فإن حاله عند عدم التحري الفساد لأن الصلاة بدون التحري عند الإشتباه فاسدة قوله : (من) (الصلاة) أي من أول الصلاة. قوله : (قويت به) أي بالعلم، وبقي من الصور ما إذا علم بخطئه فيها، أو بعدها، والصلاة فاسدة فيهما. قوله : (خلافاً لأبي يوسف فإنه يقول بالصحة لأنه لو قطع استأنف إلى غير تلك الجهة فلا يعيد. قوله: (باستصحاب الحال هو الفساد لترك التحري عند الاشتباه قوله: (ولم يرتفع بدليل) بخلاف ما إذا تبين صوابه كما سبق قوله: (لم يحصل حقيقة) وهو استقباله يقيناً. قوله: (ولا حكماً) أي بالتحري والحاصل أنه أما ان لا يشك ولا يتحرى وجوابه ان صلاته على الجواز ما لم يتبين له الخطأ، وأما أن يشك ولا يتحرى وهي على الثلاثة أوجه التي ذكرها المصنف، وإما أن يشك ويتحرى وهو أصل المسألة قوله : (لا) تجزيه وعن أبي حنيفة يخشى عليه الكفر، ولا يكفر وفي الظهيرية ومن صلى إلى غير جهة الكعبة لا يكفر هو الصحيح لأن ترك جهة الكعبة جائز في الجملة بخلاف الصلاة بغير طهارة لعدم الجواز مع عدمها بحال، واختاره الصدر الشهيد وفيه أنه يجوز لفاقد الطهورين الصلاة عدمها .
What he performed by taharri, because change of ijtihad is like abrogation. The people of Quba turned in prayer towards the Ka'bah when the abrogation reached them, and the Prophet approved it. And if he remembers a prostration of an obligatory nature, his prayer becomes invalid. And if one who is uncertain starts prayer without taharri, his action is suspended. If he completes it and after finishing knows that he hit the correct direction, it is valid, because with the manifestation of correctness, the ruling of istishab al-hal is invalidated and permissibility of the prayer is established. But if he knows his correctness during the prayer, even by overwhelming presumption, it becomes invalid, because his state is strengthened by the knowledge, so he does not build a strong upon a weak, contrary to Abu Yusuf. Just as it is invalid if he never knows his correctness at all, because the invalidity is established by istishab al-hal and is not removed by evidence. So the invalidity is established because the condition (facing the qibla) was not achieved neither in reality nor in effect (by taharri). And if his taharri pointed to a direction but he prays to another, it does not suffice him, because he abandoned the qibla in effect according to his own ruling.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on qibla. It begins by stating that changing one's ijtihad during prayer is like abrogation (naskh): it does not invalidate what came before but changes the direction going forward. The precedent of the people of Quba is cited: when they heard about the change of qibla from Jerusalem to Mecca, they turned during prayer, and the Prophet approved. If one remembers an obligatory prostration (sajdah salbiyyah) that he missed, his prayer becomes invalid because a single rak'ah cannot face two qiblas. The main ruling here is about someone who starts prayer without taharri (i.e., he does not even estimate the qibla but prays in a random direction). His prayer is suspended (mawquf): if after finishing he learns he did face the qibla, it is valid because the purpose of taharri (correct direction) was achieved. But if he knows during the prayer that he is facing the correct direction, his prayer becomes invalid because he now has certainty and should not continue on a weaker basis (his initial lack of taharri). Abu Yusuf disagreed and held it valid; the Hanafi position is the former. Similarly, if he never finds out, the prayer is invalid because the necessary condition (facing the qibla) was not met neither in reality (yaqeen) nor in effect (taharri). Finally, if one did taharri but then prays to a different direction than his estimation indicated, his prayer is invalid because he abandoned the qibla in his own legal ruling. The commentary adds that some authorities said he fears kufr but is not a kafir; the correct view is that it is not kufr because turning away from the qibla is permitted in some cases (e.g., fear).

Key Terms
سجدة صلبية (sajdah salbiyyah): An obligatory prostration that is part of the prayer, not a prostration of recitation.
استصحاب الحال (istishab al-hal): Presumption of continuity of the previous state. Here, the state of being without taharri leads to invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person starts prayer without taharri and never learns whether he faced the qibla, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid because he acted in good faith.
B) The prayer is invalid due to the condition of facing the qibla not being met.
C) The prayer is valid if he made an effort to determine the direction later.
D) The prayer is suspended indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
Prayer begun without taharri is valid only if the correct direction is known after completion; knowledge during prayer does not rescue it.

Salah — Prayer

Taharri and Knowledge of Qibla During Prayer
Explains taharri rules with Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer after taharri when one learns the correct qibla direction during the prayer, and evaluate the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Knowledge of qibla during prayer invalidates it in Hanafi law because certainty cannot rest on estimation.

This lesson examines a subtle but important rule: what happens if you estimate the qibla, pray, and then learn you were correct while still praying? Does the prayer become valid, or does it remain invalid? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer, with a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Understanding this rule is crucial for anyone who may face ambiguity in direction and needs to know the fiqh implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage presents three cases: (1) taharri performed and knowledge of correctness after prayer, (2) taharri performed and knowledge during prayer, (3) no taharri performed at all. Identify the ruling for each according to the matn.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling for each
According to Abu Hanifa: case (1) is valid (sahih), case (2) is invalid (fasid), and case (3) is invalid. Note the reasoning: istishab of invalidity is removed only by post-prayer certainty.
3
State Abu Yusuf's objection and his proof
Abu Yusuf holds that case (2) is also valid, analogizing to taharri for water: if one performs wudu with water after taharri and later learns it was pure, the prayer is valid. Here too, learning during prayer confirms the condition was met.
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy because facing qibla is a condition that must be actually met, not merely estimated.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view: prayer is invalid if knowledge comes during prayer. The practical consequence: if one learns during prayer, he must stop and repeat; according to Abu Yusuf, he may continue and the prayer is valid.
Also note: if one prays to a different direction than his taharri, it is invalid even if he hits the correct direction, because he abandoned his own estimation.

He said: 'What he performed by taharri (estimation) [is valid] because change of ijtihad is like abrogation. And the people of Quba turned in prayer toward the Ka'bah when abrogation reached them, and the Prophet approved it. And if he remembers a prostration of the backbone [i.e., obligatory prostration], his prayer is invalidated. And if he begins [prayer] while the direction is ambiguous and he does not perform taharri, his action is suspended. Then if he completes it and knows after finishing his prayer that he was correct, it is valid. Because by the manifest correctness, the ruling of istishab (presumptive continuity) is invalidated, and permissibility is established from the prayer. And if he knows his correctness during it, even by predominant opinion, it is invalid. Because his state becomes strong by it, so he does not build a strong [state] on a weak one, contrary to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him. And likewise, it is invalid if he does not know his correctness at all, because the invalidity is established by istishab of the current state, and it is not removed by evidence, so the invalidity is settled. Because the condition was not met actually nor legally. And if he made his taharri towards a direction but prayed to another, it does not suffice him because of his leaving the Ka'bah legally in his regard. Because it was recommended to face what is less in action. His statement: 'like abrogation' – so it does not invalidate previous action, but only prevents acting on it in the future. His statement: 'And the people of Quba' – with damm and it is a village of Madinah; it is declined and not declined as in al-Mughrib. Some Arabs shorten it and decline it, making it masculine; some make it feminine and do not decline it. His statement: 'And if he remembers a prostration of the backbone' – i.e., after turning – meaning he left it. His statement: 'it is invalidated' – its reasoning is that if he performs it in the direction of his raka'ah from which he turned, then he performed it to other than the qibla now. And if he performs it to the direction of his taharri now, he performs it to other than the qibla that was for his raka'ah, and one raka'ah cannot be for two qiblas. His statement: 'by the manifest correctness, etc.' – and because what is prescribed for something else, its attainment is considered, not its acquisition, like going to Friday prayer. Its explanation: that the direction of taharri, even if it is the qibla at the time of ambiguity, yet taharri is not intended for itself, but only for hitting [the correct direction]. So if hitting occurs, it suffices from it. His statement: 'the ruling of istishab is invalidated' – i.e., istishab of the current state, meaning the state of the one who has ambiguous qibla. For his state without taharri is invalidity, because prayer without taharri when it is ambiguous is invalid. His statement: 'from the prayer' – i.e., from the beginning of the prayer. His statement: 'becomes strong by it' – i.e., by the knowledge. And there remains the case where he knows his mistake during or after it, and the prayer is invalid in both. His statement: 'contrary to Abu Yusuf' – for he says it is valid, because if he cut [the prayer] he would start over to other than that direction, so he does not repeat. His statement: 'by istishab of the current state' – it is invalidity due to leaving taharri when ambiguous. His statement: 'and it is not removed by evidence' – contrary to when his correctness becomes manifest, as previously. His statement: 'did not occur actually' – i.e., facing it with certainty. His statement: 'nor legally' – i.e., by taharri. The summary: either he does not doubt and does not do taharri, and its answer is that his prayer is conditionally permissible as long as error is not manifest to him; or he doubts and does not do taharri, and it has three aspects mentioned by the author; or he doubts and does taharri, and that is the basis of the issue. His statement: 'it does not suffice him' – and from Abu Hanifa: one fears kufr for him, but he does not become a kafir. In al-Zahiriyyah: 'Whoever prays to other than the direction of the Ka'bah does not become a kafir' – this is the correct view, because leaving the direction of the Ka'bah is permissible in general, contrary to prayer without purification, because there is no permissibility at all without it. And al-Sadr al-Shahid chose it, and in it there is that it is permissible for one who lacks both purifying materials to pray without them. Then he said: 'And it is the direction he estimated, even if he hit [the correct direction], contrary to Abu Yusuf regarding the manifestation of his hitting. He makes him like the one who does taharri regarding vessels: if he deviates from his taharri and it appears that the water with which he performed wudu is pure, his prayer is valid. On this basis, if he prays in a garment while believing it is impure, or that he is in hadath, or that the time has not entered, then it appears contrary, it does not suffice him, even if the condition is found, because of the absence of another condition – which is the corruption of his action initially due to lack of certainty. As for water, purity was found actually and the intention.' His statement: 'And on this' – i.e., on what preceded that there is no consideration for hitting if he prays to other than his taharri direction, or on this difference. His statement: 'and it is corruption of his action initially' – which is in the sharh: that one does not rule corruption of his action initially because then his intention would not be valid due to lack of certainty. Suitable. His statement: 'and the intention' – i.e., intention of purification. In it, that the existence of intention is not a condition. And what is in the sharh: 'And in water, which he turned to, certainty in intention and purity were found actually, so it was valid.'
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with a ruling. It begins by stating the general principle: what one performs by taharri (estimation) is valid because a change in ijtihad is like abrogation—it does not nullify past actions. The famous example of the people of Quba, who turned towards the Ka'bah upon learning the abrogation of the direction, is cited with prophetic approval. The text then addresses specific cases: if a person prays without taharri while the qibla is ambiguous, the prayer is suspended. If he completes it and later learns he was correct, it is valid because the underlying continuity of invalidity (istishab) is overturned. However, if he learns of his correctness while still in prayer, the prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa, because he cannot build a strong certainty (knowledge) upon a weak foundation (taharri). Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that the prayer is valid because the underlying validity is now confirmed; he analogizes it to taharri for water: if one performs wudu with water after taharri and later learns it was pure, the prayer is valid. The text upholds Abu Hanifa's view as the madhhab position. It also discusses the case where one prays to a direction different from his taharri—it does not suffice, and Abu Hanifa's warning of kufr (but not actual kufr) is noted but deemed softened by later authorities. The passage concludes with commentary clarifying istishab, the distinction between actual and legal fulfillment of conditions, and reinforces that intention (niyyah) is not a condition for validity in this context, but certainty is.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Estimation or effort to determine the qibla direction when it is ambiguous.
استصحاب (istishāb): Presumptive continuity of the previous status (here, invalidity of prayer due to lack of taharri).
إصابة (isābah): Hitting the correct qibla direction accurately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon position), what is the ruling if a person performs taharri for qibla, prays, and then learns during the prayer that he was correct?
A) The prayer is valid because he now knows he faced the qibla.
B) The prayer is invalid because he cannot build strong knowledge on weak taharri.
C) The prayer is suspended until after completion.
D) The prayer is valid only if he repeats the taharri.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, if you learn the correct qibla during a prayer performed with taharri, the prayer becomes invalid because certainty cannot be built on estimation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Prayer of Followers Ignorant of Imam's Qibla Direction
Ruling on followers' prayer when ignorant of imam's qibla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a follower's prayer when ignorant of the imam's qibla direction and identify the exception for stepping ahead.

Core Idea
Follower's prayer valid if ignorant of imam's qibla; stepping ahead invalidates.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a group of people in darkness each perform personal ijtihad (taharri) to determine the qibla, but they do not know which direction their imam is facing. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that balances the obligation to follow the imam with the validity of individual prayer. Understanding the condition of ignorance and the exception of stepping ahead is essential for correctly applying the rules of congregational prayer in challenging circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (followers praying behind an imam after taharri) and the general ruling: their prayer is valid.
The ruling applies when followers are ignorant of the imam's direction.
2
Locate the Exception
Note the exception: if a follower steps ahead (taqaddum) of the imam, his prayer is invalid. This is analogized to the rule inside the Ka'bah.
Stepping ahead refers to moving beyond the imam in position or direction.
3
Trace the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is a hadith of 'Amir, previously mentioned, which establishes that inside the Ka'bah, all directions are qibla but stepping ahead invalidates. This is applied by analogy to the case of ignorant followers.
The analogy (qiyas) rests on the shared illa: uncertainty of direction.
4
Understand the Condition of Knowledge
Contrast with the case where a follower knows the imam's direction and considers it wrong: such a follower's prayer is invalid because he believes the imam is in error.
This condition does not apply inside the Ka'bah because there is no error—all directions are qibla.

ولو) تحرى قوم جهات في ظلمة (وجهلوا حال إمامهم) في توجهه (تجزيهم) صلاتهم إلا من تقدم على إمامه كما في جوف الكعبة لما قدمناه .
قوله : (وجهلوا حال إمامهم) أما من علم حال إمامه لم تجز صلاته لأنه اعتقد أن إمامه على الخطأ وهذا لا يشترط في الصلاة في جوف الكعبة، فالصلاة صحيحة مع علم حال الإمام لعدم الخطا (۱) لأن الكل قبلة. قوله: (كما في جوف الكعبة) فإن التقدم فيه مضر . قوله : ( لما قدمناه من حديث عامر، وهو علة لقوله تجزيهم.
And if people perform taharri in different directions in darkness and are ignorant of the state of their imam regarding his facing [the qibla], their prayer is valid except for the one who steps ahead of his imam, as [the rule] inside the Ka'bah, because of what we presented earlier.
His statement: 'and are ignorant of the state of their imam' - as for one who knows the state of his imam, his prayer is not valid, because he believes that his imam is in error, and this is not required in prayer inside the Ka'bah, so the prayer is valid with knowledge of the imam's state because there is no error, since all is qibla. His statement: 'as inside the Ka'bah' - for stepping ahead there is harmful. His statement: 'because of what we presented earlier from the hadith of 'Amir' - and it is the cause for his statement 'their prayer is valid'.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof. It addresses a scenario where a group of people, due to darkness, each perform taharri independently and pray in different directions, not knowing which direction their imam is facing. The ruling is that their prayer is valid, with one exception: if any follower steps ahead of the imam (i.e., beyond the imam in direction or position), that follower's prayer is invalid, analogous to the rule for praying inside the Ka'bah, where all directions are qibla but stepping ahead of the imam invalidates the prayer. The commentary clarifies that if a follower knows the imam's direction and it differs from his own, his prayer is invalid because he believes the imam is in error; this does not apply inside the Ka'bah since all directions are qibla. The proof comes from a previously mentioned hadith of 'Amir, which establishes the rule for the Ka'bah. Thus, ignorance of the imam's direction is a condition for validity in this case.

Key Terms
تقدم (taqaddum): The follower stepping ahead of the imam in position or direction, which invalidates the follower's prayer in this context.
جوف الكعبة (jawf al-ka'bah): Inside the Ka'bah, where all directions are qibla, but stepping ahead of the imam remains invalid.
تحرى (taharri): The act of exerting effort to determine the qibla direction when it is not known, e.g., in darkness.

In Hanafi fiqh, a follower's prayer behind an imam in darkness is valid if the follower is ignorant of the imam's qibla direction, provided the follower does not step ahead of the imam.

Defining Wajib in Hanafi Fiqh
Definition of 'wajib' in prayer, linguistic and technical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three linguistic meanings of 'wajib', state its Shari'a definition, and distinguish it from 'fard' in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Wajib in Hanafi fiqh is binding by evidence containing ambiguity (shubhah), distinct from fard proven by definitive proof.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi opens the section on the obligations (wajibat) of prayer by defining the term 'wajib'. It explains that 'wajib' has three distinct linguistic meanings and a precise technical meaning in Shari'a. Mastering this definition is foundational for correctly categorizing actions in Hanafi fiqh, especially distinguishing between fard and wajib.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the three linguistic meanings
Recall that 'wajib' in Arabic means binding/necessity (luzum), falling (suqut), and agitation (idtirab). These reflect the root w-j-b.
The commentator suggests using noun forms (lazim, saqit, mudtarib) for precision.
2
Understand the Shari'a definition
In Shari'a, 'wajib' is 'what is binding upon us by evidence containing some ambiguity (shubhah).' This means the proof is not absolutely certain (zanni al-thubut or zanni al-dalala).
This definition is quoted from Fakhr al-Islam and is transmitted from earlier authorities ('ruwiya').
3
Contrast with fard
Fard is binding by definitive evidence (qat'i). Wajib is a lesser category: omission of fard invalidates the act and requires full repetition; omission of wajib requires compensation (e.g., sajdah al-sahw) but the act remains valid.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school; other schools often equate wajib with fard.
4
Apply the definition to prayer
In salah, acts like reciting Surah al-Fatiha are fard (proven by mutawatir hadith), while reciting an additional surah is wajib (proven by ahad hadith). Use the definition to classify obligations.
This practical application shows the importance of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في بيان واجب الصلاة الواجب في اللغة يجيء بمعنى اللزوم، وبمعنى السقوط، وبمعنى الاضطراب، وفي الشرع اسم لما لزمنا بدليل فيه شبهة قال فخر الإسلام وإنما سمي
قوله : (يجيء بمعنى اللزوم) لو قال بمعنى اللازم والساقط والمضطرب أو قال في الأول الوجوب يجيء بمعنى اللزوم الخ لكان أنسب قوله : ( وفي الشرع إسم لما لزمنا) روي
Regarding the explanation of the obligatory of prayer. 'Wajib' in language comes to mean: binding/necessity, falling, and agitation. And in Shari'a, it is a name for what is binding upon us by evidence containing some ambiguity. Fakhr al-Islam said: 'And it is only called...'
His statement: 'it comes to mean binding' – if he said 'meaning the binding, the fallen, the agitated' or said in the first 'wujub' comes to mean binding etc., it would be more appropriate. His statement: 'and in Shari'a it is a name for what is binding upon us' – it is narrated.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling opening the section on the obligations (wajibat) of prayer. It provides the linguistic meaning of 'wajib' as having three distinct senses: lizum (binding or necessity), suqut (falling), and idtirab (agitation). The technical Shar'i definition is given: 'what is binding upon us by evidence containing some ambiguity (shubhah).' This is the classic Hanafi definition distinguishing wajib from fard: fard is proven by definitive evidence (qat'i), while wajib is proven by speculative evidence (zanni). Fakhr al-Islam (a Hanafi jurist) is quoted as beginning an explanation, but the text cuts off. The commentary (hashya) corrects the wording, suggesting that the author should have used the nouns 'al-lazim, al-saqit, al-mudtarib' instead of the verbal nouns. It then affirms the Shar'i definition with 'ruwiya' (it is narrated), indicating that this definition is transmitted from earlier authorities.

Key Terms
واجب (wājib): In Shari'a: what is binding upon a person by evidence that contains some ambiguity (shubhah), i.e., not absolutely certain.
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Honorific title of a Hanafi jurist, likely referring to 'Ala' al-Din al-Kasani or similar. Here quoted on the definition of wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of wajib as 'binding by evidence containing shubhah' is the key distinction from fard and is essential for categorizing obligations in salah.

Taharrī for Qibla and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute with Abu Yusuf
Ruling on qibla direction by taharrī and intra-Hanafi disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on taharrī for qibla and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, including the practical difference and the authority weight of each view.

Core Idea
Your best effort to find the qibla makes your prayer valid, even if you later learn you were wrong—but not everyone in the school agreed.

This passage presents a critical intra-Hanafi disagreement about the validity of prayer after performing taharrī (seeking the qibla direction). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is valid and need not be repeated even if the actual qibla is later discovered. His student Abu Yusuf disagrees, drawing an analogy to the case of taharrī for water purity. The passage also addresses what to do when taharrī yields no clear direction and the ruling for a group praying in darkness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine the act (taharrī for qibla) and the ruling: prayer performed after taharrī is valid (sahih) according to Abu Hanifa, even if the actual direction is missed.
The ruling applies when one makes a genuine effort.
2
State the disagreement
Abu Yusuf holds that if the actual qibla becomes apparent, the prayer must be repeated. Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Abu Yusuf's view is not from zahir al-riwayah.
3
Examine the proofs
Identify Abu Hanifa's proof (hadith of 'Amir) and Abu Yusuf's proof (qiyas to taharrī for water purity).
The hadith is cited as the primary dalil.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how Abu Hanifa distinguishes the two cases: intention in qibla is tied to direction, whereas in water it is tied to purification.
The distinction is based on the object of intention.
5
Apply to a branch ruling
Consider the case when taharrī yields no direction: the person may pray to one direction or all four; the most precautionary is to pray to all four.
This is a practical extension from the principle.
6
Note the authority weight
Recognize that Abu Yusuf's view is ghayr zahir al-riwayah, so the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.
Authority weight affects which view is followed in fatwa.

Source Text

It is the direction that one exerts effort for (taharrī), even if one hits (the actual qibla), contrary to Abu Yusuf regarding the manifestation of hitting it. He (Abu Yusuf) makes it like the one who exerts effort regarding vessels: if he deviates from his taharrī and the purity of what he performed wudu with becomes apparent, his prayer is valid. And upon this, if he prays in a garment while believing it is impure, or that he is in a state of hadath, or that the time has not entered, and then the contrary becomes apparent, it does not suffice him, even if the condition is found, due to the absence of another condition, which is the corruption of his action initially due to the lack of certainty. As for water, purity is found in reality and intention. And if a group of people exert effort for directions in darkness and are ignorant of the state of their imam concerning his direction, their prayer suffices them, except for one who advances ahead of his imam, as in the hollow of the Kaaba, due to what we have presented. Branch: If one exerts effort and his effort falls upon nothing, it is said: he delays; it is said: he chooses; it is said: he prays to the four directions, which is the most precautionary as in al-Fath. Yet with this, if he prays to one direction, it is permissible even if he errs, as in al-Zahiriyyah. His statement: 'Contrary to Abu Yusuf' – it is not from the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) from him as in al-Qahistani. His statement: 'And upon this' – that is, upon what has preceded that there is no consideration for hitting (the qibla) if he prays to other than his direction of taharrī, or upon this dispute. His statement: 'And it is the corruption of his action initially' which is in the sharh (commentary) – meaning that we do not rule the corruption of his action initially because then his intention would not be valid due to lack of certainty, which is appropriate. His statement: 'And intention' – meaning intention of purification; therein, that its existence is not required, and what is in the sharh and regarding the water he deviated to, certainty with intention and actual purity existed, so it is valid. His statement: 'And they are ignorant of the state of their imam' – as for one who knows the state of his imam, his prayer does not suffice him because he believes that his imam is in error. This is not required in prayer inside the Kaaba, and prayer is valid even with knowledge of the imam's state due to the absence of error because the whole (Kaaba) is the qibla. His statement: 'As in the hollow of the Kaaba' – for advancing therein is harmful. His statement: 'Due to what we have presented from the hadith of 'Amir, and it is the cause for his statement 'it suffices them.'
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of prayer after taharrī (searching for the qibla direction) when the actual direction is discovered later. The main ruling is from Abu Hanifa: a person who performs taharrī and prays has fulfilled his obligation, and his prayer is valid even if he later learns he was facing the wrong direction. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that if the correct direction becomes apparent, the prayer must be repeated, analogizing it to the case of taharrī for purity of water: if someone performs wudu with water he thought was impure, but later finds it was pure, his wudu is valid per Abu Yusuf; however, Abu Hanifa distinguishes the case because in taharrī for qibla, the intention (niyyah) is tied to the direction chosen, not the actual qibla. The passage further discusses a branch (far'): if a person's taharrī does not yield a specific direction, he may pray to one direction or all four, with the cautious approach being to pray to all four. The commentary clarifies that Abu Yusuf's position is not from the zahir al-riwayah (the well-known transmitted authoritative reports). The proof for the Hanafi position is the hadith of 'Amir, cited earlier. The ruling also applies to a group praying in darkness who do not know the imam's direction: their prayer is valid unless one advances ahead of the imam.

Key Terms
تحرى (taharrī): The act of exerting effort to determine the correct direction of the qibla when it is unclear.
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca towards which Muslims pray.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) His prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) His prayer is valid and does not need repetition.
C) His prayer is valid only if he intended the actual qibla.
D) His prayer is invalid because he had doubt.

Key Takeaway
Your best effort to determine the qibla suffices for valid prayer, even if later proven incorrect; this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Hanafi Definition of Wajib and Its Hierarchy
Definition of 'wajib' in prayer and its place in the hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of wajib, explain its distinction from fard using the four evidence types, and identify the practical consequences of omitting a wajib in prayer.

Core Idea
Wajib is an obligation established by evidence with doubt (shubha); it stands between fard (certain) and sunnah (recommended).

Understanding the Hanafi concept of wajib is crucial for correctly applying the rules of prayer. Unlike other schools, the Hanafis distinguish between fard and wajib based on the certainty of the evidence, affecting everything from takfīr to the compensation for forgetfulness. This lesson unpacks the definition, the evidence classification, and the protective hierarchy of fard, wajib, sunnah, and adab.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the linguistic and sharʿī definitions of wajib
The word 'wajib' has three linguistic meanings: necessity, falling, and disturbance. The sharʿī definition is 'what is incumbent upon us by evidence containing doubt (shubha).' Note that 'falling' here refers to the obligation not being in the realm of belief (ʿilm).
The term 'shubha' is key: it refers to the evidence being less than certain (zannī).
2
Understand the four types of scriptural evidence
The passage divides evidence into four categories based on certainty of transmission (thubūt) and certainty of meaning (dalāla). Each category yields a different ruling level: (1) qatʿī thubūt & dalāla → fard/haram; (2) qatʿī thubūt, zannī dalāla → wujūb/karāha tahrīm; (3) zannī thubūt, qatʿī dalāla → wujūb; (4) zannī thubūt & dalāla → sunnah/istihbāb/karāha tanzīh.
Memorise the four-box grid: it is the foundation of Hanafi hierarchical rulings.
3
Explore the hierarchical relationship: fard → wajib → sunnah → adab
The wājibāt complete the farāʾiḍ, the sunan complete the wājibāt, and the ādāb complete the sunan. The passage uses the analogy of concentric fortresses – the outer wall preserves the inner ones.
Examples: reciting al-Fātiḥa and a sūra is wajib (completing the fard of qirāʾa); tasbīḥ in rukūʿ is sunnah (completing the wajib of tumaʾnīna).
4
Identify the practical rulings of a wajib
Intentionally omitting a wajib deserves punishment (though less than fard), but does not cause kufr. Forgetful omission requires sajdat al-sahw; if omitted intentionally and not compensated, the prayer must be repeated within the time.
This is the thamarah al-khilāf: the same act may be treated differently across schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والطمأنينة متممة للركوع والسجود وكذا التشهد في الثانية متمم لقعدتها وضم الأنف متمم لوضع الجبهة إلا ان منها ما يكون متمماً للركن خاصة ومنها ما يكون متمماً لها من غير نظر إلى ركن كالقعود الأول وتشهده والسلام فليتأمل قوله (والسنن لإكمال الواجبات) كالتسبيح للطمأنينة، والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم متممة للتشهد والتعوذ والبسملة متمات لقراءة الفاتحة، ولا يظهر هذا التتميم في جميع السنن قوله : (والأدب لا كمال السنة) تكون كاملة بالأدب فنظر الراكع إلى القدمين والساجد إلى الأرنبة، متمم للتسبيحات لأنها حينئذ تكون مستحضرة لعدم إشتغاله بإطلاق النظر والنظر إلى حجره متمم لهيئة الجلوس، وفيه ما مر. قوله: (ليكون كل منها حصناً لما شرع (لتكميله أي حافظاً له فالواجبات كالسور على الفرائض والسنن كالسور على الواجبات والآداب كالسور على السنن فمن حفظ السور الأخير كان للأسوار الداخلة أحفظ ومن ضيعه ينجر به الحال إلى تضييع باقيها، والتهاون بها، وفي نسخ كلا بالنصب ولا وجه له قوله : (إستحقاق العقاب) هو دون عقاب ترك الفرض قوله : (والثواب بفعله هو الحكم الأخروي، وأما الحكم الدنيوي فهو سقوط المطالبة. قوله : (وإعادتها بتركه عمداً أي ما دام الوقت باقياً وكذا في السهو إن لم يسجد له وإن لم يعدها حتى ثلاثاً فإنه
On the exposition of the obligatory (wajib) of prayer. The wajib in language comes to mean necessity (luzūm), and also [؟] falling (suqūt), and also [؟] disturbance (iḍṭirāb). In the Shar‘ it is a name for what is incumbent upon us by evidence that contains some doubt (shubha). Fakhr al-Islam said: It is so named either because it is ‘falling from us’ (sāqiṭ ‘annā) in terms of knowledge (i.e., we are not required to believe in its obligation as certain), or because it is ‘falling from us’ in terms of action, or because it is ‘disturbed’ (muḍṭarib) between fard and sunnah or between obligation and non-obligation. It is binding upon us in action, not in knowledge. And the wajib acts were legislated to complete the farā’iḍ (obligatory acts), and the sunan (recommended acts) to complete the wājibāt, and the ādāb (etiquettes) to complete the sunnah, so that each of them is a fortress for what was legislated for its completion. The ruling of the wajib is: deserving of punishment for its intentional omission, but not takfīr (declaring disbelief) for the one who denies it, and reward for performing it; and the necessity of sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) for lacking it in the prayer due to forgetfulness, or its repetition (the prayer) for its intentional omission. And the fall of the fard incomplete... [text incomplete]. From the Imam: he said, the meaning of which: The difference between wajib and fard is like that between heaven and earth. Some call it sunnah, so they sometimes express it as sunniyyah (sunnah-status) and then they express it as wujūb (obligation). This is from the author of al-Bahr. His statement: (with evidence that contains a doubt) – know that the scriptural evidences (adilla sam‘iyyah) are of four types: (1) qat‘i al-thubut wa al-dalālah, like the mutawātir texts that are muhkam (unequivocal); (2) qat‘i al-thubut, zanni al-dalālah, like the ayaat that are interpreted (mu’awwal); (3) zanni al-thubut, qat‘i al-dalālah, like khabar al-wāhid whose meaning is decisive; (4) zanni al-thubut wa al-dalālah, like khabar al-wāhid whose meaning is speculative. By the first, fard (and haram) is established; by the second and third, wujūb (and karāhat al-tahrīm) are established; by the fourth, sunnah and istihbāb (and karāhat al-tanzīh) are established. So the establishment of the ruling is according to its evidence. This is from al-Kashshāf, elaborated in the sharh. His statement: (because it is falling from us in knowledge) i.e., we are not required to believe in its obligation. His statement: (or because it is falling from us in action) – if he had said 'or because it is incumbent upon us in action' it would have been more appropriate to point to the first meaning (luzūm) explicitly, although what he mentioned also indicates it by context. His statement: (or because it is disturbed) i.e., ambiguous. His statement: (and the wajib acts were legislated to complete the farā’iḍ) – for example, recitation (qirā’a) is fard, and the obligation of reciting al-Fātiha and a sūrah is wajib that completes that fard; so if one leaves it, it is makrūh tahrīmī and it is a supplement. Tranquillity (tuma’nīna) is a complement to rukū‘ and sujūd; likewise the tashahhud in the second rak‘ah complements its sitting; and pressing the nose to the ground complements placing the forehead. However, some complements are specific to the pillar, and others complete the act without reference to a specific pillar, like the first sitting, its tashahhud, and the taslīm – so reflect. His statement: (and the sunan to complete the wājibāt) – like the tasbīh (glorifications) for tranquillity, and the salawāt (blessings) on the Prophet (peace be upon him) complements the tashahhud, and the ta‘awwudh and basmalah complement the recitation of al-Fātiha. But this complementarity is not apparent in all sunan. His statement: (and the adab completes the sunnah) – the sunnah attains perfection through adab. For example, the look of the one in rukū‘ at his feet, and the one in sujūd at the tip of his nose, completes the tasbīhāt because then they are present-minded as his gaze is not loose; and looking at the lap is a complement to the sitting posture. This has been mentioned. His statement: (so that each of them is a fortress for what was legislated for its completion) – i.e., a protector. So the wājibāt are like walls around the farā’iḍ, the sunan are like walls around the wājibāt, and the ādāb are like walls around the sunan. Whoever preserves the outermost wall will be better at preserving the inner walls; whoever neglects it will gradually lead to the neglect of the rest. And in some copies: 'kullā' (both) with fatha (nasb), but this has no basis. His statement: (deserving of punishment) – it is less than the punishment for leaving a fard. His statement: (and the reward for performing it) – this is the otherworldly ruling; as for the worldly ruling, it is the dropping of accountability (suqūṭ al-muṭāliba). His statement: (and its repetition if it is left intentionally) – i.e., as long as the time remains; similarly in forgetfulness if he does not perform prostration for it and does not repeat it until three times [text incomplete].
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and analysis of the term 'wajib' as used in prayer. It begins by giving the linguistic meanings of wajib: necessity (luzūm), falling (suqūṭ), and disturbance (iḍṭirāb). The technical Shar‘i definition is 'something that is incumbent upon us by evidence that contains some doubt (shubha).' This is a key Hanafi distinction: fard is established by qat‘ī (certain) evidence, while wajib is established by evidence that is less than certain (zannī). Therefore, rejecting a wajib does not constitute disbelief (kufr) as rejecting a fard does. The text then explains the hierarchy of obligations: farā’iḍ (fard) are the foundational obligations; wājibāt are complements to farā’iḍ; sunnan are complements to wājibāt; and ādāb are complements to sunnan. This is likened to protective walls: the best preservation is to maintain the outermost level (ādāb) so that the inner levels (sunan, wājibāt, farā’iḍ) are protected. The passage then elaborates on the four types of scriptural evidence, each yielding a different level of ruling: qat‘ī thubut and dalālah yields fard/haram; qat‘ī thubut with zannī dalālah or zannī thubut with qat‘ī dalālah yields wujūb/karāhat tahrīm; zannī thubut and dalālah yields sunnah/istihbāb/karāhat tanzīh. The ruling of a wajib is: intentional omission deserves punishment (but not as severe as omitting a fard), forgetful omission requires sajdat al-sahw, and if intentionally omitted, the prayer must be repeated while the time still remains. Examples are given: recitation of al-Fātiha and a sūrah is wajib (since recitation itself is fard, but the specific set is wajib), tranquil posture in rukū‘ and sujūd complements those pillars, etc. The text also mentions that some scholars (al-Bahr) quote the imam saying the difference between fard and wajib is like heaven and earth. The passage ends abruptly in the middle of discussing repetition in cases of forgetfulness.

Key Terms
واجب (wājib): An act that is obligatory by evidence that is not fully certain (contains shubha). Its omission intentionally deserves punishment but not takfīr, and forgetful omission requires sajdat al-sahw.
فرض (fard): An act obligatory by qat‘ī (certain) evidence; denial constitutes disbelief.
سنة (sunnah): Recommended act; established by evidence that is zannī thubut and dalālah; omission is not sinful but may be makrūh tanzīhan.
أدب (adab): Etiquette or recommended behavior that completes the sunnah; not obligatory.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetful omission of a wajib or other deficiencies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the technical definition of 'wajib'?
A) An act obligatory by evidence that is certain (qat‘ī)
B) An act obligatory by evidence that contains some doubt (shubha)
C) An act that is recommended (sunnah)
D) An act that is prohibited (haram)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, wajib is a distinct category of obligation based on zannī evidence, with consequences different from fard, and the hierarchy of fard → wajib → sunnah → adab forms a protective structure for prayer.
