The First Two Wājib Acts: Reciting al-Fatiha and Adding a Surah
Listing and proving the first two wājib acts of prayer with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (wājib) for reciting al-Fatiha and adding a surah in prayer, explain the evidence from hadith and why it indicates wājib not fard, and identify the ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatiha and a surah are wājib in prayer because ahad hadith with negation of perfection indicate obligation, not compulsion.

In this lesson, we examine the first two wājib acts of prayer from the Hanafi school: reciting Surah al-Fatiha and adding another surah or three short verses. The passage provides the evidence from two hadith and explains why these acts are considered wājib rather than fard. We will break down the proof and understand the interpretive principle that governs the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the act is (reciting al-Fatiha and adding a surah) and what ruling the text assigns to it (wājib). Note that the text explicitly says these are the first two wājib acts.
The matn lists them as wājib; the commentary clarifies the evidence.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence cited: 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha' and 'No prayer for one who does not recite Alhamdulillah and a surah.' Identify that these are ahad hadith.
The hadith are from Abu Hurairah and others, reported in the major collections.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith prove wājib status. The key is the negation ('no prayer'), which in Hanafi usul is interpreted as negation of perfection due to the probability in meaning (it could be negation of permissibility or virtue). Thus it indicates wājib, not fard.
The hadith is zanni al-dalala, so it cannot impose fard (which requires qat'i dalala).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the cross-madhhab difference: the Shafi'i school considers reciting al-Fatiha to be fard (rukn). Also note intra-Hanafi difference on adding a surah: some earlier views considered it sunnah, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is wājib.
The commentator mentions that the hadith 'la salata...' is used by the Shafi'is to argue fard, but the Hanafi response is that it negates perfection.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school takes the position of wājib: because the hadith is ahad and its negation is interpreted as negation of perfection. Also, the hadith does not abrogate the Quranic verse that allows reciting 'what is easy,' so it cannot be fard.
The tarjih is based on usul principles regarding the weight of ahad hadith and the interpretation of negation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وهو) أي الواجب على ما ذكر هنا وإلا فهي تزيد على ما ذكره والتتبع بنفي الحصر. قوله : (الأول وجوب قراءة الفاتحة) الصواب حذف وجوب قوله : (قراءة الفاتحة قالوا بترك أكثرها يسجد للسهو لا أن ترك أقلها، ولم أر ما إذا ترك النصف نهر لكن في المجتبى يسجد بترك آية منها، وهو أولى . وعليه فكل آية ،واجب ولو قرأ الفاتحة على قصد الدعاء تنوب عن القراءة كما في الفتاوى الصغرى خلافاً لما في المحيط قاله السيد قوله : (لنفي الكمال) فغاية ما يفيده الوجوب لا الافتراض لأنه وإن كان قطعي الثبوت فهو ظني الدلالة لأن مثله يقال لنفي الجواز ولنفي الفضيلة فكان محتملاً قوله: (لا ينسخ قوله تعالى (الخ) أي ولو قيد به لكان ناسخاً لذلك المطلق لأن تقييده ،نسخ، وهو لا يجوز بخبر الواحد قوله : (فوجب العمل به) أي بهذا الحديث، وهو تفريع على ثبوت الوجوب به وعدم نسخه مطلق الكتاب. قوله : (أو ثلاث آيات قصار) قدر أقصر سورة أو آية طويلة تعدل ثلاث آيات ،قصار وهذا الضم سنة عند الثلاثة كما في سكب الأنهر، وهل يكره الضم في الأخيرتين المختار لا كما في الدر، ووجوب هذا وما قبله مقيد بما إذا كان في الوقت سعة فإن خاف فوت الوقت لو قرأ الفاتحة، والسورة أو قرأ الفاتحة أو أزيد من آية قرأ في كل ركعة آية في جميع الصلاة نهر عن القنية، وتقسيم القراءة إلى فرض، وواجب وسنة بالنسبة لما قبل الإيقاع أما بعده لو قرأ القرآن كله في ركعة واحدة لم تقع القراءة إلا فرضاً اهـ من السيد بزيادة قوله : (لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد لله وسورة) الدليل أخص من المدعي، وقد يقال أن الثلاث آيات ألحقت بالسورة بدلالة النص، قال بعض الأفاضل وهذا يرد على من قال بفرضية الفاتحة فإنه يلزمه ان يقول أيضاً بفرضية السورة كما لا يخفى اهـ. قوله : (غير الثنائي) يعم الرباعي والثلاثي قوله: (لمشابهة السنة) بل هو عندهما . قوله: (لما (روينا من قوله : ولا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد الله وسورة في فريضة أو غيرها، وإنما لم تجب القراءة في الآخريين من الفرض كالنفل لقول علي رضي الله تعالى عنه : القراءة في الأوليين قراءة في الأخريين وعن ابن مسعود وعائشة رضي تعالى عنهما التخيير سنة
His saying: (and it) i.e., the obligatory duty, as mentioned here, otherwise it exceeds what he mentioned, and verification negates limitation. His saying: (the first is the obligation of reciting al-Fatiha) the correct [expression] is to drop 'obligation' [as part of the text]. His saying: (reciting al-Fatiha, they said: for abandoning most of it one prostrates for forgetfulness, not for abandoning a little of it, and I have not seen if one abandons half; in al-Nahr [it says] but in al-Mujtaba one prostrates for abandoning a verse of it, and that is more appropriate. Accordingly, every verse is wājib. And if one recites al-Fatiha with the intention of supplication, it substitutes for recitation as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra, contrary to what is in al-Muhit, as stated by al-Sayyid. His saying: (to negate perfection) so the utmost it indicates is obligation, not compulsory, because even though it is definite in transmission, it is probable in indication, because the like of it is used to negate permissibility and to negate virtue, so it is possible. His saying: (it does not abrogate the saying of Allah, etc.) i.e., even if it were restricted by it, it would be an abrogator of that absolute, because restricting it is abrogation, and that is not permissible by a solitary hadith. His saying: (so acting upon it is obligatory) i.e., by this hadith, and it is a branch on the establishment of obligation by it and the absence of its abrogation of the absolute book. His saying: (or three short verses) meaning the shortest surah or a long verse equivalent to three short verses. This addition is sunnah according to the three [imams] as in Saki al-Anhar. Is it disliked to add in the last two rak'ahs? The chosen view is no, as in al-Durr. The obligation of this and what precedes is restricted to when there is time to spare; if one fears the time will pass if he recites al-Fatiha and the surah, or he recites al-Fatiha or more than a verse, he recites in each rak'ah a verse in the entire prayer, as in al-Nahr from al-Qunyah. The division of recitation into compulsory, obligatory, and sunnah is with respect to before the actual performance; after it, if one recites the entire Quran in one rak'ah, the recitation is only compulsory. This is from al-Sayyid with additions. His saying: (no prayer for one who does not recite 'al-hamdu lillahi wa suratin') the evidence is more specific than the claim, and it may be said that the three verses are annexed to the surah by textual indication. Some scholars said: This refutes those who say al-Fatiha is compulsory, for it would require them to also say the surah is compulsory, as is not hidden. His saying: (other than the two-rak'ah) it includes four-rak'ah and three-rak'ah. His saying: (because of resemblance to the sunnah) rather it is with them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. His saying: (because of what we narrated from his saying: no prayer for one who does not recite 'al-hamdu lillahi wa suratin' in a compulsory prayer or otherwise. And recitation was not made obligatory in the last two rak'ahs of the compulsory prayer like the supererogatory, because of the saying of Ali: recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two, and from Ibn Mas'ud and Aisha the choice is sunnah.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the first two wājib acts of prayer: reciting Surah al-Fatiha (wājib 1) and adding a surah or three short verses (wājib 2). The author explains that the matn lists these as wājib, and the commentator discusses the evidence and details. For al-Fatiha, the proof is the hadith 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha' (reported by Abu Hurairah). The commentator clarifies that this hadith negates perfection, not validity, because it is a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) with probable indication, so it establishes wājib, not fard. The hadith cannot abrogate the Quranic command to recite 'what is easy' (al-Muzzammil:20). As for adding a surah or three short verses, the evidence is another hadith: 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-hamdu lillahi wa suratin' (Alhamdulillah and a surah). This is also wājib, not fard, and the surah is required in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers (except for two-rak'ah fard prayers like Fajr and Maghrib? Actually the text says it applies to non-two-rak'ah fard, meaning Zuhr, Asr, Isha – the first two rak'ahs only; for two-rak'ah fard (Fajr) it applies to both rak'ahs; and for Witr and Nafl, the addition is wājib in all rak'ahs. The commentator discusses the details: if one fears the time will expire, he may recite only a verse per rak'ah. The division of recitation into fard (the recitation itself), wājib (al-Fatiha and surah), and sunnah (other recitations) is relative to before the action; if one recites the whole Quran in one rak'ah, it still counts as fard. The passage also addresses the objection that the evidence is more specific than the claim, and argues that three verses are annexed to a surah by textual indication, refuting those who consider al-Fatiha to be fard.

Key Terms
قراءة الفاتحة (qirā'at al-fātiḥah): Reciting Surah al-Fatiha in prayer; classified as wājib in this text.
ضم سورة (ḍamm sūrah): Adding a surah or three short verses after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs; classified as wājib.
نفي الكمال (nafy al-kamāl): Negation of perfection; used to interpret the hadith as negating perfect prayer, not validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Why does the Hanafi school consider reciting al-Fatiha wājib rather than fard?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because the hadith is ahad and its wording negates perfection, not validity
C) Because it is a sunnah that became obligatory by consensus
D) Because it is a pillar of prayer according to all schools

Key Takeaway
Reciting al-Fatiha and adding a surah are wājib acts of prayer, proven by ahad hadith that indicate obligation through negation of perfection, and their omission requires sajdah al-sahw.

First Seven Wajibat of Salah with Proofs
Critical refinement of the first seven wajibat of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first seven wajibat of salah according to the Hanafi school, identify their proofs, and explain why they are classified as wajib rather than fard or sunnah.

Core Idea
The seven wajibat of salah are proven by ahad hadiths and the Prophet's constancy, making them obligatory but not fard.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi critically refines the list of wajibat in salah as presented in Maraqi al-Falah. It details the first seven obligatory elements, each supported by specific proofs (dalil) and intra-madhhab discussions. Understanding these wajibat is crucial for correctly performing salah and knowing when sajdah al-sahw is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each of the first seven wajibat, name the specific action (e.g., reciting al-Fatiha, adding a surah) and state that the ruling is wajib.
Wajib means omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
For each wajib, find the proof cited in the text. This may be a hadith (e.g., 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Opening of the Book') or the Prophet's constant practice (muwazaba).
The proofs are all khabar wahid (solitary reports), which are zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proof indicates obligation. The negation of prayer is interpreted as negation of perfection (nafy al-kamal) rather than validity, due to the general Quranic command (al-Muzzammil 20).
This is why the ruling is wajib, not fard: the proof cannot abrogate the qat'i Quranic text.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify any intra-madhhab disagreements. For example, on adding a surah, Abu Hanifa says wajib while the three (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar) say sunnah. On tranquility, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say wajib, al-Jurjani says sunnah, Abu Yusuf says fard.
These differences affect whether sajdah al-sahw is required.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine which view is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The text indicates that the correct view is that adding a surah is wajib (Abu Hanifa) and tranquility is wajib (the majority).
Al-Tahtawi relies on al-Durr al-Mukhtar and other later authorities for tarjih.

Source Text

يسجد ولم يعد (وهو) أي الواجب (ثمانية عشر شيئاً) الأول وجوب (قراءة الفاتحة) لقوله : «لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب» وهو لنفي الكمال لأنه خبر آحاد لا ينسخ قوله تعالى: (فاقرؤا ما تيسر) فوجب العمل به (و) الثاني (ضم سورة قصيرة أو ثلاث آيات) فصار لقوله : «لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد لله وسورة في فريضة أو غيرها» (في ركعتين غير متعينتين من الفرض غير الثنائي، وفي جميع الثنائي (و) يجب الضم (في جميع ركعات على قراءة السورة) للمواظبة حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة، ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو كما لو كرر الفاتحة، ثم قرأ السورة (و) يجب (ضم (الأنف أي ما صلب منه (للجبهة في السجود) للمواظبة في غير الأوليين وصحح. قوله : (حتى لو قرأ من السورة) أي بعض السورة ولو حرفاً واحداً كما في السيد وغيره والمراد من السورة ما . الآيات ومثل بعض السورة كلها كما سيأتي قريباً قوله: (ويسجد للسهو) إذا كان ساهياً وإلا كره تحريماً لأن فيه تأخير الواجب، وهو العلة في وجوب السهو بتكرار الفاتحة قوله : وهو (أي ما صلب منه فلو اقتصر على الأرنبة لا يكون آتياً بالواجب قوله : (ولا تجوز الصلاة بالاقتصار على الأنف في (السجود ما لم يكن بالجبهة عذر قاله السيد قوله : (ولو بعد القعود) ولو بعد السلام قبل الكلام قوله : (ثم يعيد القعود طريق الإتيان بها أنه إذا تذكرها بعد السلام، أو قبله بعد القعود أن يسجد المتروكة ثم الأخيرة، وهي فرض بخلاف سجود السهو فإنه يرفع التشهد فقط حتى لو سلم بمجرد رفعه منه، ولم يقعد صحت صلاته ولكنه يكره لتركه التشهد وهو واجب كما في الدر وغيره. قوله: (وهو التعديل) أي التتميم والتكميل وهو في اللغة التسوية قوله: (حتى تطمئن مفاصله) ويستقر كل عضو في محله بقدر تسبيحة كما في القهستاني هذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد على تخريج الكرخي، وعلى تخريج الجرجاني سنة كتعديل القومية، والجلسة والأول هو الصحيح وإنما خص الركوع والسجود لأنهما مظنة التخفيف بخلاف القيام لأنه يطول بطول القراءة حتى لو لم يقرأ في الأخريين وبقي ساكتاً كان عليه أن يقف بقدر تسبيحة لأجل تعديل الركن كما صرح به في النهاية ولو لم يقف هذا القدر إثم ولا تفسد صلاته لوجود أصل القيام فإن المفروض من الركن أدنى ما يطلق عليه الإسم . قوله : (ولا) فرض كما قاله أبو يوسف)
He prostrates and does not repeat. And it (i.e., the wajib) is eighteen things. The first: obligation of reciting al-Fatiha, due to his saying: 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Opening of the Book.' This is for negation of perfection because it is a khabar wahid that cannot abrogate the verse 'So recite what is easy thereof.' So action upon it is obligatory. The second: adding a short surah or three verses, due to his saying: 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd (al-Fatiha) and a surah in an obligatory or other prayer.' This is in two non-specific rak'ahs of non-two-rak'ah obligatory prayers, and in all two-rak'ah prayers. And adding is obligatory in all rak'ahs of witr due to its similarity to sunnah, and in all rak'ahs of nafl due to what we narrated: for every pair of nafl is a prayer by itself. And it is obligatory to specify the obligatory recitation in the first two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer due to the Prophet's constancy in recitation therein. And it is obligatory to give precedence of al-Fatiha over recitation of the surah due to constancy, such that if one began reciting from the surah and then remembered, he recites al-Fatiha, then recites the surah and prostrates for forgetfulness, just as if he repeated al-Fatiha and then recited the surah. And it is obligatory to include the nose (i.e., its hard part) with the forehead in prostration due to constancy upon it, and prayer is not valid by confining to the nose in prostration according to the correct view. And it is obligatory to observe order between the two prostrations, which is performing the second prostration in every rak'ah (obligatory or otherwise) before moving to something other than prostration from the remaining actions of prayer, due to constancy. If it is missed, he prostrates it even after the final sitting, then repeats the sitting. And it is obligatory to have tranquility (i.e., settling) in the pillars, by calming the limbs in bowing and prostration until his joints are at rest, in the correct view, to complete the pillar; it is not sunnah as al-Jurjani said, nor fard as Abu Yusuf said. And the evidence requires seven (verses?) of al-Fatiha, its place is general, because in the last two rak'ahs, if he wishes he recites and if he wishes he does not, from the commentary. And his saying: (and specifying the recitation etc.) was said to be fard, and would be qada if found in other than the first two, and it was corrected. His saying: (even if he recited from the surah) means part of the surah, even one letter, as in al-Sayyid and others, and what is meant by surah is verses, and partial recitation is like the whole as will come soon. His saying: (and prostrates for forgetfulness) if he was forgetful, otherwise it is makruh tahriman because it delays the wajib, and that is the cause for wajib of forgetfulness in repeating al-Fatiha. His saying: and it (i.e., the hard part) so if he confined to the tip, he is not fulfilling the wajib. His saying: (and prayer is not valid by confining to the nose in prostration unless there is an excuse with the forehead, said by al-Sayyid. His saying: (even after the final sitting) and even after salam before speaking. His saying: (then repeats the sitting) the way to perform it is that when he remembers it after salam, or before it after the final sitting, he prostrates the missed one, then repeats the final sitting and tashahhud, and gives salam, then prostrates for forgetfulness, then sits and recites tashahhud, because returning to the spinal prostration nullifies the final sitting and tashahhud, and likewise for the recitation prostration. So if he does not repeat the sitting and merely gives salam upon rising from prostration, his prayer is invalid due to missing the final sitting, which is fard, unlike forgetting prostration which nullifies only tashahhud, such that if he gives salam upon rising from it and does not sit, his prayer is valid but it is makruh due to missing tashahhud, which is wajib, as in al-Durr and others. His saying: (and it is the adjustment) meaning completion and perfection, and it is in language equality. His saying: (until his joints are at rest) and each limb settles in its place for the duration of one tasbih as in al-Qahistani. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad according to al-Karkhi's derivation, and according to al-Jurjani's derivation it is sunnah, like the adjusting of standing and sitting. The first is the correct one. He specifically mentioned bowing and prostration because they are likely to be hastened, unlike standing which lengthens due to recitation. Even if he does not recite in the last two rak'ahs and remains silent, he must pause for the duration of one tasbih for the sake of adjusting the pillar, as stated in al-Nihaya. If he does not pause this amount, he sins but his prayer is not invalidated because the essence of standing exists, for the fard of the pillar is the minimum that the name applies to. His saying: (and not) fard as Abu Yusuf said.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, commenting on the earlier text of Maraqi al-Falah, which lists the wajibat (obligatory elements) of salah. The author states that the wajibat are eighteen in number, and then proceeds to explain the first seven in detail. 

The first wajib is recitation of Surah al-Fatiha. The proof is the hadith 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Opening of the Book.' The author emphasizes that this hadith is khabar wahid (solitary report), so it cannot abrogate the general Quranic command 'recite what is easy' (al-Muzzammil 20). Therefore, the obligation is only wajib, not fard, because the hadith is zanni al-dalala (probable in meaning) and cannot overrule the qat'i command. 

The second wajib is adding a short surah or three short verses after al-Fatiha. This is proven by another hadith: 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd (Fatiha) and a surah.' This applies in two rak'ahs of non-two-rak'ah obligatory prayers (e.g., the first two of Maghrib, Isha, Zuhr, Asr), in all rak'ahs of two-rak'ah obligatory prayers (Fajr), and in all rak'ahs of witr and nafl. The text notes that some scholars (the three: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar?) consider this addition as sunnah, not wajib.

The third wajib is specifying the obligatory recitation (i.e., al-Fatiha + surah) in the first two rak'ahs of obligatory prayers. This is established by the Prophet's constant practice.

The fourth wajib is giving precedence to al-Fatiha over the surah. If one inadvertently starts with the surah, he must recite al-Fatiha then repeat the surah and perform sajdah al-sahw. This is due to violating the prescribed order.

The fifth wajib is placing the nose (its hard part) together with the forehead in sujud. The correct view is that prayer is invalid if one prostrates only on the nose without a valid excuse (e.g., a forehead wound).

The sixth wajib is maintaining the proper sequence between the two prostrations: the second sajdah must be performed before moving to any other action of prayer. If omitted, it must be made up even after the final sitting, and then the sitting must be repeated.

The seventh wajib is tranquility (itminan) in the pillars, specifically in ruku' and sujud, meaning each limb must settle for at least one tasbih. This is wajib to complete the pillar; it is not sunnah (as al-Jurjani held) nor fard (as Abu Yusuf held). The correct view in the madhhab is that it is wajib.

The commentary also includes discussions on the implications of missing these wajibs, such as the need for sajdah al-sahw, the invalidity of prayer for missing a fard (like final sitting), and the correct procedure for making up missed prostrations.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): A legal obligation that is established by a zanni (probable) proof; omission necessitates compensation (sajdah al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
الاطمئنان (al-itminan): Tranquility or settling of all limbs in ruku' and sujud for at least the duration of one tasbih (subhanallah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the first seven wajibat of salah as listed in this passage?
A) Recitation of al-Fatiha
B) Adding a short surah or three verses
C) Raising the hands for takbir
D) Tranquility in ruku' and sujud

Key Takeaway
The first seven wajibat of salah are proven by ahad hadiths and muwazaba; they are wajib, not fard, and omission requires sajdah al-sahw.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Wujub of Specifying Recitation in First Two Rak'ahs
Ruling with proof for wajib recitation in first two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying recitation in the first two rak'ahs, explain the proof from prophetic constancy, and distinguish between the views that it is fard versus wajib.

Core Idea
Specifying wajib recitation to the first two rak'ahs is wajib, not fard, because the proof is zanni.

This passage addresses a key detail in the fiqh of salah: in which rak'ahs is the recitation (Fatihah + surah) obligatory? The Hanafi school specifies it to the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer. The ruling is based on the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah). However, there is a difference of opinion within the school: some consider it fard, but the correct view is that it is wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is specifying the wajib recitation (al-qira'ah al-wajibah) to the first two rak'ahs of the fard prayer. The ruling is 'wajib'.
The term 'wajib' is used, not 'fard'.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The Prophet's constancy (muwazabah) in reciting in these two rak'ahs. This is a Sunnah ahad proof.
Muwazabah indicates a consistent practice, which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The Prophet's continuous practice without leaving it shows that it is an obligation (wujub) in the Hanafi view.
The proof is zanni al-thubut, so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any view differ? Yes, some (within the Hanafi school) say it is fard. The text states 'qila innahu fard' (it is said that it is fard).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The text says 'suhhiha' (it is corrected), indicating the correct view is that it is wajib. This is the mufta bihi position.
The tarjih is based on the weakness of the fard claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب تعيين القراءة الواجبة في الأوليين من الفرض لمواظبة النبي على القراءة فيهما وقيل إنه فرض وتكون قضاء إذا وجدت في غير الأوليين وصحح
And it is obligatory to specify the wajib recitation in the first two [rak'ahs] of the fard due to the Prophet's constancy in reciting in them. And it is said that it is fard, and it becomes qada if found in other than the first two, and it is corrected.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This is a ruling on the obligatory nature of specifying the wajib recitation (al-qira'ah al-wajibah) in the first two rak'ahs of the fard prayer. The proof is the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) of reciting in these two rak'ahs. In Hanafi fiqh, this specification is wajib, not fard, according to the correct view, though some have held it to be fard. If the recitation is delayed and performed in the later rak'ahs, it is considered qada (make-up), and the prayer is still valid but requires sajdah al-sahw if the omission was deliberate? The text says 'and it is corrected (suhhiha)' referring to the preferred view.

Key Terms
تعيين القراءة الواجبة (ta'yin al-qira'ah al-wajibah): Specifying the obligatory recitation (Fatihah and surah) to the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on specifying the wajib recitation to the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer?
A) It is fard.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah.
D) It is mustahabb.

Key Takeaway
Specifying the wajib recitation to the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, and delaying it requires sajdah al-sahw.
